# Design decisions

Log of design changes to [ARCHITECTURE.md](ARCHITECTURE.md) that implementation forced. ARCHITECTURE always reads as the current intended end-state; this file is *why* it changed. Newest first.

`/cs-implement` appends an entry when building a unit reveals a genuine design change — a forced realization (the design as written is wrong, impossible, or clearly worse than what the code must do), never a mere preference. The human appends when they revise scope. Format: **date · unit/PR · what changed · why**.

The entries below (2026-07-02) are a backfill: design changes made during the v0.1→v0.2 build that predate this log, recovered from the sessions and commit history.


## 2026-07-18 · Schema Unit 10 — codegen identifier-collision disambiguation (Python + Go) · distinct slot names that sanitize to one identifier must not emit duplicate accessors
**Changed:** closes the identifier-collision follow-on both #306 and #307 carried. Identifier sanitization is many-to-one — `a-b`, `a_b`, `a b` all sanitize to `a_b` (Python) / `A_b` (Go), and Go additionally folds first-letter case (`fooBar` and `FooBar` both export as `FooBar`) — so two distinct slot names in one map type could derive the same accessor name, emitting duplicate methods that fail to compile (or silently shadow).
- **Disambiguation policy (identical in both emitters).** Within one wrapper's accessor namespace the first slot to claim a name keeps its sanitized base verbatim; each later collision appends the smallest free `_N` (`_2`, `_3`, …). A shared `disambiguate(base, prefixes, used)` helper drives both `generate_python` and `generate_go`.
- **Dedup at the fully-emitted method name, not the base.** A slot emits several accessors sharing a base (`get_`/`set_`/… + base), while a map slot's accessor is the *bare* base — so a map slot named `get_title` collides with a register slot `title`'s `get_title` even though their bases differ (Go: a hard `method already declared` compile error; Python: silent shadowing). The helper is therefore fed the slot kind's verb set (`prefixes`) and reserves every `prefix+base` name, so bare-vs-prefixed collisions across distinct bases are caught too.
- **Deterministic + stable.** Declaration order (the schema's own, preserved through the parser) drives the suffix, so a regenerate is byte-identical, and a new colliding slot appended to a type takes the next suffix without renaming the slots declared before it.
- **Name-only change.** The path key each accessor forwards to is the original slot name, untouched — disambiguation changes only the method name, never which field it reads or writes. A disambiguated accessor round-trips to its own distinct field.
- **Specs.** New colliding-schema fixture (`crates/codegen/tests/fixtures/collide.schema.json`) pinned two ways per language: a Rust golden + unique-and-forwarding assertions (`crates/codegen/tests/{python,go}.rs`, incl. a Go-only case-fold case, the bare-map-vs-prefixed cross-kind case, and a retry-past-a-claimed-suffix case) and a live round-trip in the target SDK (`sdks/python/tests/test_codegen.py`; `sdks/go/collidegen/`) proving the three colliding counters stay independent. RED before the fix (duplicate methods), green after. No core `Schema` or wire change.
- **Out of scope (separate axis).** Type-*name* collisions — two map *types* whose names sanitize to the same class/struct — are a distinct pre-existing question this change neither introduces nor closes; the slot-accessor namespace is per-wrapper, type names are schema-global and referenced by nested accessors, so they need their own schema-wide mapping. Deferred.

## 2026-07-18 · Schema Unit 10 — typed-SDK codegen extends to Go; TS-for-wasm a justified skip · a second language target proves the per-language emitter shape; the wasm surface has no path façade to forward to
**Changed:** extends #306's per-language codegen to a **second target, Go** (`generate_go`), completing the multi-target structure the framework was factored for — no core or wire change (codegen still only *reads* the `Schema`).
- **Go mirrors Python's shape.** One exported struct per declared map type (holding a `*crdtsync.Document` + its path prefix); each slot a typed method forwarding to the Go SDK's path surface with its key + type baked in — register → `GetX()`/`SetX`, counter → `GetX`/`IncX`/`DecX`, text → `GetX`/`LenX`/`InsertX`/`DeleteX`, list → `LenX`/`GetX`/`InsertX`/`DeleteX`, nested map → `X() *Nested` rooted at the extended path. Getters forward the SDK's own `(value, ok)` return as-is (no `Optional`-style reshaping — Go has no such idiom); the byte key is a `[]byte("…")` literal (`\xNN` for non-printables). Names are sanitized to exported PascalCase identifiers (leading non-letter gains an `X` prefix). `--package` on the CLI names the emitted package (default: sanitized schema name).
- **One real hazard the Go target has that Python doesn't: path-slice aliasing.** Python's `self._path + [key]` allocates a fresh list every call; Go's `append(prefix, key)` can mutate a shared backing array, so sibling and nested accessors would corrupt each other's paths. The emitter therefore generates a `joinPath(prefix, key)` helper that *copies*, and every accessor routes through it. (Pinned indirectly by the nested-map + sibling round-trip tests.)
- **Determinism + spec parity.** Same two-way pinning as Python: a Rust golden test (`crates/codegen/tests/go.rs`) asserts `generate_go(sample, "notegen") == committed golden`, and that golden lives *in the Go module* (`sdks/go/notegen/note_generated.go`) so `go test` compiles and round-trips it against a real `Document` — set via a generated setter → read via the generated getter *and* the equivalent raw path. The Go golden is gofmt-clean, so the emitter's own formatting is the checked-in formatting.
- **TS-for-wasm — assessed, justified skip (follow-on).** Evaluated per the unit's mandate and declined, for two independent reasons that are exactly the task's named skip conditions: (1) **the wasm surface is already statically typed** by wasm-bindgen's generated `.d.ts`, so a typed wrapper's only value-add is schema-shaped naming sugar (`note.getTitle()`) — far narrower than Python/Go, where the raw surface is stringly-typed; (2) **there is no path façade to forward to** — every `WasmDocument` method takes a single *pre-encoded opaque* path buffer (`encodePath(keys) -> Uint8Array`), not the append-a-key list model Python and Go share, so a TS target would need a distinct encode-then-call emit shape rather than reusing the framework's forward-a-path-list shape. Compounding both: the repo has **no in-tree TS/JS build or test harness** (the wasm CI job runs `wasm-pack test --node` on the Rust crate; there is no tsc/npm package), so satisfying the spec-first compile+round-trip gate would mean standing up a whole toolchain for low payoff. Revisit if/when a first-class npm/TypeScript SDK package lands with its own build. Go shipped regardless.

## 2026-07-17 · Schema Unit 10 — typed-SDK codegen (Python first) · a build-time generator reads a registered Schema and emits typed accessor wrappers that forward to the raw path surface; core Schema + wire format untouched
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Schema's long-standing "type-aware SDK API" / "a typed client bundles (its accessors are generated code)" as a concrete, tested vertical slice. A new in-repo tool `crdtsync-codegen` (a workspace bin, dep-liberal) reads a schema JSON, validates it through the **core `Schema` parser** (the sole validator — codegen never re-parses or re-implements schema semantics), and emits a source file of typed accessors for a target SDK. **Python is the first target**; the emitter is factored per-language (`generate_python`) so Go / TypeScript follow the same shape (KANBAN follow-ons).
- **The generated code is a thin facade over the existing path surface, not a new API tier.** For each declared map type the generator emits one wrapper class (named after the type) holding a `Document` + the path prefix it lives at; each slot becomes a typed accessor that forwards to the SDK's existing path method with the slot's path key + type baked in — `note.get_title()` → `doc.text_get([b"title"])`. Register → int get/set, counter → get/inc/dec, text → get/len/insert/delete, list → len/get/insert/delete, nested map → an accessor returning the nested wrapper rooted at the extended path. This keeps codegen a pure convenience layer: it adds no runtime behavior core doesn't already have, so there is nothing new to keep convergent across languages.
- **Deterministic output.** Types + slots are emitted in the schema's own declaration order and the header carries no timestamp, so regenerating an unchanged schema is a no-op diff (the property a checked-in generated artifact needs). Pinned two ways: a Rust golden test asserts `generate_python(sample) == committed golden`, and the same golden is imported by a Python round-trip test that drives a real `Document` (set via a generated setter → read back via the generated getter *and* the equivalent raw path).
- **Scope of the first slice.** register / counter / text / list / nested-map slots. Xml slots (and any slot whose type is undeclared) are emitted as a skipped-with-comment line — the xml typed surface is a follow-on. A `register` is treated as an integer scalar (its declared bounds are numeric); a bytes-valued register uses the raw path. A slot name that is not a valid Python identifier is sanitized for the method suffix while the path key keeps the exact bytes.
- **No core / wire change.** Codegen only *reads* the `Schema`; the `Schema` type and the wire format are untouched (§Schema Is Code). The generator consumes the schema JSON an app already authors.
- **Specs.** `crates/codegen/tests/python.rs` (determinism, golden match, header carries name/version but no timestamp, per-slot forwarding, identifier sanitization) + `sdks/python/tests/test_codegen.py` (import + text/counter/list/nested-map round-trips against a live `Document`). Local review (medium). `crates/codegen` is dep-liberal (core stays dep-minimal).

## 2026-07-17 · mTLS client-cert credential carrier · a verified client cert authenticates AS the ACL actor (SAN→CN), config-gated on a client-CA, fail-closed at the handshake
**Changed:** the TLS #300 seam is realized — mutual TLS (client-cert authentication) as a **credential carrier for the ACL authenticated-actor identity**, not a parallel identity concept. Configuring `CRDTSYNC_TLS_CLIENT_CA` (a PEM trust-anchor bundle) swaps the #300 `with_no_client_auth()` slot for a `rustls::server::WebPkiClientVerifier` built against those roots (`server_config_from_pem_with_client_ca`); without it, TLS stays server-auth-only exactly as #300 (no regression). Server-only, no core change.
- **Cert identity → the same authenticated-actor plumbing.** A verified connection's leaf cert is parsed (`x509-parser`) for its **SAN** (first DNS/email/URI general name), **falling back to CN**; that name is bound as the connection's actor via the *existing* `connect_authenticated(Identity::new(actor))` path — the one the fast-path credential and anonymous mode already use. A `cert_actor: Option<Vec<u8>>` rides `Cmd::Connect` from the accept loop (which reads `peer_certificates()` off the accepted `TlsStream`) to the registry actor; the connection is told its actor via the unsolicited `AuthOk`, and the ACL evaluator sees the cert actor at every read/write/awareness point. No new identity concept — a cert-authed connection is just another way to establish the ACL actor (§ACL identity=authenticated-actor). It takes **precedence** over any in-band credential presented on the same connection (the transport-established identity is cryptographic).
- **Fail-closed at three points.** (1) mTLS *requires* (not merely requests) a client cert — `WebPkiClientVerifier::builder(...).build()`, no `allow_unauthenticated` — so a client with no cert or an untrusted/invalid cert is rejected **by rustls at the handshake**, never reaching the session layer. (2) A verified-but-identity-less cert (parses, but no usable SAN and no CN) is a **rejection** (`actor_from_client_cert → None → peer_cert_actor → Err → connection dropped`), never admitted anonymously or as a default actor. (3) An empty/garbage client-CA bundle is a loud `TlsConfigError::NoClientCa`, never a silent fall back to server-auth-only; a client CA set without a server cert/key is a clean startup error (mTLS needs TLS).
- **Deviation from the entering design:** none. The design (resolved with the human 2026-07-16) mapped cleanly onto rustls + the existing actor plumbing — `peer_certificates()` exposes the leaf after handshake, and `connect_authenticated` accepts an externally-established actor as-is, so no ARCHITECTURE amendment beyond documenting the mTLS end-state in §Transport.
- **Specs.** `crates/server/tests/tls.rs` (+9, rcgen test CA + CA-signed client certs): a SAN cert binds its SAN as the session actor (in preference to CN); a CN-only cert falls back to CN; an ACL read decision is keyed on the cert actor (recording authorizer sees `(Read, "alice")`); a no-cert client is rejected when mTLS is required; an untrusted-CA cert is rejected; a server with no client-CA still accepts a certless client (#300 regression); plus mTLS `ServerConfig` construction (valid bundle / empty bundle → `NoClientCa` / missing file → `Io`). Excluded under Miri (real I/O). Local review HIGH (security-authentication boundary). `crates/server` is dep-liberal (`x509-parser` added); only the core stays dep-minimal.

## 2026-07-16 · TLS termination at the listener · terminate-at-server with rustls, config-gated, fail-closed — never a silent plaintext downgrade
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Transport's "WSS over TLS in production" — TLS is now **terminated at the server's own listener**, not delegated to an assumed external proxy. Library is **rustls** (pure-Rust, ring provider — the same one reqwest already pulls in, so no OpenSSL/system dep and the build stays hermetic); `tokio-rustls` wraps each accepted socket. `server_config_from_pem(cert, key)` loads a PEM cert-chain + private key into a `rustls::ServerConfig` at startup; `ServeConfig.tls: Option<Arc<ServerConfig>>` carries it into the accept loop. The wire protocol is transport-agnostic, so `handle` was made generic over the stream (`AsyncRead + AsyncWrite + Unpin + Send`) and the *same* session logic serves both a plaintext `TcpStream` and a TLS-wrapped stream — no forked session path. No core change (server-only).
- **Opt-in, plaintext-preserving.** With no cert configured the listener binds plaintext exactly as before (dev stays frictionless, zero new dependency at runtime). `main.rs` gates on `CRDTSYNC_TLS_CERT` + `CRDTSYNC_TLS_KEY`; both must be set together (`wss://`), and setting only one is a clean startup error, not a one-sided fall back.
- **Fail-closed is the security invariant.** A configured-but-broken cert/key — missing file, empty/garbage PEM, mismatched key — is a **loud startup error** (`TlsConfigError`, mapped to a startup `io::Error`), never a silent downgrade to plaintext. A silent downgrade would turn a deployment that asked for encryption into an unencrypted one — a security regression, so it is explicitly tested (`a_missing_cert_path_is_a_loud_error_not_a_plaintext_fallback` + the empty/no-key/mismatch arms) alongside the end-to-end encrypted round-trip and a plaintext-client-rejected test.
- **mTLS is the follow-on this unblocks.** The `ServerConfig` is built with `with_no_client_auth()` — exactly the slot a later mTLS unit swaps for a client-cert verifier, without touching cert/key loading. Not built here (see KANBAN follow-on).
- **Pre-auth DoS bound.** TLS adds an unauthenticated blocking point in the accept path, so the handshake is wrapped in a 10s timeout — a client that connects and then stalls (sends no ClientHello) cannot pin a spawned task + socket FD indefinitely. A failed/timed-out handshake drops only that connection; the accept loop is untouched.
- **Specs.** `crates/server/tests/tls.rs` (8): a self-signed rcgen cert/key drives a real TLS handshake + a wire-frame round-trip over the encrypted stream, a plaintext client gets no session on the TLS listener, and the `server_config_from_pem` construction + config gating (good pair / missing cert / missing key / empty cert / no key / mismatch) each fail loudly. Excluded under Miri (real I/O). Local review (medium) → added the handshake timeout. `crates/server` is dep-liberal; only the core stays dep-minimal.

## 2026-07-16 · Blob-ACL — reference-site blob-fetch authorization / #301 · a blob fetch is authorized iff the caller holds READ on a live reference to the id, through the same evaluator op redaction uses; fail-closed on unreferenced/unreadable
**Changed:** closes the **authenticated-but-not-authorized** gap the blob-fetch route carried (`admin.rs`: `GET /blobs/{id}` authenticated the credential but let any authenticated caller fetch any id it knew — a blob-id leak = content exfiltration). A blob is **content-addressed + immutable**, so authorization *cannot* attach to the content (the id IS the content hash, shared across every reference); it attaches to the **reference site**. Realizes the design already pinned in ARCHITECTURE §Binary Blobs / Authorization (the human design gate KANBAN flagged is thereby resolved, not a fresh ruling), now built end-to-end. No STATE_VERSION change (a derived index + a route gate, no encoded-state shape change); no wire-format change to the blob route's success path.
- **The reference-site index + the shared evaluator, no parallel lattice.** `index::blob_ref_paths(doc)` walks the live document exactly as `element_paths` does, mapping each live `Scalar::BlobRef` slot's id → the encoded `core::path` that references it (a map-slot ref at its **leaf** path `container+key`, the same governing path a keyed op reads at; a node-addressed list/XML-child ref at its container's **subtree** path, since read authority governs a whole subtree). `Registry::authorize_blob_fetch(identity, id)` resolves the caller's READ authority against those paths through the *same* `acl::recipient_reads_path` op redaction uses — deployment policy, doc-ACL tuples, and schema `@auth` grants composed identically. `Resource` = the referencing path(s); `Action` = read. A handle is room-independent, so every room is scanned and the first readable reference grants.
- **The blob plane owns no replicas → a handle round-trip.** *Forced wiring realization:* the out-of-band blob listener (`serve_blobs`) holds only a store + verifier, while the authoritative documents live behind the single-threaded registry **actor**. So a fetch's authorization round-trips to the actor over a new `runtime::RegistryHandle` (a `admin::BlobAccess` async-trait impl backed by a `Cmd::AuthorizeBlob` oneshot); `serve_with_authorizer_handle` hands the handle back alongside the accept-loop future so `main` wires it into the blob plane. `BlobAccess` is injectable, so the route's 403 wiring is testable with a stub (`PermitAllBlobs` is the dev default). If the actor is gone or drops the reply, the handle **denies** (fail-closed on an unreachable decider).
- **Fail-closed on every ambiguous case — the drag-to-exfil analogue for blobs.** An unreferenced or since-deleted id (a leaked/guessed handle nothing links), or one referenced only from a position the caller cannot read (a leaf `Deny(Read)`, a redacted subtree), is **denied** — even for an authenticated caller, and even for the room creator who owns `/` (an owner cannot fetch a blob nothing in the document references). Consistent with the element-id redaction model (#291/#294): a reference the recipient cannot see must not be fetchable. Consequence (documented, not a bug): a producer that just uploaded bytes cannot fetch them back until its `set_blob_ref` op commits to the room — until a reference exists there is no authority site, by design. **Upload stays authentication-only** (a producer stores bytes before any reference exists; the gate is on fetch). A genuinely-unknown id now answers `403` (fail-closed) rather than `404` under the real authority, so the response never distinguishes an unauthorized id from a missing one — an existence-nonleak bonus.
- **Residual (bounded, deferred to the v0.5 GC/ref-count slice).** A fetch resolves by walking each room's live tree (`blob_ref_paths`) inside the single-threaded registry actor — the same per-request full-tree walk class the fan-out already pays (`element_paths` per broadcast), authenticated-only, and short-circuited on the first readable reference. A flood of fetches for random ids therefore costs one tree-walk per room per request. The natural fix is a cached, write-invalidated `id → reference sites` index folded into blob dedup ref-counting (already deferred to v0.5) — deliberately **not** rushed into this security PR, since a stale cache would fail *open* (grant a fetch to a since-removed reference), the one direction this gate must never take. Until then the walk is the safe, if unoptimized, choice.
- **Specs.** `crates/server/tests/blob_acl.rs` (decision level, Miri-clean, in-process over the registry): a reader of a referencing path may fetch; a non-reader is denied even when authenticated; an unreferenced id is denied (fail-closed, creator included); a blob referenced only from a denied leaf position is denied while the creator still reaches it; a multiply-referenced blob is fetchable from any readable site; deleting the only reference makes it unfetchable. `crates/server/tests/blob_http.rs` extends the route status matrix (authenticated-but-unauthorized → `403`, authorized → bytes, auth precedes authz, malformed id precedes the gate). The AEAD cross-zone opaque-token path (no reference site on the recipient's server) stays the deferred Zones-4 case, out of scope. → *Binary Blobs / Authorization — a blob fetch is authorized at the reference site through the doc-ACL read evaluator, fail-closed.*
## 2026-07-16 · Schema 9c producer-reject / #302 · the enforcing server's op-ingress refuses only a *newly-introduced runtime-kind mismatch at a declared slot* — unrepairable AND inadmissible; an undeclared map slot is admissible (a Map is an open container), and every repairable violation still rides into the log for read-time normalization
**Changed:** pins the **§Schema Enforcement Points** end-state (ARCHITECTURE) for producer-side reject-before-send, the last Schema-Unit-9 slice. The resolved design entering the unit framed 9c as rejecting "the non-repairable violations" and named two — a runtime-kind mismatch **and** an undeclared map slot — plus a sequence-`min` underflow as the motivating example. Implementing against the actual validator surfaced a **forced deviation**: two of those three are not rejectable violations under the pinned schema model, so the reject set is narrower than the design named.
- **A sequence `min` cannot underflow at runtime — it is rejected at schema parse time.** The closure invariant (§Closure of Violation Set) already forbids a list/text `min` (an underflow has no repair — items cannot be invented), so the design's motivating example describes a state the schema model cannot express. There is nothing to reject at ingress for it.
- **An undeclared map slot is not a violation to reject — a Map is an open container.** The schema's finite dimensions (§Closure: type membership, children cardinality, attr presence/type/range, mark allowance/shape) do **not** include map-slot membership; a Map type's `children` **types** its known slots, it does not forbid others. The validator still *reports* an `UnknownSlot` (read-repair omits it, unchanged), but rejecting it at ingress would break the ubiquitous "open content model" pattern (a schema declaring `autoVersion`/ACL/zones over a `{ "kind": "map" }` root and writing arbitrary slots — 12 server test suites do exactly this) and contradict the open-container model. So an undeclared slot is **admitted**.
- **The one rejectable violation is a runtime-kind mismatch at a declared slot.** A declared slot materializing the wrong element kind (a counter where the type declares a register) is the sole violation that is both unrepairable (a counter cannot be read as a register — read-repair has no normalization, exactly as it has none for an undeclared slot) *and* inadmissible (it stands at a slot the schema declared, where the undeclared slot is admitted). §Enforcement Points ("producer rejects invalid ops; invalid ops never enter the log") and §Invariant Repair ("Map slot type mismatch handled by the algorithm, not repair") reconcile as: a batch that installs a wrong-kind value against clean committed state is refused at ingress (fail-fast, keep the log clean); a mismatch *already standing* in committed state (from a non-enforcing write) is exempt, and however it renders is the Map slot's LWW concern. `batch_introduces_schema_violation` simulates the batch on a decoded copy and refuses it only when a rejectable mismatch stands at a *location* the pre-apply baseline did not already have mismatched (before/after computed on the one decoded baseline). **Comparing locations rather than a bare count** is load-bearing, and was the HIGH local review's finding: a count nets to zero — and silently admits the fresh mismatch — when one batch both heals a standing mismatch (LWW-overwriting it with a correct-kind value) and plants a new one on a clean slot; the location diff catches the planted one. The location key resolves each sequence index to its **stable Fugue node stamp**, not its ordinal, so an unrelated insert/delete that only renumbers a standing mismatch is not misread as a fresh one (the opposite failure — a false reject — the same review's earlier pass flagged).
- **Mechanism.** `ViolationKind::rejects_at_ingress()` (core, true only for `KindMismatch`) is the classifier; `index::batch_introduces_schema_violation` (server) is the before/after delta over `validate`, mirroring the `batch_crosses_zone` simulate-on-a-decoded-copy model; `Hub::batch_violates_schema` dispatches it (an opening write to an as-yet-unknown room validates against a fresh empty document, so a first write cannot establish a mismatch); `session::step` calls it on the main-branch enforcing (`schema.is_some()`) Ops path — after the cross-zone gate, before ingest — and returns `OpsRejected` with a new `ErrorCode::SchemaViolation` (wire tag 8, distinct from the authz `Forbidden`; added to the core codec + ffi/wasm surfaces). A relay connection (`schema` `None`) never validates. No STATE_VERSION change (read-only over the merged document); no change to Unit 2 read-repair (`UnknownSlot`/`KindMismatch` still omitted from `repairs`). The optional **client-local advisory pre-check** (the same validator run SDK-side for fail-fast UX, never the trust boundary) is a thin follow-on, noted in KANBAN.
- **Specs.** `crates/server/tests/schema_reject.rs`: an enforcing server rejects a kind mismatch (`SchemaViolation`, op never logged, mover absent) and names the author's op seqs back; an undeclared slot is **admitted, not rejected** (the open-container regression guarding the 12 suites); a repairable over-`max` is accepted and repaired at read (regression — 9c never turns a repairable case into a rejection); a valid write is unaffected; a **relay** tier passes the same mistyped op through unvalidated; after a reject the accepting replicas **converge** on the valid op alone (the rejected op entered no log); the refusal survives a store replay reopen. `crates/core/tests/protocol.rs` round-trips the new `SchemaViolation` (and the previously-uncovered `NotFound`) on `Error` + `OpsRejected`. Local review (HIGH — enforcement trust boundary). Targeted Miri clean (core validate/repair/protocol, server schema_reject); full Miri concurrent. → *Schema — the enforcing server's op-ingress rejects a newly-introduced declared-slot kind mismatch (`OpsRejected` / `SchemaViolation`); repairable violations ride to read-time repair, an undeclared slot is admissible.*
## 2026-07-16 · audit-fix tree-move × displacement / #299 · a tree-move (and the delete that must win over it, and the insert that materialises its node) applies into a *materialised-but-displaced* children sequence instead of buffering-forever or dropping — the move fold is a pure function of the move-set + tombstone-set, independent of any parent's transient slot state
**Changed:** clarifies the **Tree Moves** invariant (ARCHITECTURE §Tree Moves) that displacement retention extends to a displaced container's *children sequence*, not only its own retained handle. The convergence oracle (with the tree-move arm restored, left out of #296) surfaced a **CRDT convergence violation**: an `XmlMove` did not converge when the move's source or destination parent was concurrently displaced (its map slot lost to a higher-stamped scalar / other create). The move's `XmlInsertChild` (materialise), the `XmlMove` (relocate), and the `ListDelete` (delete-wins-over-move) all gated on `resolvable(target)` / `live_list`, which treat a *displaced* container identically to an *unseen* one — so a parent born displaced buffered the child insert forever (node lost), dropped a move into a displaced destination (log divergence), and buffered the delete of a moved node's birth placement while the move committed elsewhere (delete-wins held on one replica, not the other). No STATE_VERSION change (readiness/apply-routing only, no encoded-state shape change); no ARCHITECTURE end-state change (realises the existing "Displacement retains, it does not forget" convergence requirement across the children axis).
- **Materialised, not installed, is the readiness bar for the sequence-editing op families.** `ready` / `tx_group_ready` gate `XmlInsertChild`, `XmlMove`, and `ListDelete` on the target children **sequence being materialised** (present in the list registry) rather than **installed** (reachable through an all-installed ancestor chain); `insert_xml_child`, `apply_move`, and the `ListDelete` apply path record into the materialised list handle regardless of its displaced flag. A displaced parent retains its children, so the edit is applied and **retained hidden** — the fold re-derives visibility from the move-set, rendering the node hidden while its effective parent is displaced and revealing it if the slot is re-won. A parent whose container is **unmaterialised** (its create genuinely unseen) still buffers — that is the only true not-ready state.
- **Why installed-gating diverged.** A moved node keeps a live placement under its new parent even while its birth sequence is displaced. Gating on *installed* dropped or buffered the op depending on the transient slot state *at apply time*, which differs by arrival order: forward arrival (parent installed when the op lands) recorded it; reverse arrival (displacing scalar first, parent born displaced) dropped/buffered it — the same op set folding to two trees. Making the three op families apply into a retained-displaced sequence makes the fold a pure function of the move-set + tombstone-set, byte-independent of arrival order.
- **Specs.** `crates/core/tests/xml_move.rs`: a move survives its **source** parent's displacement (`a_move_out_survives_the_source_parents_displacement`), a move into a **displaced destination** converges (`a_move_into_a_displaced_destination_converges`), and a concurrent **delete still wins** over a move when the birth parent is displaced (`a_concurrent_delete_still_wins_over_a_move_when_the_source_parent_is_displaced`) — each red before the fix, green after. `crates/core/tests/convergence.rs`: the tree-move **and** xml-child-delete arms are restored to `random_edit`; the full shuffle + reverse + double sweep passes at 8000 native seeds (the two residual seeds — source- and destination-displaced — fixed with no deferral). The delete-wins gap was caught by the HIGH local review (a second finder pass) after the initial move fix and fixed with its own regression test. Targeted Miri clean (convergence / xml_move / xml_doc / treemove / doc); full core Miri concurrent. → *the Kleppmann tree-move now converges across a displacement of any parent on the move path*.

## 2026-07-16 · text char_id sub-lamport offset / audit-fix · a text run derives one id per codepoint by carrying the lamport surplus into a new `Stamp.offset` field, so a run based at the lamport ceiling keeps every codepoint distinct instead of collapsing
**Changed:** `Text::insert_run` derived each codepoint's char_id as `(base.lamport.saturating_add(k), client)`. At `base.lamport == u64::MAX` — reachable by an adversarial/ceiling-clocked wire op — the `saturating_add` collapsed every codepoint of a run onto the same id: `insert_run(MAX, "ab")` produced `"a"`, silently dropping the rest. The collapse is convergent and non-crashing (both replicas lose the same char), so a normal test run never catches it; the original audit assumed "saturation ⇒ distinct ids", which is wrong (saturation collides at the top exactly as wrapping does at the bottom). `Stamp` gains an `offset: u64` (the char_id is now `(lamport, client, offset)`); `Stamp::run_member(k)` counts the lamport up from the base and, once it would pass `u64::MAX`, carries the surplus into `offset`, so N codepoints always get N distinct, replica-independent ids. No end-state feature change (realizes the already-intended "every codepoint gets a stable char_id" invariant at the ceiling); pre-release, so the wire format changed freely (no version shim).
- **offset is a last-resort tiebreak, so nothing else moves.** The total order is `(lamport, client, offset)` with `offset == 0` for every op stamp and every non-ceiling codepoint, so all existing comparisons are byte-identical; `offset` only separates a single client's codepoints pinned at `lamport == MAX`. A minted op always bases a run at `offset == 0`, where the carry is exact; the offset carry itself `saturating_add`s, so a crafted stamp decoded near the offset ceiling stays total (never panics) and convergent rather than opening a DoS. On the wire the offset rides behind a present-flag byte (`0` when absent), so an offset-0 stamp — every op stamp and non-ceiling codepoint — costs one extra byte, not a full `u64`. The tombstone run-length codec compresses only the offset-0 lamport-consecutive chain, so a ceiling run's members fall out as length-1 records that round-trip their offset verbatim — deterministic encode, faithful decode.
- **Both ceiling tests strengthened from assert-nothing to the real property** (`crates/core/tests/text.rs`, `crates/core/tests/transaction.rs`): a multi-codepoint run based at `u64::MAX` yields all codepoints with distinct char_ids (through `insert_run`, through the tx `apply()` boundary, across a snapshot round-trip, and convergent across two replicas). Confirmed red against the saturating derivation (`"ab"`→`"a"`), green after. Local review (HIGH). Targeted core Miri (text/transaction/state_seq/convergence) clean; full core Miri + CI sharded-Miri gated. → *Text — a char_id is `(lamport, client, offset)`; the offset disambiguates the codepoints of a run based at the lamport ceiling so a run never collapses.*

## 2026-07-15 · reveal-on-move-in / #294 · a node born in a denied subtree then moved into a readable one is revealed to the reader at its current position, converging the op stream with the snapshot projection — resolves the mirror-case limitation the move-into-denied entry flagged
**Changed:** resolves the deferred **born-in-a-denied-subtree, then moved into a readable one** limitation the move-into-denied entry (below) recorded. That case did not converge: a fresh op-catch-up joiner never received the node's create (its read path is the denied *birth* position) and the readable `XmlMove` it did receive could not materialize a node it never had, so the op joiner **lacked** the node — while the snapshot projection, judging by the node's readable *current* position, **kept** it. The **user chose the semantics: REVEAL ON MOVE-IN** — a node whose current position a reader can read becomes visible to that reader at that position (dragging a private page into a shared folder reveals it to collaborators), consistent with #293's "you see the node at positions you can read." No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (extends the #284/#293 op-join≡snapshot-join convergence across the mirror tree-move); no STATE_VERSION change — the mechanism is a redaction-time op synthesis, never persisted.
- **The synthesis: a shell op delivered by current position, not birth path.** The op stream withholds the node's create (birth path denied) and cannot re-target it — a create's element id derives from its birth list, so no create into the readable destination could reproduce the node's identity. So the server synthesizes a new redaction-only op, `OpKind::XmlReveal { node, tag }`, carrying the node's stable id and current tag with **no placement**; applied, it materializes the node shell (its attrs Map + children List by derived id) and marks it *revealed-pending*. The reader's (readable) `XmlMove` then lands the shell's **first** placement — `apply_move`/`XmlMove` readiness accept a revealed-pending node exactly as they accept one with a prior placement, where a move of any other placement-less node (a keyed root) stays a no-op. The node's readable subtree **content** ops (attrs, descendants) need no synthesis: their targets are the node's derived sub-container ids, whose current path is the node's now-readable position, so the ordinary per-path redaction already delivers them and the apply buffer folds them onto the shell once it exists. `XmlReveal` is never authored, logged, or persisted (a placed node is an ordinary moved node), so `encode_state`/STATE_VERSION are unchanged; the op wire codec gains tag 21.
- **Derived from the same projected state, so the two seams agree by construction.** `Document::reveal_ops(reads)` is the exact mirror of `project_read_paths`: for every movable node it emits a shell iff the node's **birth** list path is denied **and** its **current** path is readable — precisely the nodes the projection keeps at their readable current position. **Catch-up** prepends `reveal_ops` to a partial reader's filtered delta (whole-document readers get none — nothing is denied; a shell is added only for a node whose placing move survives into the delta, so a shell never rides without its move). **Live fan-out** prepends, for any node an `XmlMove` in the batch reveals to a recipient (born-denied to it, now readable), the shell **plus the node's now-readable subtree content replayed from the room log** (`Hub::reveal_backfill` — the content authored while the subtree was private is withheld on the live stream and absent from the move's batch, so without the replay a live reader would materialize an empty node and diverge; the catch-up seam needs no replay, its whole-delta re-filter already delivers the content by current position). Both call the server's element-context resolver, so an **element-scoped** grant that makes the node readable resolves identically to a **path** grant on both seams.
- **No history leak.** The reveal carries only the node's current identity + tag; the shell is stamped from the node's birth stamp (so the reader's clock reaches what the origin advanced) under an id derived from the node in a reserved reveal namespace (a UUIDv5, disjoint from a real replica's UUIDv7 ClientId, so it can never alias — and never a real authored op the reader could reconstruct the private origin from). No op of the node's denied origin (its birth create, its origin fragment, its pre-move content in the denied position) is delivered — asserted by a leak check that no revealed op targets the origin subtree.
- **A reveal is server-only, never client-authored.** `XmlReveal` is a redaction synthesis, not an authored op; the op-submit write gate rejects a client that submits one as a protocol violation, so it can never enter the log or the authoritative document (it would otherwise inject an unplaced, arbitrarily-identified node shell). Committed on the wire only, per-recipient.
- **Out of scope (doc-ACL × zones + descendant-regrant metadata).** Reveal shells/back-fill are zone-blind; in a room combining doc-ACL with zones, a reveal for a node in a partition a zone-scoped subscriber cannot read is not converged — but it never strands stray state: catch-up gates the shell on its move's presence in the (zone-filtered) delta, and live fan-out stamps the shell + back-fill with the move's zone so the per-channel zone filter co-travels them (a shell never rides without its move). This is within the documented doc-ACL × zones op-stream divergence class (#278). Separately, the `XmlMove` op-read gate resolves a single leaf path where the projection prefix-walks ancestors, so a move into a descendant re-granted below a denied ancestor is delivered (applied as a no-op) even though no shell is emitted and the state converges to absent — a pre-existing metadata surface of the move gate, not introduced here.
- **Convergence bar = materialized content, not whole-state bytes.** An op-catch-up joiner and a snapshot joiner materialize the **same tree** (deep `board_render` equality) and each re-encodes canonically (no dangling reference); they legitimately differ only in each replica's own identity header and its causal `seen` frontier, which the snapshot projection deliberately clears for a partial reader — so literal whole-`encode_state` equality is not the invariant (no convergence test in the suite asserts it), materialized convergence is. A whole-document reader, whose frontier is not cleared, is byte-identical past the identity header. `project_zones` shares the current-position gap class and is left as-is (out of scope). Specs: `crates/core/tests/state_project_read.rs` (`reveal_ops` reveals the born-denied node, is empty for a born-readable node and a whole-document reader, and shell+move converges with the projection) + `crates/server/tests/acl_redaction.rs` (op-join≡snapshot-join for **path** + **element** scope, a **deep** subtree reveals its whole current state, a **live** reader is revealed on the move-in, whole-document reader unchanged, no-ACL regression, no origin leak — the #293 forward case still converges). The redaction×move convergence work is now **COMPLETE both directions** (move-into-denied keep-at-origin + move-out-of-denied reveal). Local review (HIGH). CI sharded-Miri gated all crates; targeted core + server acl/state/doc/move Miri clean locally. → *Authorization — doc-ACL redaction × tree-move now converges in both directions: a node moved into a denied subtree stays at its readable origin, a node moved out of one is revealed at its readable destination.*

## 2026-07-15 · move-into-denied snapshot convergence · a node moved into a denied subtree is kept at its readable origin in the snapshot projection, matching the op stream; born-in-denied is a documented limitation
**Changed:** `Document::project_read_paths` (the doc-ACL snapshot half) redacted a movable XML node by its **current** position. That diverged from the op stream and, worse, left a **dangling reference** that crashed the snapshot decode: a node created readable (its `XmlInsertChild` admitted at its birth list's path) then moved into a denied subtree via `XmlMove` (whose read path is the denied *destination*, so the reader never receives it) is still held by a fresh op-catch-up joiner at its **origin** — but the projection dropped it by its denied current position, leaving its birth slot referencing a purged node in the retained origin list → `decode_state` fails `dangling reference`. This makes the projection judge a moved node the way the op stream does: **a node created in a readable subtree and moved into a denied one is kept at its readable origin**, with the subtree it grew in the denied position cleared (a fresh joiner never received those content ops — their read path is the denied position). No ARCHITECTURE change (extends the #284/#285/#287 op-join≡snapshot-join convergence property across a tree-move); no STATE_VERSION change.
- **Keep-at-origin, not drop-by-position.** A movable node whose birth list is readable but whose current position is denied is un-purged (with the attrs map + children list a decoded `XmlElement` needs); its move placement/log edge into the denied destination and every placement/move into a denied position are dropped, and the fold is rebuilt (`refold_projected_moves`, the same reconstruction `restore_moves` runs on decode) so the node re-folds under its readable origin exactly where a decoded joiner lands it. A retained list at a denied path (the children list of a kept-at-origin node) is **cleared**, not tombstoned — a tombstone would leak the dropped descendants' stamps (and thus their derivable ids) and add a slot the op joiner lacks. Holds for both **path** scope and **element** scope: an element grant on the origin container resolves to the origin path on both seams, so the node is kept identically.
- **Documented limitation (needs a design decision): born-in-a-denied-subtree, then moved into a readable one.** The mirror case does **not** converge from a current-state snapshot. A fresh op joiner never receives the node's create (its read path is the denied birth position) and the move it does receive cannot materialise a node it never had, so the op joiner **lacks** the node — but the snapshot, judging by the readable current position, **keeps** it. Making them converge needs either an op-stream change (deliver a node's create by its current/grantable position, not its birth path) or a Fugue-safe way to remove a single node from a populated readable list (today a list node can only be tombstoned — which leaks — or dropped with its whole list, since it anchors the RGA/Fugue tree). Both are a redaction-architecture change beyond the snapshot projection; deferred. The wholly-general convergence (a node modified *after* moving into denied) is likewise unreconstructable from a current-state snapshot without an op-stream withdrawal, since a live reader's view freezes at move time. `project_zones` shares the current-position class of this gap and is unaffected by this change.


## 2026-07-15 · Element-id ACL / #291 · doc-ACL grants keyed by a stable ElementId that resolve to the element's current path, so a grant follows the element across a tree-move; STATE_VERSION 10→11
**Changed:** a doc-ACL grant was keyed only by a **position path** (`AclTuple.path`), which is a security hole under the shipped Kleppmann `XmlMove` tree-move: moving a restricted element leaves its `deny` at the OLD path (now governing whatever slides in) while the element lands at a NEW path under possibly-open ACL. This adds a grant keyed by a **stable ElementId** that resolves to the element's CURRENT path at check time. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (realizes movable-content permissions over the already-scoped ACL model); STATE_VERSION 10→11.
- **`AclScope { Path | Element }` on the tuple and the `AclGrant` op.** A `Path` scope is a fixed structural location (a zone, a well-known field) — it governs whatever occupies that slot. An `Element` scope is movable content that carries its own permission (a page dragged between parents, a card across columns). Element scoping closes **both** holes tree-move opens: **exfil-by-move** (a restricted element cannot be freed by relocating it) and **stranded-restriction** (the restriction moves with the element instead of stranding on the old slot).
- **Element→path resolution is an injected resolver, so core stays index-free.** *Forced realization:* the pure core evaluator hosts no element index, yet must map an `Element` scope to a path to compose in the EXISTING deny-overrides / inheritance / provenance lattice. So the evaluator takes an injected `id → current path` resolver (a `&dyn Fn(ElementId) -> Option<Vec<u8>>`); it resolves every tuple's scope up front, then the whole authority walk (rooting / attenuation / provenance-bounded deny) runs over the resolved paths unchanged — an element scope composes exactly as a path scope pinned to the element's live location. The delegation/attenuation rooting walk resolves the scope BEFORE rooting.
- **Unresolvable id → inert (fail-closed), never fail-open.** An `Element` scope whose id names no live element resolves to nothing: it roots nothing, governs nothing, owns nothing, and denies nothing. A `Path` scope never consults the resolver, so all existing path-ACL behavior is byte-identical.
- **Server injects its element-context index as the resolver** (`index::element_paths`) at every doc-ACL enforcement seam — the write gate, per-op read redaction (fan-out + catch-up), and snapshot projection — so an element resolves to the same current path everywhere. Snapshot projection derives its resolver from the decoded snapshot it projects, so it cannot drift from what is projected. An unresolvable-element ACL tuple redacts by **root read on both catch-up seams**, so an op-served and a snapshot-served reader converge on it.
- Pre-release: a `STATE_VERSION` mismatch is rejected hard, no dual-decode shim. Core ACL-format change → CI sharded-Miri gated all crates (core 20m, server shards 15–20m, ffi 5m, ≤30min); targeted core + server ACL/state/doc Miri clean locally. → *Authorization — path/zone ACL keys stable structural locations; element-id ACL keys movable content that carries its permission across a tree-move.*

## 2026-07-15 · Faithful container-field migration / #289 · the persist-vs-accept gate RESOLVED as PERSIST — persist the deleted container's create identity so the snapshot seam re-keys it byte-identically with the op seam; STATE_VERSION 9→10
**Changed:** resolves the long-standing `faithful container-field migration` design gate. A schema rename/drop of a container field applied to a created-then-deleted container diverged between the two migration seams: the op seam still holds the create op (resurrects the container live at the old key + re-keys the delete), but the materialized snapshot had overwritten the container slot's create-stamp with the delete stamp, so `migrate_leaf_slots` carried the tombstone verbatim under the old key — op-served and snapshot-served joiners then held the deleted field's tombstone under **different dead keys**, byte-divergent state for one op set. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (realizes the already-scoped op↔snapshot convergence for container fields); STATE_VERSION 9→10.
- **Chose PERSIST over ACCEPT.** *The gate:* bump the snapshot format to persist the lost create identity (faithful, pays bytes) OR accept + document the residual divergence (zero build cost, both seams already agree the field is deleted, disagreeing only on the dead key). Chose persist because the tax is **narrow** and it restores strict op↔snapshot byte-convergence — the same property #274 gave leaf fields, now extended to container fields. The cost falls **only on a deleted-container tombstone: one stamp + a 1-byte kind = 25 bytes**; a live slot and a leaf tombstone pay nothing, and the baseline per-slot LWW stamp was already universal, so no across-the-board snapshot growth.
- **Persist the create *identity*, not just the stamp.** *Forced realization:* a snapshot key can host more than one container kind over its life (a map created+deleted, then a list created+deleted at the same key), and both derived ids stay registered — so the stamp alone cannot pick which container to resurrect. The tombstone records `(create-stamp, kind)` (new map-slot tag `SLOT_CONTAINER_TOMB`); `migrate_leaf_slots_scoped` resurrects the exact recorded-kind container live at the old key and re-keys the delete, reinstating it only when it wins the old key by LWW. XML kinds derive ids by node not key, so they are not resurrectable here and record nothing (their deleted slot migrates as a leaf, the pre-existing behavior).
- **Merge stays commutative.** `Map::merge` carries the create identity of the LWW winner only — never a mix of the two entries — so the retained `(stamp, kind)` is a deterministic function of the winning delete, not of the merge order.
- Pre-release: a `STATE_VERSION` mismatch is rejected hard, no dual-decode shim. Core state-format change → CI sharded-Miri gated all crates (core 22m47s, server shards 11–20m, ffi 6m, ≤30min); full local core Miri clean (1388 tests). **The migration follow-on list is now empty.** → *Migration — op↔snapshot byte-convergence now holds for container fields as well as leaf fields.*

## 2026-07-15 · Clone-room client-wire surface / #288 · the #196 `Hub::clone_room` primitive exposed to clients over a room-keyed frame; authz = read-on-src + management-write-on-dst; cross-shard clone is a documented no-op, not cross-node transfer
**Changed:** closes the #196 "wire/session/SDK exposure deferred" note — the `clone_room(src, dst)` primitive ("duplicate this doc as a template") is now reachable by clients. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (realizes the already-scoped client exposure of an existing primitive); no STATE_VERSION change (a new client frame, not a persisted-format change).
- **Frame shape — a small explicit result, not a list.** *Forced realization:* branch mutations reply with the refreshed `Branches` list (their authoritative post-state); a clone has no post-state collection to echo — its whole outcome is created-or-not. So `Message::CloneRoom { src, dst }` (wire tag 42, the next free tag after the Branch block 27-33 + Diff 40/41) replies with a dedicated `CloneRoomResult { dst, created }` (tag 43), keyed by `dst` so a client reads the result of the clone it issued (the `clone_results` view, parallel to `branches`/`diffs`). Room-keyed, runnable before any subscription — cloning is a room-level op.
- **Authz composes two tiers over two rooms.** *Forced realization:* a clone READS `src`'s whole state AND CREATES `dst`, so one gate cannot express it. The dispatch requires Read on `src` (the `branch_authorized` read tier a branch list / diff uses — doc-ACL abstains, deployment+schema decide) AND the branch-management write tier on `dst` (the create). Deny either → recoverable `Forbidden`; unauthenticated → violation; a persist `io::Error` → `internal` (closes); never a panic. `created == false` (a clean no-op the client can act on) when `src` is unknown or `dst` already exists.
- **Leader-redirect on `dst`, and a documented cross-shard limitation.** The create persists a new room, so like a branch mutation it is leader-redirected — on `dst` (the room being created/persisted), so `dst` lands on the node that will own it. *Forced realization (all 3 review angles converged):* the clone then reads `src` from that same node, so `src` and `dst` must co-locate on one leader; a cluster where they hash to different leaders finds no local `src` and reports `created == false` rather than misplacing `dst` on the wrong leader (where every later access would redirect to an empty HRW leader). Redirect-on-`dst` makes the failure mode a clean, observable no-op instead of an unreachable-but-"created" room. Cross-leader clone needs genuine cross-node state transfer — out of scope for this single-hub primitive, documented in the dispatch comment. Single-node (the shipped default, membership `None`) is unaffected: no redirect, both rooms local.
- **SDK fan-out mirrors BranchFork** across all four bindings (FFI `crdtsync_client_clone_room` + `crdtsync_client_clone_result`, Go `CloneRoom`/`CloneResult`, Python `clone_room`/`clone_result`, wasm `cloneRoom`/`cloneResult`). Core-touching (`protocol.rs`, `client.rs`) → CI sharded-Miri gates all crates; targeted core + server + FFI clone-suite Miri clean locally. → *Snapshots / Export-Import — the #196 clone primitive now has its client surface.*

## 2026-07-15 · Doc-ACL per-recipient RangedElement redaction / #287 · marks/annotations redacted by their anchor-sequence paths (require-all, outbound-only), previously root-gated
**Changed:** completes the §Authorization finer-grain wire redaction — the final axis after op-stream (4b), snapshot projection (4d), and ACL-tuple redaction (4e/#285). `RangedCreate`/`RangedSetPayload`/`RangedDelete` ops and persisted RangedElements were root-gated (only whole-document readers received them); now each is redacted by the path(s) of the sequence(s) its endpoints anchor. Per-recipient doc-ACL wire redaction is now COMPLETE across every op/state axis: ops, snapshot, ACL tuples, and RangedElements. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (realizes the already-scoped noted follow-on); no STATE_VERSION change (redaction narrows what is sent, not the persisted format).
- **Governing rule — require-all over anchor-seq paths.** *Forced realization:* a mark/annotation reveals content-region info at BOTH endpoints, so it is visible to a recipient iff it can read the path of EVERY sequence its endpoints anchor (fail-closed). The single-sequence mark (the common case, the 6a-iv path-façade marks) has `start.seq == end.seq` → one governing path; the cross-element range (ranged 3b) has two → both must read. A single-path return cannot express this, so the fan-out/catch-up filters switch to `acl::op_read_paths` (returns an op's governing path *set* — a Ranged op's distinct anchor seq paths, one path for every other op) and require `recipient_reads_path` on ALL of them. `Document::project_read_paths` keeps a RangedElement iff every anchor seq's path reads, by the same rule.
- **Anchor→path resolution and fallbacks.** A `RangedCreate` carries its anchors; a `RangedSetPayload`/`RangedDelete` carries only the range id, resolved to its anchors through `Hub::ranged_anchors` / `Document::ranged_anchors` — the held anchor set, **tombstoned ranges included** (a just-applied delete's target is already tombstoned), mirroring how a revoke resolves its tuple through `acl_records`. An anchor seq the element-path index does not resolve (a since-deleted or re-parented sequence), or a range id no held entry carries, falls back to the root — so only a whole-document reader carries it, fail-closed.
- **Outbound-only** — the server keeps the full RangedElement set and evaluates authority over all of it; only what each recipient RECEIVES narrows, identical stance to #285.
- **Convergence (asserted in both suites):** a fresh op-served partial reader (gets a `RangedCreate` only when it reads all anchor seqs) and a fresh snapshot-served partial reader (RangedElement kept only when all anchor seqs readable) materialize the SAME subset — same require-all path authority both sides, same root fallback when an anchor is unresolvable. Core-touching (`crates/core/src/doc.rs`) → the full sharded Miri gate ran green (slowest job server 1/3 ~17m25s, ≤30min); targeted core + server Miri clean locally. → *Authorization — doc-ACL wire redaction now COMPLETE across every op/state axis: ops, snapshot, ACL tuples, and RangedElements.*

## 2026-07-15 · Doc-ACL per-recipient ACL-tuple redaction / #285 · ACL ops and tuples redacted by their governing path (outbound-only), previously root-gated
**Changed:** completes the §Authorization "per-recipient ACL-tuple redaction, since ACL state is itself privacy-sensitive" item. Doc-ACL wire redaction (op-stream 4b + snapshot 4d) sent every `AclGrant`/`AclRevoke` op and every persisted ACL tuple only to whole-document (root-gated) readers; now each is redacted by the tuple's **own governing path**, so a subtree reader receives the ACL state governing paths it may read and none on paths it may not. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (this realizes an already-scoped item); no STATE_VERSION change (redaction narrows what is sent, not the persisted format).
- **Redaction by governing path, not root.** *Forced realization:* a tuple reveals a subject, an effect, and the existence of a governed path — itself privacy-sensitive — so the 4b/4d root gate withheld from a subtree reader the ACL state on paths it legitimately reads. `acl::op_read_path` now maps `AclGrant{path}` to that path (already the same encoded-path format it returns) and `AclRevoke{id}` to the tombstoned tuple's path (resolved through the server's full record set; a root fallback for an id no held tuple carries → a moot revoke reaching only a whole-doc reader, so a recipient sees the revoke exactly where it saw the grant). `Document::project_read_paths` keeps each ACL tuple iff its own path is readable by the predicate, mirroring the op rule. Ranged annotations stay root-gated — path-scoped ranged/marks redaction is a separate privacy axis (follow-on).
- **Outbound-only — the server keeps its FULL tuple set and evaluates authority over all of it; only what each recipient RECEIVES is narrowed.** A partial-ACL client therefore holds an incomplete, advisory view (per ARCHITECTURE "SDK canDo is advisory, client-side checks advisory only") — intended, max-privacy: sending ancestor-chain tuples to "complete" a subtree reader's provenance would leak the ancestor ACL, the opposite of the goal.
- **Convergence (asserted in both suites):** an op-served partial reader (AclGrant/AclRevoke ops only on its readable paths) and a snapshot-served partial reader (ACL tuples only on its readable paths) materialize the same ACL subset — same path authority, same result. Core-touching (`crates/core/src/doc.rs`) → the full sharded Miri gate ran; targeted core + server Miri clean locally. → *Authorization — doc-ACL wire redaction now COMPLETE across ops + snapshot + ACL-state-itself; Ranged/marks redaction remains a noted follow-on.*

## 2026-07-15 · Doc-ACL Slice 4d / #284 · doc-ACL snapshot projection for partial readers — served, not refused; a path predicate matching `op_read_path`, with all-prefixes subtree semantics
**Changed:** closes the explicit 4b deferral (recorded 2026-07-13): a subtree-scoped doc-ACL reader was **refused** a compacted room's cold-start `Catchup::Snapshot` because the snapshot could not be op-filtered. It is now **served a projected snapshot** — the state narrowed to its readable paths — mirroring how a zone-limited subscriber is already served a `Document::project_zones`-narrowed snapshot. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (§Authorization already scoped per-recipient read redaction on every seam; this fills the snapshot seam 4b left as a refusal). No STATE_VERSION change — a read projection needs no format change.
- **New core primitive `Document::project_read_paths(reads: impl Fn(&[Vec<u8>]) -> bool)` — the doc-ACL analogue of `project_zones`, the state half of the per-path read redaction.** Core hosts no ACL: the server passes in its composed read verdict at a `core::path`, the exact per-path authority `acl::op_read_path` gates each op on, so the projection drops precisely the elements the op stream withholds. The server helper `session::project_snapshot_reads` decodes the snapshot, drives the projection from `recipient_reads_path`, re-encodes; the existing `project_snapshot_zones` then stacks on top, so a reader limited by both doc-ACL and zones is served the intersection.
- **A path *predicate*, not a `HashSet<ElementId>` of authorized containers — forced by a review-caught leak.** *Forced realization:* the first cut passed the server-resolved authorized container-id set (the shape `project_zones` uses for zones). Two review agents proved it cannot express a **leaf-level** read decision (`op_read_path` gates a keyed leaf op at `path+key`, container granularity can't) nor a **nested grant below a denied ancestor** — both would leak state the op stream withholds, re-opening the very leak the 4b refusal closed. The predicate resolves the exact `op_read_path` for a container (its path), a leaf slot (map path + slot key), and doc-level ACL/ranged ops (root), so all three converge with the op stream.
- **Subtree semantics = *every prefix* of a path must read, not just its own.** A container is dropped when any path level above it is unreadable, even where a more-specific grant re-opens the child: op catch-up withholds the create op at the denied level, so a child whose parent create never arrived can never apply on an op-served joiner — it materializes neither, so the snapshot must drop it too (no orphaned subtree left in the by-id registries for `encode_state` to emit). Doc-level ACL tuples + ranged annotations are root-path-governed (kept only with a readable root); a cut counter's registry entry is pruned (no phantom tally); `seen`/buffer are scrubbed once anything drops (no op-count leak); a whole-document reader is an identity projection (byte-identical re-encode).
- **Convergence is the load-bearing correctness property** (asserted in `tests/acl_redaction.rs`): a snapshot-served partial joiner materializes byte-for-subtree the same replica an op-served joiner does, because both drop exactly the same elements. Core-touching (`crates/core/src/doc.rs`) → the full sharded Miri gate ran (slowest job core at 21m, ≤30min); targeted core + server Miri clean locally. → *Authorization — Doc-ACL epic now: 4a enforcement · 4b redaction · 4c grant/revoke SDK · 4d snapshot projection.*

## 2026-07-15 · Zones Unit 5 / #281 · zone-scoped subscribe client surface across all SDKs; `resume` preserves the channel's zone selector
**Changed:** exposes the Unit-3 `Subscribe.zone` selector (already on the wire + enforced server-side) out through the client-session subscribe surface and all four SDKs, closing the deferred SDK-facing subscribe surface Unit 3 named. No new wire tag, no `protocol.rs` change — the `zone: Vec<u8>` field already rides `Message::Subscribe`. `ClientSession::subscribe_zone(room, zone)` is the whole addition to the core client, structured exactly like `subscribe_branch`; the empty-zone `subscribe`/`subscribe_branch` shortcuts route through a shared `subscribe_inner(room, branch, zone)`.
- **The client `Room` records the channel's `zone` so `resume` re-issues it, rather than always re-subscribing whole-room.** *Forced realization:* `resume` re-emits a held channel's `Subscribe` from its caught-up position after a reconnect; the pre-Unit-5 code hard-coded `zone: Vec::new()`, so a reconnect on a zone-scoped channel would silently *widen* the subscription to the whole room — a correctness gap the moment a zone selector exists. The fix mirrors how `resume` already preserves `branch`: `Room` gains a `zone: Vec<u8>` field, and `resume` clones it. A `zone(channel)` accessor mirrors `branch(channel)`. The server enforces a resumed zone-scoped `Subscribe` identically to a fresh one, so no server change is needed.
- **Semantics are Unit 3's, unchanged:** empty zone = whole room (every zone the actor may read + root); a name = that partition + root. SDK surfaces: FFI `crdtsync_client_subscribe_zone`, wasm `subscribeZone`, Go `SubscribeZone`, Python `subscribe_zone` — each mirrors its `subscribe_branch` sibling's shape. Core-touching (`client.rs`) → CI Miri gates the PR; targeted core + FFI client-suite Miri clean locally. Specs assert the zone rides the frame (decoded off the wire), the empty-zone shortcut stays empty, and `resume` preserves the zone; per-SDK marshal/receive tests mirror each existing subscribe test. → *Zones — the epic's client surface is now complete (declaration → resolution → enforcement → per-zone streams → SDK subscribe); Unit 4 (cross-zone token) stays deferred.*

## 2026-07-15 · CI Miri gate / #282 · shard the server crate across 3 nextest partitions to hold the Miri gate ≤30min
**Changed:** the Miri gate wall-clock is the slowest single job, and the `crdtsync-server` job had grown to ~31m — over the 30-min ceiling. The `miri` matrix converts from a bare `crate` list to explicit `include` entries so only the server crate fans further: `crdtsync-server` runs as three parallel jobs, each `cargo +nightly miri nextest run -p crdtsync-server --partition count:N/3`, while core and ffi stay single jobs. The three shards share one `rust-cache` key (`crate`, not partition) because they build the identical crate and restore the same warm build without clobbering.
**Why:** nextest `--partition count:N/M` splits the test binaries' tests into M hash buckets and runs bucket N, so three shards cover the full set disjointly (locally verified: 748 server tests → 270/250/228, no overlap, union = full set — a silent under-run can't make the gate falsely green). The mechanism holding the gate ≤30min is now three-fold: the per-crate matrix (each crate a parallel job, wall-clock = slowest crate not the sum), the warm build cache (#280, skips cold Miri codegen + sysroot rebuild), and this server nextest partitioning (splits the long-pole crate below core's wall-clock). Measured on the landing run: server shards 12m44s / 21m19s / 15m47s, core 23m25s, ffi 4m09s — slowest job core at ~23m, comfortably under 30min. CI-yaml-only (`.github/workflows/rust.yml`), no source change.

## 2026-07-14 · Zones Unit 3 / #278 · zone-scoped subscription + per-zone replication streams + wire redaction (server); a container-create belongs to the created child's zone
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Zones' "each zone a separately replicated stream … an unauthorized zone withholds ops/snapshot/structure/existence/size" at the server, consuming the Unit-2 op-envelope `zone` substrate. Turns the causally-independent partitions into actual per-zone streams: a subscription is scoped to a zone, gated on the authorizer, and the fan-out + catch-up + snapshot redact by partition so an unauthorized zone is *wholly absent*. **Forces one Unit-2 refinement** (below): a container-create now belongs to the created child's zone, not the parent it targets. Server-plus-one-core-frame (`Subscribe` gains a `zone` field); the op wire/state break freely, no migration.
- **The zone selector rides `Message::Subscribe` as a `zone: Vec<u8>` field — empty is the whole room, a name scopes to one partition.** The honest minimal wire representation: the selector pairs with `branch` (both per-subscription), length-framed in the hand-rolled codec after `branch`. Empty = every zone the actor may read (plus the root partition); a named zone = that partition alone (plus root). A room that declares no zones ignores the selector — one implicit root partition, byte-identical to a zoneless subscribe. The opaque `Channel` handle resolves to include the zone server-side; the SDK-facing subscribe surface is deferred to Unit 5.
- **`Resource::Zone { room, zone }` gates a zone subscription; a refusal is generic, never confirming the zone exists.** A named-zone subscribe resolves the name to its compact id and gates on `authorizer.decide(Read, Resource::Zone)`; a nonexistent name and an unauthorized zone are answered with the **same** `forbidden("read denied")`, so a probe cannot tell a hidden real zone from a nonexistent one (strong isolation: existence itself is concealed). A deployment that abstains on the zone inherits the room read verdict — a zone is visible by default within a readable room, and an explicit per-zone deny is what carves out an isolated partition. The shipped `Acl` gains a `ResourceMatch::Zone { room, zone }` so this is expressible without a custom authorizer.
- **Per-zone streams are one channel per room with a per-recipient zone filter, not a channel per zone.** A whole-room subscribe fans every *authorized* zone over the one channel, filtered per-recipient by `op.zone` at the exact seam doc-ACL redaction and the awareness auth-filter already use. Chosen over one-channel-per-zone (physically cleaner isolation, but heavier and a wire/SDK multiplication) because the per-recipient filter reuses the existing redaction machinery and is correct: the subscription stores the set of authorized zone ids, and an op is admitted iff it is unzoned (root, always) or its zone is in the set. The per-zone clocks (Unit 2) make this leak-free — a recipient never sees another zone's clock advance, since it never receives another zone's ops.
- **The snapshot to a zone-limited subscriber is projected to its authorized partitions (`Document::project_zones`).** A below-floor (compacted-room) join is served a whole-replica snapshot; doc-ACL cannot redact one (it refuses a non-whole-document reader), but zones *can* — the projection decodes a throwaway copy, drops every element/edge/clock/annotation resolving to an unauthorized zone (detaching the hidden zone-root slots, purging the reachable containers + their metadata, dropping the hidden zones' clocks), clears the causal `seen` (a below-floor subscriber only ingests ops after the snapshot sequence, so it needs no prior dedup and the emptied set carries no op count), and filters the buffer to authorized partitions. A whole-zone or no-zones subscriber takes the snapshot verbatim (byte-identical regression).
- **A container-create belongs to the created child's zone, refining Unit 2's "stamp from the target's zone".** *Forced realization:* Unit 2 stamped a `MapCreate{board}` from its target (the root map it mutates) → the root partition, so the zone-root container's create rode a partition an unauthorized subscriber *does* see. That both (i) leaked the zone root's existence on the op stream and (ii) diverged from the snapshot projection, which drops the hidden container — two identically-authorized subscribers converging differently by compaction state. The fix: a container-create's zone is the created *child's* path (parent path + key), so a zone owns its whole lifecycle including its root container, and that create is withheld from an unauthorized subscriber on every seam. `zone_of_op(target, kind)` replaces `zone_of_target`; the Unit-2 clock specs are updated (the create now advances the child zone's clock, not the root's). Relatedly, `MapCursor::map`/`into_map` no longer re-emit a redundant `MapCreate` when the live map already occupies the slot (`holds_live_map`) — an idempotent re-create is a no-op on state but a real op in its partition, and re-emitting it on every nested write would churn the zone clock and bloat the log; a concurrent ancestor-delete is then resolved delete-wins rather than resurrected by the re-emit (convergent either way, and no test depended on resurrection).
- **First-cut limitations, documented (follow-on hardening within the Zones epic):** (1) doc-level ops — ACL grants and Ranged annotations — target the root doc-level set, so they are stamped `zone = None` and reach an unauthorized-zone subscriber on the *op* stream even when their referenced path/anchor is inside a hidden zone; the snapshot projection *does* strip them (by path/anchor), so the two seams diverge for a zone that uses fine-grained ACL or annotations. (2) The snapshot projection scrubs *reachable* state; a displaced-by-LWW or tombstoned container retained in the by-id registry for a hidden zone is not walked by `element_paths`, so it survives the re-encode. (3) Nested zones where an actor is authorized for an inner zone but denied its containing outer zone are not yet projected correctly. (4) The snapshot header's `seq` (total authored high-water across all partitions) is not scrubbed. Each is a narrow vector over the dominant structural-content isolation, which is real, consistent across the live/delta/snapshot seams, and tested. Specs `crates/server/tests/zone_streams.rs` (9: zone-scoped delivery, generic-denial no-existence-leak, forbidden≡nonexistent, whole-room omits the unauthorized zone, zone-W activity delivers nothing incl. no clock signal, no-zones regression, cold-start snapshot omits the other zone incl. its clock, authorized convergence, Acl-`ResourceMatch::Zone` isolation) + updated `crates/core/tests/zone_lamport.rs`; local review (four finder angles — surfaced the zone-root create divergence, the shipped-Acl gap, and the reachable-only projection edges; the first two fixed, the rest documented above). → *Zones — Unit 3 done; the isolation model is functionally real (declaration → resolution → enforcement → per-zone streams). Unit 5 (SDK subscribe surface) is the remaining zone work; Unit 4 (cross-zone token) stays deferred.*

## 2026-07-14 · Branches Unit 7b / #277 · the diff query rides a new client-wire frame (reusing 6b's client-wire-query approach per the 2026-07-14 Q2 ruling); the encoded `Change` list crosses as an opaque payload; DiffError → a new `ErrorCode::NotFound`
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Schema-Aware-Diff's client exposure of the branch/version diff, which Unit 7 (#251) deferred (it built only the server-side `Hub::diff_versions`/`diff_branches` computation). No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (the diff engine and its client exposure were already scoped); records the query frame shape, the opaque-change-payload marshaling, the read authz tier, and the `NotFound` error mapping. **This closes the branch-layer client exposure — 6b (management) + 7b (diff query) complete the branch epic's client surface.**
- **The diff query is a client-wire frame, not admin HTTP — the same ruling 6b settled.** Unit 7 built `Hub::diff_*` but had no way to return a diff to a client; the exposure question ("client-wire frames vs admin HTTP plane") was pre-settled by 6b's 2026-07-14 Q2 ruling: an app-facing query rides an in-band, session-authenticated, SDK-native frame, not the operator-authenticated admin plane. 7b applies it: `DiffQuery { room, kind, a, b }` → `DiffResult { room, changes }`, room-keyed like the Branch* set (a client may diff a room before it subscribes any of its branches).
- **`kind: DiffKind { Versions, Branches }` selects the state space; one frame, not two.** A tag byte (0 = two saved versions, 1 = two branches' HEADs) routes the server to `Hub::diff_versions` vs `Hub::diff_branches`. One request/response pair rather than a frame per kind — the two seams already share a `Change`-list return, so the wire distinction is a single discriminant.
- **The encoded `Change` list crosses as an opaque length-framed `Vec<u8>`, reusing `encode_changes`/`decode_changes`.** `DiffResult.changes` is not a structured `Vec<Change>` on the frame — it is the `encode_changes` byte string the FFI diff bindings (#232/#113) already marshal, carried as one `put_bytes` field. This keeps `protocol.rs` free of diff internals, and lets every SDK feed the payload straight into its EXISTING diff-decode binding (`crdtsync_diff_decode` / `DiffDecode` / `_decode_changes`) rather than a second decoder. `ClientSession` decodes on receipt (validating — a malformed payload → `ClientError::BadDiff`, no view touched) and holds a per-room `Vec<Change>` view.
- **Tags 40/41 — deliberately gapped past the 27–33 Branch* block.** Not 34: a concurrent sibling PR (Zones Unit 3) also edits `protocol.rs` (in the SUBSCRIBE/Channel region, not the `Message` enum), and a clearly-distinct number avoids a collision on either merge order. Hand-rolled codec, total decode (round-trip empty + many-change, truncation → `UnexpectedEof`, bad-kind-tag → `BadTag`, trailing → `TrailingBytes`, distinct-tag test).
- **DiffError → a new `ErrorCode::NotFound` (wire tag 7), recoverable; a decode fault → `internal`, closing.** An unknown version or branch is a well-formed query naming something absent — surfaced as an `Error` frame with the new `NotFound` code, connection stays open (mirroring a denied branch op's recoverable `Forbidden`), not a result-carrying variant. There was no existing code for "named resource absent" (`UnknownRoom` is room-specific), so `NotFound` is added to the closed `ErrorCode` enum and threaded through every exhaustive map (core codec tag 7, FFI `error_code_discriminant`, wasm `ErrorCode`, Python `ErrorCode.NOT_FOUND`). A snapshot that fails to decode is a server fault → `internal` (closes), as elsewhere.
