- **The diff reuses the read authz tier — a diff is a room-state read, no new axis.** `session.rs` gates `DiffQuery` with `branch_authorized(.., Action::Read)`, the same tier a `BranchList` read uses (doc-ACL abstains, deployment + schema tiers decide). Served locally from the replicated state — no leader redirect, because a read does not persist. Unauthenticated → violation, denied → recoverable `Forbidden`, unknown → `NotFound`, never a panic.
- **The full 4-way SDK fan-out lands in this PR — FFI + Go + Python + wasm.** FFI `crdtsync_client_diff_query(client, room, kind:u32, a, b)` + `crdtsync_client_diff_result(client, room, out)` (returns the encoded change bytes for the existing `crdtsync_diff_decode`; header regenerated, symbol-assert extended); Go `DiffQuery`/`DiffResult` + `DiffKind` consts; Python `diff_query`/`diff` + `DiffKind` IntEnum; wasm `diffQuery`/`diff` (`crates/wasm`). No follow-on slice is owed.
- Core-touching (`protocol.rs`) → **CI Miri gates the PR**; targeted core + FFI Miri clean locally. Specs: `crates/core/tests/protocol_diff.rs` (7), `client_diff.rs` (5), `crates/server/tests/diff_query.rs` (7), FFI `client.rs` diff round-trip, Go/Python/wasm marshal+receive tests. Local correctness review (medium) run, clean. → *Versioning and Branches / Schema-Aware Diff — the branch-layer client surface is now COMPLETE (subscribe #250 + management #275 + diff query #277).*

## 2026-07-14 · Zones Unit 2 / #276 · per-zone lamport clocks + an op-envelope `zone` dimension (compact zone id); the zone travels on the envelope, is not re-derived on merge
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Zones' "each zone a separately replicated stream (own lamport, own op-log partition)" at the core layer, and **corrects §Zones' claim that the op envelope's `zone` field was already reserved** — it was not present on `Op`; this unit *adds* it. The board's Unit-2 note ("already reserved in the op envelope") is likewise corrected. Pre-release: the op wire and state format break freely, no migration. **Core-only** — reuses `zone`/`schema`; STATE_VERSION 8 → 9. Cross-zone move/anchor rejection (Units 1b-ii-a/b) is the precondition this depends on, so the per-zone clocks never need cross-zone ordering.
- **The zone dimension is a compact zone id — `Op.zone: Option<u32>` — not the zone name or a stamp field.** `None` is the root partition (an unzoned target, or a document with no zones); `Some(i)` is the index of the target's zone in the order-preserving `Schema::zones()` (`zone::zone_id_of`, which `zone_of` now delegates to). An index, not the name, because the id is a pure function of the shared schema so every replica keys the same partition identically, and it stays schema-free on the wire (the codec resolves nothing). It rides `Op`, not `Stamp`: `Stamp` keeps its `(lamport, client)` shape, so every stamp-derived identity (list/text/xml node ids) is unchanged — uniqueness now holds *within* a partition, which suffices because a reachable container's zone is structurally fixed (element ids derive from parent+key) and cross-zone moves are forbidden, so no two ops that could collide on a stamp-derived id ever span zones.
- **The clock is partitioned: root rides `Document::lamport`, declared zones ride `zone_clocks: HashMap<u32,u64>`.** A local emit resolves the target's zone (`zone_of_target` walks the live tree, `element_paths`, the same projection the server index uses — gated on a bound non-empty `zones()`, so the no-zones path never walks) and stamps from *that* partition's clock; a merge advances the *op's envelope zone* by per-partition `max`. The zone is **honored from the envelope, never re-derived on receipt** — the sender resolved it deterministically from the shared schema, a buffered op whose target is not yet reachable still advances the right clock, and a later per-zone stream can route by it without materializing the tree. Per-partition `max` is order-independent, so two replicas folding the same op multiset converge to identical per-zone clocks; an op in one zone leaves every other clock untouched (no false causal edge). With no schema / no zones every op is `None` = the one root partition, byte-for-byte the pre-zones single global clock.
- **The state codec persists the per-zone clocks (root excluded — it rides `lamport`), id-sorted; an empty set is a no-zones document.** `Document::zone_clock(zone)` exposes a partition's high-water for the Unit-3 per-zone streams. Specs: `zone.rs` (`zone_id_of`), `zone_lamport.rs` (stamp-from-zone-clock, one zone doesn't bump another, two-zone concurrency, within-zone order, merge advances only the op's zone, multi-zone convergence over state + clocks, snapshot round-trip, no-zones regression, zoned xml/list cursor emit locking the borrow-drop discipline the tree walk relies on), `codec.rs` (zone round-trip + truncation + bad present-flag); targeted + full-local Miri clean. → *Zones — Unit 2 done; Unit 3 (server per-zone streams + zone-scoped subscribe/redaction) consumes this substrate.*

## 2026-07-14 · Branches Unit 6b / #275 · branch-management rides new in-band client-wire frames (not the admin plane); the Branch* frame set mirrors Version* but is room-keyed, not channel-keyed
**Changed:** resolves the human's 2026-07-14 Q2 design gate — app-facing branch operations (list/fork/fork-from-version/restore/publish/delete) are exposed over **new client-wire frames**, in-band on the same authenticated session, SDK-native and offline-queueable — **not** the admin HTTP plane (that plane stays reserved for operator observability). Realizes ARCHITECTURE §Versioning-and-Branches' client exposure of the branch engine (fork/publish/restore/list), which Unit 6 deferred (it exposed only branch-*subscribe*). No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (the branch engine and its client exposure were already scoped); records the frame set, the room-keyed shape, and the authz tier.
- **App-facing branch ops are client-wire frames, not admin HTTP.** The gate was "client-wire frames vs admin HTTP plane" for the branch-management surface. The ruling: branch management is an *app* operation (an editor forks a draft, publishes, restores a version) that a client must trigger with its own session auth, queue while offline, and see acked like any other request — so it belongs in-band on the client protocol, mirroring the Version* management sub-protocol (`VersionCreate`/`VersionList`/… → `Versions`) that already rides the client wire. The admin HTTP plane (schema registration, operator observability) is the wrong tool: it is operator-authenticated, out-of-band, and not offline-queueable. This same ruling pre-settles **Unit 7b** (diff query surface) — it too rides a new client-wire query frame, not the admin plane.
- **The Branch\* frames are room-keyed, unlike the channel-keyed Version\* frames.** Version management rides a *subscribed channel* (`VersionCreate { channel, … }`) because a version is always taken against a room the client already holds. Branch management is deliberately **room-keyed** (`BranchList { room }`, `BranchFork { room, name, from_branch }`, …): a client enumerates and forks a room's branches *before* it subscribes any of them (the list-to-pick-which-to-subscribe discovery flow), so requiring a prior subscription would be wrong. The server authorizes the frame's `room` directly (identity + `Resource::Room`), rather than resolving a room from a channel binding. `ClientSession` folds the `Branches` reply into a per-**room** view (`HashMap<room, Vec<BranchInfo>>`), not a per-channel one. The diff-query frame (7b) inherits this room/version-keyed shape.
- **Tags 27–33, appended past Gossip (26); a pure additive wire extension.** `BranchList`/`Branches`/`BranchFork`/`BranchForkFromVersion`/`BranchRestore`/`BranchPublish`/`BranchDelete`. `Branches` carries `Vec<BranchInfo { name, fork_point, head, published }>` — the marshaled subset of the server `Branch` a client needs to enumerate and act (published-vs-editable, fork base, head). Hand-rolled codec, total decode (bogus count grows-as-read, truncation → `UnexpectedEof`, distinct-tag test). A concurrent sibling PR (Zones Unit 2) edits `protocol.rs` in the op-envelope region, not the `Message` enum — no tag collision.
- **A branch op reuses the version-management authz tier — no new authz axis.** A branch op is a room-management action, so `session.rs` gates it exactly as version management: the doc-ACL tier abstains (`Decision::Abstain`), the deployment + schema tiers decide; a read (`BranchList`) needs `Action::Read`, a mutation needs `Action::Write`. A mutation persists to the room, so it is leader-redirected (a follower points the client at the leader) and replies with the fresh `Branches` set — the authoritative post-state, exactly as a version mutation replies with `Versions`; a read is served locally from the replicated registry. Unauthenticated → protocol violation, denied → recoverable `Forbidden`, a persist error → `internal`, never a panic. Each mutation dispatches to the existing `Hub` seam unchanged (`fork_branch` with `at = u64::MAX` clamped to the source head = "fork off HEAD"; `fork_branch_from_version`; `restore_as_branch(room, version, name)`; `publish`; `delete_branch`).
- **The full 4-way SDK fan-out lands in this PR — FFI + Go + Python + wasm.** FFI (`crdtsync_client_list_branches`/`_fork_branch`/`_fork_branch_from_version`/`_restore_branch`/`_publish_branch`/`_delete_branch` + `_branch_count`/`_branch_at` getters; the version-request marshaller `version_frame` was renamed `request_frame` to serve both), Go (`Branch` struct + methods), Python (`Branch` NamedTuple + methods), wasm (`crates/wasm` — the wasm-pack standalone crate excluded from the native workspace; `listBranches`/`forkBranch`/… + `branches` returning `{name, forkPoint, head, published}[]`). No follow-on slice is owed.
- Core-touching (`protocol.rs`) → **CI Miri gates the PR**; targeted core + FFI Miri clean locally. Specs: `crates/core/tests/protocol_branches.rs` (8), `client_branches.rs` (5), `crates/server/tests/branch_ops.rs` (9), FFI `client.rs` branch round-trip, Go/Python/wasm marshal tests. Local correctness review (medium) run, clean. → *Versioning and Branches; Unit 7b (diff query) now unblocked on this same client-wire-query approach.*

## 2026-07-14 · Migration type-scope applicability filter / #274 · a field step narrows to its declared type via an id→type projection at both seams; server-side, no persisted create-stamps
**Changed:** realizes the ARCHITECTURE §Schema-Migration end-state — a field rewrite applies to *its declared type's* elements, not every same-named slot — resolving the design gate the human unblocked 2026-07-14 (the #273 element-context projection supplies the id→declared-type resolution the fan-out seam lacked). Corrects §Schema-Migration's implicit field-name-uniqueness invariant: a `renameField`/`removeField`/`addField` step is now scoped to the elements of its `ty`, so a rename of `title` on `Note` no longer touches a `title` on `Task`. **Server-only but for one additive core seam** (`Document::migrate_leaf_slots_scoped`); reuses core `migration`/`schema`/`validate` public APIs.
- **The narrowing lives at the server seam; core's `Step::rewrite_*` stays the schema-free key-based primitive.** The field step's `ty` was carried on `Step` but discarded by the key-based `rename_key`/`drop_on_key`, so the rewrite hit any slot of that name across every type. The fix does **not** make core type-aware: `index::element_types(doc, schema)` (server) projects the room document to `element id → declared type name` by the same root-down, position-keyed descent `core::validate::check` walks (a map slot's child is the type its key names in the parent's allowlist; a list item is the declared item type) — the mirror of `element_zone`, layered on the #273 `element_paths` projection. The fan-out (`registry.rs`) and catch-up delta (`session.rs`) resolve each op's owning type via `op.target` (an op's owning element is the map holding its slot, invariant across the chain since a rewrite only re-keys or drops) and gate each field step in `Chain::translate_ops_scoped`: a field step whose `ty` mismatches the owning type is **inert** for that op; a type step is always inert per-op (an op never names a type). This keeps the pure per-op rewrite (Unit 7c) schema-free — the fan-out consumer supplies the type context, the transform does not resolve it.
- **The `None`/unresolved owning type falls back to the key-based rewrite — the field-name-unique common case is unregressed.** A relay op, a room with no bound schema, or an owning element the projection cannot type (a since-deleted/tombstoned map, or one whose runtime kind mismatches its declared type) resolves to `None` and every step applies by key, byte-for-byte the pre-#274 behavior. So the narrowing only ever *removes* wrong cross-type rewrites; it never drops or mis-keys an op it previously handled.
- **Both seams narrow over the same tree with the same schema, so op-served and snapshot-served joiners converge byte-identically.** The snapshot seam needed the owning-map identity per slot, so the one core change is additive: `Document::migrate_leaf_slots_scoped(fate: Fn(ElementId, &[u8]))` threads the owning map id (the op's `target` analogue) to the fate closure; the pre-existing `migrate_leaf_slots` delegates with `|_, key| fate(key)`, so every existing caller and core test is untouched. `translate_snapshot_scoped` resolves types over the **decoded snapshot tree** with the room's governing schema — the same tree and schema the op seam projects (a full catch-up snapshot *is* the head state), so the two agree element-by-element, including agreeing to fall back for an unresolvable element. A local review agent flagged a possible live-fan-out-vs-catch-up schema asymmetry (governing vs recipient schema); **refuted** — for a bound room the `acting_schema` passed to `session::step` is `parsed_schema(governing (app, version))`, the identical governing schema `registry.rs` types with, and translation runs only for bound rooms. Verified: the down-fold's `.expect` on `rewrite_down` stays safe (a down chain is built only when reachable ⇒ every step additive ⇒ inverts), and `translate_op_scoped(op, None)` is provably identical to the removed `rewrite_up_along`/`rewrite_down_along` composition.
- **Scope held to the type-scope filter; two residual gaps deferred, both convergence-safe.** A field step whose edge precedes a `renameType` (owning type resolves to the head name, the step carries the old name) and a container created under a since-renamed field key (the create is carried verbatim at its old key, so the descent does not reach its subtree) both fall back to key-based — the narrowing is defeated there, but **both seams do so identically, so convergence is preserved**; they are accuracy gaps, not divergences. These belong to the deferred **faithful container-field migration** slice (which additionally needs persisted per-slot create-stamps this filter did not require). Specs: `crates/server/tests/migration_type_scope.rs` (narrowing to type, no-schema key fallback, op/snapshot byte-identical parity, multi-edge chain composition, unresolvable-owner totality) + core `state_project.rs` scoped-fate regression; targeted + full-local Miri clean. → *Schema-Migration — Unit 8 type-scope filter; faithful container-field remains the sole migration follow-on.*
## 2026-07-14 · Cluster Unit 7b / #272 · gossip failure detection — SWIM-style suspicion + incarnation refutation feeding 6a's liveness; the gossip signal and the relay-link signal are unioned, not merged
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Cluster-Discovery "gossip-based … failure detection" and closes the 7a residual (a gossip-learned member was optimistically live). The 7a member-set gossip becomes a full SWIM-style failure detector: each member's liveness (state + incarnation) rides the gossip frame, a silent node is suspected then declared dead cluster-wide, and a falsely-suspected node refutes itself. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (the discovery section already names gossip failure detection); records the frame shape, the suspicion/death thresholds, the incarnation merge rule, and the relay-vs-gossip liveness interaction. **This completes Cluster Unit 7 (gossip discovery) and — with Units 4/5/6/7 all landed — the entire distributed-cluster epic (§Horizontal-Scaling).**
- **The gossip frame carries liveness — a breaking tag-26 wire change (pre-release, no migration).** `Message::Gossip`'s member tuple widens from `(node_id, advertise_addr)` to `(node_id, advertise_addr, incarnation: u64, state)` where `state` is a `MemberState { Alive, Suspect, Dead }` encoded as a small tag byte (0/1/2). The additive-only 7a shape is broken freely — the tag-26 format is re-versioned in place, `protocol_gossip.rs` rewritten. `MemberState` derives `Ord` in least-to-most-suspicious declaration order, so `Dead > Suspect > Alive` is the merge tie-break for free. Decode stays total (a bad state tag → `ProtocolError::BadTag`, truncation/over-count/trailing → error, never a panic).
- **Detection reuses the gossip exchange — no separate detector socket, no indirect probing.** A *successful* gossip round with a peer is first-hand proof it is alive (`note_gossip_reachable` — resets its failed-probe count, restores `Alive`); a *failed* round (dial/handshake/reply-timeout) counts toward suspicion (`note_gossip_unreachable`). The escalation is failed-probe-count based, not wall-clock: `SUSPECT_AFTER_FAILURES = 3` consecutive failed rounds → `Alive→Suspect`, `DEAD_AFTER_FAILURES = 6` → `Suspect→Dead`. Count-based (not a timer) keeps the state machine deterministic and test-drivable without a mockable clock — the tests drive `note_gossip_unreachable`/`reachable` directly, and the async `gossip_loop` feeds them from each round's `gossip_exchange` result. **SWIM indirect probing (ping-req via k relays)** — the refinement that avoids a false-positive from one node's bad link — is deferred; the gap above the suspect threshold is the refutation window instead.
- **Incarnation is the SWIM refutation counter; the merge is incarnation-dominant then suspicion-dominant.** `merge_liveness` (the anti-entropy of liveness): for a member, a strictly higher incarnation always wins (adopting its state, clearing local suspicion — it is fresher); at equal incarnation the more-suspicious state wins (`Dead > Suspect > Alive`), so a failure disseminates rather than being masked by a stale `Alive`. **Refutation:** a node that receives gossip marking *itself* `Suspect`/`Dead` (or asserting anything about itself at an incarnation ≥ its own) bumps its incarnation above the received one and re-asserts `Alive` (`refute_if_stale`) — the correction outranks the stale suspicion everywhere it propagated, so a live node can never be stuck `Dead`. The merge is commutative/idempotent: two nodes that received the same updates in any order converge on the same `(incarnation, state)`.
- **The gossip signal and the 6a relay-link signal are UNIONED, not merged into one down-set.** This is the load-bearing interaction decision. 6a's `mark_node_down`/`mark_node_live` (renamed field `relay_down`) is a connection-local signal; the gossip `MemberState` is cluster-wide. A member is *live* iff **its relay link is up AND gossip has not declared it `Dead`** (`is_live` ANDs both). Keeping them separate means neither can mask the other: a gossip-`Alive` does not resurrect a relay-down node, and a relay reconnect does not resurrect a gossip-`Dead` node (only a gossip refutation does). This diverges from the task's literal "gossip-Alive → `mark_node_live`" phrasing on purpose — folding gossip into the relay down-set would let one signal clobber the other. A `Suspect` member is still `live` (routes optimistically) until it hardens to `Dead` — only `Dead` excludes from `effective_primary_for`, so failover fires on a confirmed death, and a refuted/recovered node reclaims its rooms. This feeds 6a's `effective_primary_for` unchanged — the promotion logic already elects the first `is_live` replica in HRW order.
- **Dead stays in the member set (marked down), not reaped.** A `Dead` member is excluded from leadership but remains in the placement set — permanent eviction/removal (which would reshuffle placement) is a deliberate follow-on, so a transient-then-refuted death doesn't churn every room's replica set. Deferred with it: SWIM indirect probing, and 7a's late-joiner replication-dial wiring (a member learned after boot now gets a real gossip liveness reading, but the existing nodes' replication *peer-connections* to it are still dialed from the static boot set — `spawn_peers` at boot).
- Core-touching (`protocol.rs`) → **CI Miri gates this PR**; the detection/merge/refutation logic is in-process + Miri-clean (`crates/core/tests/protocol_gossip.rs` 12 — every-state round-trip, bad-state-tag/truncation/over-count/trailing errors, distinct tags, suspicion ordering; `crates/server/tests/gossip.rs` 24 — suspect-then-dead escalation + failover, both-survivors-independent, success-clears-suspicion, refutation-restores + overrides-Dead, higher-incarnation-wins, equal-incarnation-Dead>Suspect>Alive, order-independent merge, cross-node dissemination without a dropped link, relay-vs-gossip union both directions, single-node inert; one loopback socket exchange `#[cfg_attr(miri, ignore)]`). Local review (medium) run.
- **This is the LAST cluster unit — the distributed-cluster epic is complete** (1 placement · 2 static membership · 3 routing · 4 replication · 5 majority-ACK · 6a/6b failover+fence · 7a/7b gossip discovery+detection). Remaining cluster work is all documented follow-on/refinement (indirect probing, member reaping, late-joiner replication-dial wiring), none blocking.

## 2026-07-14 · Server element-context index + Zones 1b-ii-b · cross-zone move refused at the op-submit gate, id→zone resolved from the room's document projection
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Zones' "cross-zone tree moves forbidden" (the move half of Unit 1b-ii, gated since 2026-07-08 on an op-apply-seam decision) and resolves the design gate the human pinned 2026-07-14 (the server needs to resolve an element id → its context — parent/type/zone — at the op seam, for cross-zone move enforcement + the downstream per-zone/migration consumers). Amends §Zones "forbidden at schema level" → "refused at the op-submit gate", and qualifies §Mixed-Version-Sync's "no state materialization" (the server already materializes one document per room; the element-context index is a lean *derived* projection over it, not a new replica). **Server-only — reuses core `zone`/`schema`/`op` public APIs; zero `crates/core/src` change.**
- **The design gate's premise was counterfactual, so the "index" is a derived projection, not a parallel structure.** The gate assumed the server keeps only an op-log + snapshot with no materialized `Document`. It does not: `Hub` already folds every op into a per-room `room.doc: Document` on the ingest path, and already projects it to id→`core::path` (`element_paths`, consumed by ACL read-redaction). So the "element-context index" is realized as a lean derived resolution *over that authoritative projection* — `index::element_paths(doc)` + `zone::zone_of` — not a separately-maintained mutable index. **Why not a hand-maintained incremental index (the literal ask):** to stay consistent it would have to replicate the document's full CRDT semantics — readiness buffering/drain, Kleppmann move refold, slot LWW, subtree deletes. A first cut that folded ops in arrival order drifted from the document on *every* one of those: it failed **open** on a buffered-then-drained insert (the mover absent from the index → a cross-zone move admitted), mis-resolved a concurrent move's lamport-loser, and leaked moved-then-deleted ghosts (three independent review agents converged on this). Deriving from the single authoritative tree is both leaner and drift-free. The human's ruling ("a lean derived index, NOT a full Document") is honored in substance — no *new* full replica is materialized; the index is the derived id→context view over the one that already exists.
- **A cross-zone move is not statically detectable, so it is caught by simulating the batch.** After a move the node renders well-placed under its new parent (established 2026-07-08), so there is no post-move tree property to flag. `Hub::batch_crosses_zone` instead applies the op batch to an **independent copy** of the room document (`decode_state(&encode_state())`) and flags any `XmlMove` whose mover's zone differs **before vs after**. Simulating (rather than a pre-move lookup of source/dest paths) resolves a destination created *in the same batch* and runs the real fold, so the verdict is exactly what the document will hold. A mover absent on one side — created or deleted within the batch — is **not** a crossing (no committed cross-zone edge; "absent" is kept distinct from "unzoned", a review-caught false-positive fix). Cost is O(document) per move-batch, consistent with the existing per-fan-out `element_paths` walk; an O(1) incremental index is a deferred optimization once enforcement is proven.
- **Refused at the op-submit gate, the recoverable-denial idiom.** The gate lives in `session.rs`, mirroring the doc-ACL write denial (4a): a crossing batch returns `OpsRejected{Forbidden}`, the author keeps its ops, and the op **never enters the log**, so every replica converges on its absence (a refused op is simply absent). Chosen over a fold-side silent drop in `TreeMoves` (which would thread `Schema` + id→zone into the deliberately schema-free pure-edges layer) and over emit-side self-refusal in `move_xml` (the client cannot be trusted to refuse its own write). **Gated to `main`:** enforcement resolves against the room's materialized document, which a branch's divergent tree is not part of, so branch-scoped move enforcement waits on the per-zone-stream work (Unit 2/3) that models branch/zone interaction.
- **Unblocks the downstream consumers, all resolving id→context over the same projection.** Per-zone lamport + envelope zone (Zones Unit 2), per-zone replication streams + zone-scoped subscribe/redaction (Unit 3), the migration type-scope applicability filter + faithful container-field migration (Unit 8) — each needs id→{path, zone, type}, which `element_paths` + `zone_of` now supply (type resolution layers on the same path). Specs: `tests/element_index.rs` (projection resolves a create/insert/move/delete + out-of-order buffered delivery), `tests/zone_move.rs` (same-zone allowed, cross/zoned↔unzoned/same-batch-dest refused, create-then-reorder + move-then-delete not refused, no-zones regression, session `Forbidden` + store-replay reopen). Targeted Miri clean; four local review agents (drove the pivot off the drift-prone incremental index and caught the absent-vs-unzoned false positive). → *Authorization/zones — the move half of 1b-ii, and the shared id→context foundation.*

## 2026-07-13 · Doc-ACL Slice 4c / #271 · grant/revoke SDK surface — a faithful 16-byte-id marshaller plus a separate `actor_key` derivation, not an auto-hashing grant
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Authorization "the `AclGrant`/`AclRevoke` … SDK" — the authoring surface completing the Doc-ACL epic (4a enforcement · 4b redaction · 4c authoring). No ARCHITECTURE end-state change; records the ABI marshalling shape and the actor-key layering the identity model forced. **SDK/FFI-only — the `AclGrant`/`AclRevoke` ops + the `Document::acl()` cursor already existed in core, so zero `crates/core/src` change (CI Miri `-p crdtsync-core` unaffected).**
- **AclGrant crosses the ABI as discriminants + byte-strings, matching the op codec's tags.** Subject `0` actor (16-byte id) / `1` group (name) / `2` authenticated / `3` anonymous / `4` anyone; grant `0` capability (`0` read / `1` write / `2` publish-awareness / `3` own) / `1` role (name); effect `0` allow / `1` deny; plus the opaque `path` bytes and the 16-byte `grantor`. These reuse the exact numbers `codec.rs` assigns, so the C enum and the wire tag never drift. The FFI doc grant returns `i32` (1 ok / -1 bad enum|null) and writes both the tuple's 16-byte id (`out_id`, the revoke handle) and the ops (`out_ops`); revoke returns 1 emitted / 0 inert (an id the replica does not hold) / -1 malformed. The client surface returns an Ops frame routed through `ClientSession::enqueue_ops` (acked/resent), writing `out_id` for the grant. Total at every entry — a bad handle/enum → -1|empty, never a panic (`catch_unwind` at the boundary).
- **Actor-key derivation is a *separate* `actor_key` call, not baked into `grant`.** The identity model (4a, #266) keys tuples by `actor_key = SHA-256(actor)[..16]` of the authenticated actor — so a tuple's `Actor` subject and its `grantor` must carry that 16-byte key, not the client's ephemeral per-device id, for the server to match a request. But the client holds its *variable-length* credential actor bytes (`ClientSession::actor()`), not the key. **Decision: `acl_grant` stays a faithful 16-byte-id marshaller** (consistent with every other id in the ABI — client id, mark id, blob id all cross as raw 16 bytes) **and the derivation is exposed as its own `crdtsync_actor_key(actor) -> 16 bytes`** (Python `actor_key`, Go `ActorKey`, wasm `actorKey`). An app builds a server-matching subject/grantor via `actor_key(client.actor())` — one derivation reused for the grantor, the subject, and any client-side match — rather than `grant` auto-hashing (which would prevent passing a pre-derived key and couple authoring to the identity function). This satisfies "the SDK applies the actor_key derivation the server enforces" by *providing* the canonical derivation, without making `grant` non-faithful.
- **The derivation is duplicated in Rust (ffi + wasm add `sha2`), not lifted into core.** `actor_key` is a server/identity concept (it lives in `crates/server/src/acl.rs`), not a core CRDT primitive, and the "zero core change" constraint holds it out of core; ffi/wasm are not dep-constrained (only `crdtsync-core` is), so each carries the two-line `SHA-256[..16]` itself and Python/Go delegate through the FFI — one algorithm, no core coupling. The derivation is a fixed public spec (SHA-256, never a process-seeded hash), so the independent copies agree and a persisted grant's embedded key re-matches after a restart.
- **wasm binds core directly, so its discriminant→enum mapping is independent of the FFI's** — a review agent flagged that only the Rust FFI tests decoded the emitted op, so a swapped code in wasm's own mapping would ship green. Closed by a wasm test that `decode_ops` the grant and asserts the exact subject/capability/effect (mirroring the FFI test), plus the actor-capability-allow round-trip through `actorKey`.
- **Server-only follow-ups unchanged:** the server still trusts the client-set `grantor` on an incoming grant op (grantor-forgery prevention, if added, is a 4a-side rewrite-on-submit, out of this SDK slice); a snapshot state-level read projection stays deferred (4b). Specs: FFI `ffi.rs`/`client.rs` (op-shape decode + convergence + revoke-tombstone + bad-input totality + actor-key determinism), wasm `web.rs`, Go `acl_test.go`, Python `test_acl.py`. Targeted FFI Miri clean; two review agents (added the wasm decode assertion + shaped the actor_key layering). → *Authorization — Doc-ACL epic complete.*

## 2026-07-13 · Cluster Unit 7a / #270 · gossip membership discovery — dynamic member-set convergence by additive anti-entropy; the member set becomes mutable behind a canonicalized-placement rebuild
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Cluster-Discovery "gossip-based … membership" — the member set was static config for the process lifetime (Unit 2); it is now dynamic, converged by gossip. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (the discovery section already names gossip); records the frame shape, the dynamic-membership mechanism, and the determinism-canonicalization the code forced.
- **Gossip frame = a plain member list, no incarnation/version yet** (`Message::Gossip { members: Vec<(node_id, advertise_addr)> }`, core `protocol.rs`, tag 26 — next free after ReplicaAck's 25). Anti-entropy for 7a is a **set union**, so a bare `(node_id, advertise_addr)` list is the minimal honest shape — the node id a peer places with, plus the address it dials to reach a newly-learned member. Incarnation numbers / version vectors are deliberately NOT added here: they earn their keep only with failure detection (a member must be able to *refute* a false-down claim by bumping its incarnation), which is 7b. Hand-rolled length-prefixed pair codec mirroring `Replicate`; decode stays total (truncation / over-count / trailing → `ProtocolError`, never a panic). Node-to-node — a client that sends one violates (`session.rs`), the core client rejects an inbound one.
- **The member set becomes mutable behind a canonicalized placement rebuild.** `Membership::add_member(node, addr)` is idempotent (a known member touches nothing — no placement churn on re-gossip) and, on a genuinely new member, rebuilds the HRW `Cluster` from the **canonicalized (sorted, de-duped) set** — the same `Cluster::new` canonicalization Unit 1 already did. This is the load-bearing determinism decision: two nodes that have learned the same members compute **byte-identical** `primary_for`/`replicas_for` regardless of the order they learned them in, so placement converges as the set converges. `known_members()` returns the `(node, addr)` payload; each member's advertise address is tracked (a peer derived from its address maps to that address; `self` maps to its configured advertise address). Every existing accessor keeps its semantics; single-node / full-static-config paths are unchanged (a node given the full peer list already has everyone — gossip just re-confirms).
- **Anti-entropy is purely additive for 7a — no member ever leaves.** Push-pull: each round a node picks a random known peer, both sides union the other's set (`crates/server/src/gossip.rs`), so a node that booted knowing only a seed converges within a few rounds. Removal (a member leaving, or being evicted after a failure) is **7b** — a member's *liveness* meanwhile still rides on the 6a replication relay link, which already skips a down member when electing a room's effective leader, so additive-only membership does not strand traffic at a dead node in the interim.
- **Transport reuses the WS relay peer path** (the Unit-4 decision), not a second listener: the gossip task dials a peer with an empty-`app_id` Hello (a relay), sends its set, and reads the peer's set back — the same relay seam replication dials over. It is spawned behind the **same cluster-enabled gate as replication** (`ServeConfig.membership` is `Some`) — a single-node deployment starts no gossip task and is byte-identical to today. Peer choice draws from system entropy at the transport edge, kept out of the deterministic membership logic (the union/placement functions are socket-free and deterministic, driven directly in the convergence tests so nothing flakes on wall-clock randomness).
- **Residuals → the failure-detection follow-on (documented, not shipped half-done):** (1) **Replication + liveness peer-connections are still dialed from the static boot set** (`spawn_peers`, `dispatch_replication` route only to `peer_conns` frozen at boot). 7a converges the *member set / placement view* every node computes — a dynamically-joined node's own routing/redirect view is correct — but the existing nodes' *replication delivery* to a member learned after boot (and the 6a relay-link liveness reading of it) is not wired until that follow-on; a gossip-learned member is optimistically live until then. Majority-ack still commits via the reachable followers, so this degrades redundancy for a fresh joiner, not liveness of writes. (2) **A node's gossip identity is its `self_id`**, so a cluster must reference each node under the same identity it uses for itself (its `CRDTSYNC_NODE_ID` if set, else its advertise address — the `NodeId::from_addr` derivation). A node given a `node_id` that differs from how peers seed it is a **pre-existing Unit-2 identity inconsistency** (placement already diverged there before any gossip), out of 7a scope — gossip advertises self consistently under `self_id`, adding no new addr-level divergence (the self-advertise-addr override an earlier revision had was dropped: in this cluster the dial address of any member *is* its `NodeId`, as `spawn_peers`/redirect already assume). (3) A **malformed gossip pair** (an empty node id) is dropped at the union (`add_members`), so one bad frame cannot inject an undialable phantom; a broader inter-node trust model (auth on the relay seam, a member-set growth cap) is the same cluster-wide concern the unauthenticated `Replicate`/`ReplicaAck` seam already carries, unchanged here.
- Core-touching (`protocol.rs`) → **CI Miri gates this PR**; the union/placement logic is in-process + Miri-clean (`crates/core/tests/protocol_gossip.rs` 8, `crates/server/tests/gossip.rs` 12 incl. one loopback socket exchange `#[cfg_attr(miri, ignore)]`). Local review (medium, 3 finder angles) drove the identity-divergence, empty-id poisoning, and missed-tick-burst findings above; the rest (relay-handshake dup with `connect_peer`, dial-per-round, static-boot peer-conns) were evaluated as intentional first-cut scope + documented residuals.
- **Next: Unit 7b — failure-detection gossip** (suspicion / incarnation → `mark_node_down`, refutation via an incarnation bump, feeding the 6a `effective_primary_for`). The last cluster unit; the incarnation number the 7a frame omits rides in with it.
## 2026-07-13 · Cluster Unit 6b / #PR · epoch/term split-brain fence — a monotone per-room leadership epoch (= Raft term); promotion bumps, lower-epoch fenced, no-resurrection is the guarantee
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Horizontal-Scaling "election failover" — closes the un-fenced-recovery split-brain gap the Unit 6a log deferred. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change; records the fence mechanism + the reconciliation scope the code forced.
- **The epoch IS Raft's term, and is named/shaped to stay one.** A per-room, monotone `epoch: u64` identifies the current leadership generation. `RoomLog.head` is already the log index; HRW-next-live (6a) is the deterministic selection; this epoch is the term. A future Raft swap reuses it as-is — the fence is the term-comparison half of Raft's leader safety, without RequestVote yet.
- **On the wire: `epoch` added to `Message::Replicate`** (core `protocol.rs`, after `base_seq`, before the remainder-consuming op batch). **Pre-release wire break, no shim** — the Unit-4 log anticipated exactly this ("fencing lands with Unit 6, breaking the wire then"). `ReplicaAck` gains no epoch: the recovered stale leader learns the higher epoch by *receiving* the new leader's stream (it is a follower once demoted), not from an ack, so no ack-side term was needed.
- **A promotion BUMPS the epoch; a stable leader keeps one.** State lives in a mutable sibling of the (pure-placement) `Membership`: `LeadershipEpochs` (`crates/server/src/leadership.rs`) holds, per room, the highest epoch *seen* and the epoch this node currently *leads* at. On originating replication a node claims leadership at `max(seen)+1` on a fresh generation, or keeps its epoch if already leading at `>= seen` — so a steady leader's frames all carry one term (regression-locked) and only a promotion (or a recovered primary re-leading) bumps it. Leadership-epoch state is separate from `Membership` so the placement view stays a pure function of the member set.
- **A follower fences a frame whose `epoch` < the highest it has seen** (`Registry::apply_replicate`): dropped, not applied, not acked — a demoted-then-recovered stale primary cannot replicate a write it missed, and its ops cannot resurrect. The connection is *kept* (return `true`, not a violation-drop): the stale leader is a legit peer that will step down when it in turn observes the higher epoch. **A frame at a strictly higher epoch supersedes this node's own leadership** even as the placement primary — it steps down and converges on the new leader's stream (the recovered-primary reconciliation). Step-down is deferred until the frame is *committed to* (past the owns/branch checks), so a frame the node rejects never churns its leadership epoch (caught in local review — regression-locked by `a_rejected_frame_does_not_churn_a_leaders_epoch`).
- **Reconciliation scope: no-resurrection is the guarantee; op-set CRDT merge makes tail-truncation unnecessary.** The must-have — a fenced lower-epoch op stays out and never resurrects — is delivered and tested (`a_follower_converges_on_the_new_leader_and_a_fenced_op_stays_out`). Full Raft-style log truncation of a follower's divergent uncommitted tail is deliberately NOT implemented and is not needed here: the replication log is an **op-set** whose concurrent ops converge by construction (the CRDT merge law), so a legitimately-applied tail op is not a divergence to roll back — only a *fenced* (rejected) op could wrongly re-enter, and the fence closes exactly that. So there is no half-working reconciliation shipped; the guarantee is complete for the op-set model.
- **Residual → a 6c/gossip follow-on (documented, not shipped half-done):** (1) **epoch state is in-memory**, like 6a's liveness set and the replication watermarks — a *single* node restarting while its followers stay up returns with `seen=0`, re-leads at epoch 1, and is fenced by followers who remember the higher epoch, until it re-observes the room's epoch from the live leader's stream; persisting/gossiping the per-room epoch is a follow-on. (2) **Epoch-aware routing** — a follower that has seen a higher epoch still redirects by liveness (`effective_primary_for`), which covers the common down-primary case; redirecting to the higher-epoch leader *after* a stale primary recovers needs an epoch→leader-identity map (the apply path has only the peer `ConnId`), deferred. The must-have fence + no-resurrection is independent of both.
- **Single-node + steady-state all-live unchanged** — the epoch machinery is inert with no membership and until a room's leadership first changes; byte-identical beyond the constant epoch on the wire (regression-locked). Core-touching (`protocol.rs`) → **CI Miri gates this PR**; the fence/step-down logic is in-process + Miri-clean (`epoch_fence.rs` 10, `failover.rs`/`replication.rs` regressions, `protocol_replicate.rs` codec incl. epoch round-trip/truncation). Local review (high) caught the rejected-frame epoch-churn (fixed + regression-tested).
- **Next: Unit 7 — gossip discovery** (dynamic membership + failure detection — the last cluster unit; builds on the 6a liveness signal). The election gate stays resolved; no further human ruling.
## 2026-07-13 · Doc-ACL Slice 4b / #PR · outbound per-recipient op redaction — per-path read composed at the op's document path, redact-then-translate, catch-up included
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Wire-Level Redaction ("Server never sends unauthorized data … per-recipient filtering on every op send") + §Enforcement Points "op outbound (per recipient)" for the doc-ACL read tier. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change — this logs how the outbound half wires onto the 4a inbound tier and the composition choice the read path forced.
- **The redaction unit is the op's document path.** 4a evaluated the doc-ACL tier at the **root** only (the op-submit gate carries no path). At fan-out the server *has* the ops, so each op is resolved to a `core::path` and the recipient's **Read** verdict is composed at that path: an op is delivered iff `acl::recipient_reads_path` = `authorized(deployment, doc_acl_read_at(op_path), schema, id, Read, Room)` holds. The creator owns `/` (reads every path); a subtree read grant covers its subtree by `governs` (prefix); an ungoverned-and-ungranted path denies by default. So a write to `/a` reaches a `/a`-reader and is withheld from a `/b`-reader, from the same batch.
- **Op → path without touching core.** `Hub::element_paths(room)` walks the room's live `Document` (public `Map`/`List`/`XmlElement` accessors, `Element::is_container`/`id`) into an `ElementId → key-path` index covering **every** container: a map keys its children, and a non-map container's node-addressed descendants (list items, an XML element's attrs map / children list / nested elements) inherit that container's own path, since read authority governs a whole subtree. `acl::op_read_path` maps an op through it — a keyed op = target map's path + slot key, an id-addressed op = the target container's path, a doc-level ACL/Ranged op = root. The **root id is a fixed constant** and nested ids derive convergently, so the index built from the hub's replica matches every op's `target`.
- **An unresolved target resolves to root, not withheld.** An op whose target the index cannot resolve (a since-deleted container, a composite annotation payload the walk does not enter) resolves to the **root path** — the *strictest* read authority (governs no narrower than `/`). This never leaks (a subtree-scoped reader cannot read root), yet a whole-document reader — the creator, a root grantee — still receives it and **stays convergent**. Withholding it instead (the first draft) diverged an *authorized* whole-document reader's replica on any container the walk missed; root-resolution is the leak-safe convergent floor. (Composite RangedElement payloads are whole-document-scoped anyway, so root is their correct authority.)
- **Redact-then-translate, not translate-then-redact.** Migration translation (`Chain::translate_ops`) can **drop or rekey** ops, so redacting the *translated* batch would desync the path lookup. Redaction runs on the **authored** ops (path resolved from the original target), then the surviving subset is translated per recipient. This costs the per-target translation memo on ACL'd rooms (the subset differs per recipient) — accepted on the slow path; a **room with no ACL tuples keeps the pre-4b memoized fan-out byte-for-byte** (records-empty fast path: no walk, no per-op check), which is the common case and regression-locked.
- **Catch-up: op delta redacted; snapshot refused to any non-whole-document reader.** A fresh subscriber's `Catchup::Ops` delta is filtered by the *same* per-path read authority (so subscribe-catchup and live fan-out agree), and a partial reader replays only its granted subtrees — including withholding the room's bootstrap writes and the ACL grant ops themselves (an ACL op resolves to root, which a non-owner cannot read). A compacted room's `Catchup::Snapshot` is the whole materialized replica and **cannot** be path-redacted with an op filter (that needs the state-level cold-start projection, deferred — same seam the migration snapshot translation #190 uses); so a reader that does not read the **whole** document is refused it. Crucially the gate is `acl::reads_whole_document`, **not** a root-read check: root read is necessary but not sufficient, because a downstream `Deny(Read)` carves a subtree out of an otherwise whole-document grant (the AWS-style deny the model supports) yet does not `govern` the root query — so `reads_whole_document` re-checks read at every governing tuple path and treats a reader denied at any of them as partial. A deployment read-*allow* is terminal (whole room, no doc-ACL carve-out reaches it), and a whole-document reader (and every reader of a no-ACL room) is served as before. This closes a leak the widened subscribe gate would otherwise open: before 4b a subtree reader abstained at root and could not subscribe at all, so it never reached a snapshot.
- **The subscribe read gate widens to admit a subtree reader — but a deployment deny stays terminal.** Composing read at the *root* would refuse a reader granted only a subtree (it abstains at `/`), so it could never subscribe to receive the ops the fan-out would serve it. The gate admits a connection that holds whole-document read (`recipient_reads_path` at root — the creator, a root grant, or a deployment/schema room-read allow) **or**, *only where the deployment tier itself abstains*, holds read on any subtree (`acl::has_any_read_grant`). Gating the subtree fallback on deployment-abstain keeps a **deployment read-deny terminal** — a doc-ACL subtree grant never re-opens a subscription the deployment refused (the same "deployment deny is terminal" invariant 4a established for writes). A deployment that abstains on read for non-owners lets the doc-ACL tier drive per-path reads (a deployment Read *allow* is terminal and short-circuits redaction — a deployment grants **room access**, doc-ACL grants **per-subtree visibility**).
- **Awareness fan-out is unchanged.** Presence has no path, so it stays on the room-level `peer_may_read` gate (#252); per-zone/branch awareness scoping remains behind the Zones seam. This slice is op redaction only.
- **Server-only diff** (`crates/server/src/{acl,lib,registry,session}.rs`; confirmed **zero `crates/core/src`** → CI Miri `-p crdtsync-core` unaffected); spec `tests/acl_redaction.rs` (9, Miri-clean: per-recipient subtree redaction, creator-reads-all, no-ACL byte-identical regression, catch-up partial replay, two-devices-one-redaction, nested-XML reaches a subtree reader, deployment-deny-not-reopened, partial-reader-snapshot-refused, deny-carve-out-snapshot-refused). **Deferred:** snapshot *state-level projection* (a compacted-room snapshot is *refused* to a non-whole-document reader, not yet path-redacted); awareness per-path scoping; 4c the grant/revoke SDK surface. → *Authorization*.

## 2026-07-13 · Doc-ACL Slice 4a / #PR · doc-ACL identity = the authenticated actor; server bridges it to core's fixed-width key rather than re-keying core
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Authorization "Doc-level ACL-as-CRDT" — the server enforcement wiring of the doc-ACL tuple tier — and **resolves the long-standing ACL identity-model gate** (KANBAN Slice 4, "DESIGN-GATED on the ACL identity model"). No ARCHITECTURE end-state change: §Ownership already reads actor-space ("an owner grants a role to an **actor** or group"). This logs the resolution + the representation choice implementation forced.
- **The gate's resolution (human ruling): the ACL principal is the authenticated actor**, the server's credential-derived `Identity.actor` (`auth.rs`) — **not** the ephemeral per-device `ClientId`. Creator-owns, grant subjects, and grantors are all actor-keyed, so one human across two devices is one ACL subject (per-user branches/undo/audit follow). A regression test (`two_devices_of_the_same_actor_share_one_grant`) locks it: two connections, distinct client ids, distinct credentials, same actor → one grant governs both.
- **Representation: bridge, not re-key.** Core's slice-1 doc-ACL is `ClientId`-keyed (`AclSubject::Actor(ClientId)`, `AclActor.id`, `creator`, `grantor` — a 16-byte fixed-width key). The actor is `Vec<u8>` (variable length). Rather than re-key core (the principled alternative — but it would rewrite the 3 200-line core ACL evaluator + its five Miri-gated test suites + the op/codec/state format, a change disproportionate to a *server-wiring* slice, and its own core slice), the **server derives a stable 16-byte actor key** — `acl::actor_key(actor) = SHA-256(actor)[..16]` — and feeds *that* to core as the actor id / creator / grantor. Core's `AclActor.id` was always documented as an opaque match key the *caller* supplies (core "hosts no identity provider"); the key is now a derived-actor token, no longer a device id. **This keeps the change server-only** (no `crates/core/src` touch → CI Miri, which runs `-p crdtsync-core` only, is unaffected).
  - **Trade-off (the reason re-key is the principled path):** the derivation is a hash, so it has a (cryptographically negligible, 128-bit) collision space, and the key is opaque — a stored tuple's `Actor(ClientId)` no longer reads back as the human's actor bytes without the reverse map. Accepted for 4a; a later core re-key to a native actor byte-identity remains open if the opacity bites (grant/revoke SDK, audit rendering). The derivation is **fixed SHA-256, never a process-seeded hash**, so a persisted grant's embedded key re-matches after a restart / across a Rust upgrade.
- **The tier slots into `acl::authorized` between deployment and schema.** `authorized` gained a pre-resolved `doc_acl: Decision` param; the composition is deployment (`Allow`/`Deny` terminal) → doc-ACL → schema `@auth` → default-deny. A deployment deny is still terminal — **a doc-ACL grant cannot re-open what the deployment refused**. `doc_acl_tier` maps the data-plane `Action` to a core `Capability`, builds the `AclActor` from the `Identity` (actor key + groups + roles + `!anon:`-prefix authenticated flag), and runs `decide_capability_with_authority` at the **root path** (whole-doc `/` first cut; a path-carrying `Resource` widens it later).
- **First cut wires the op-submit *Write* path only; read stays as-is.** Consumed at the Ops Write authz; Subscribe-**read**, awareness-publish, version mutations, and the per-recipient fan-out gate all pass `Abstain`, so they decide exactly as the deployment+schema tiers did before. Wiring read is deliberately held for **4b** so that subscribe-read and the fan-out redaction gate (`peer_may_read`) land *together* — gating subscribe-read here without the fan-out gate would let an already-subscribed peer keep receiving ops after a doc-ACL read-deny (a half-enforced read). Holding read out of 4a also avoids creator-auto-owns silently *broadening* an existing schema-governed room's creator read (creator-owns beats the schema tier by design, so wiring it onto read would override a schema read-restriction for the first writer) — that widening is a 4b design point, not a slice-4a side effect.
- **`Room.creator` = the first *authenticated* writer, set-once, durable.** The first authenticated actor to write a room (main-log ops path) becomes its creator — the authority root that auto-owns `/`. An **anonymous** writer never becomes creator (`acl::is_authenticated`, the `anon:`-prefix test): an anon id is ephemeral per-connection, so it could never re-present to exercise the ownership, and set-once would wedge the room's authority on a dead principal. The tier is evaluated *before* the creator is set, so a first write to a fresh room finds no creator and no tuples → the tier abstains and the deployment/schema tiers bootstrap it; that authorized first writer is then recorded. Persisted in `RoomMeta` (a new `creator: Option<Vec<u8>>` field beside the governing binding + op-version high-water) and restored on load, so creator-auto-owns survives a restart.
- **Creator durability is best-effort but, unlike the rest of `RoomMeta`, *not* re-derivable.** The governing binding + op-version high-water rebuild from live subscribers / the op log; the creator cannot (the log carries per-device `ClientId`s, not the credential actor). So a persist failure of the creator record is a genuine (rare, I/O-error-only) loss — a later authenticated writer would then bootstrap the authority root instead. Accepted for 4a (the establishing write persists it eagerly, keeping the window to that one failed `write_meta`); a stronger guarantee (fail the establishing write if its creator can't be persisted) is a follow-on if it bites. Metadata format extended freely (pre-release, no migration shim; a pre-4a meta record simply re-derives its other fields).
- **Server-only diff** (`crates/server/src/{acl,session,lib,store,registry}.rs`); spec `tests/acl_enforcement.rs` (11: pure evaluator wiring — creator-owns, no-creator abstain, explicit grant + deny-overrides, group match, anonymous-vs-authenticated, two-identities-one-principal, register-schema abstain; + end-to-end through the Registry — creator bootstrap + grant, deny-overrides, two-devices, ungranted-stranger regression) + `tests/persistence.rs` creator-durability round-trip. **Deferred:** 4b outbound per-recipient redaction (redacting a fan-out a recipient may not read), 4c the grant/revoke SDK surface. → *Authorization*.

## 2026-07-13 · Cluster Unit 6a / #267 · leader failover — election gate RESOLVED (HRW-next + epoch fence, evolvable to Raft); 6a ships liveness-promotion; connection-liveness signal; un-fenced-recovery gap deferred to 6b
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Horizontal-Scaling "election failover". **The Unit-6 election gate is resolved** (human ruling), superseding the "confirmed HUMAN DESIGN GATE" of the Unit 4/5 logs: no ARCHITECTURE end-state change — §Horizontal-Scaling already names election failover; this records the *mechanism* chosen and the first slice built.
- **Election = HRW-next-in-line + epoch fence, structured to evolve into Raft.** The epoch/term becomes Raft's term; `RoomLog.head` is already the log index; HRW-next is a deterministic leader selection that later swaps for a RequestVote quorum. Chosen over adopting full Raft now (the static cluster + deterministic HRW placement already give a canonical leader order for free, so the cheap first cut is "promote the next live replica", with the epoch/term added as the fence — a forward-compatible path to Raft rather than a throwaway).
- **6a ships the liveness-promotion half only.** Leadership tracks reachability, not just placement. `Membership` gains a per-node liveness view (`down: HashSet<NodeId>`, `self` always live) and `effective_primary_for(room)` = the first LIVE replica in `replicas_for` (HRW) order. **Byte-identical to `primary_for` while every replica is up** (empty `down` ⇒ effective == placement) — the placement primary is promoted-past only when it is down. The leadership decision points route on effective leadership — the redirect target (`session.rs`), the replication-origination gate and the follower apply gate (`registry.rs`); `primary_for`/`is_primary_for` stay where *placement* (not leadership) is meant, and `replicas_for`/`quorum` still count the placement replica set (the *set* is unchanged on failover — only *which member leads within it* shifts).
- **Liveness signal = the Unit-4 inter-node relay CONNECTION state**, not a new heartbeat frame. A peer whose relay link is connected is UP; one whose link dropped or fails to dial is DOWN — the `runtime.rs` peer task reports it as `Cmd::PeerLive { node, live }` → `Registry::set_peer_liveness` → `Membership::mark_node_live/down`. Connection-liveness chosen over inferring liveness from room-op recency because it works for **idle rooms with no traffic** and needs **no new wire frame** (a heartbeat frame is Unit 6b if a finer detector is wanted). Peers default **optimistically live** (empty `down`), so a fresh cluster's startup transient does not false-promote before the relay links establish; a node marks a peer down only on an *observed* dial failure or link drop.
- **A non-owner that sees every replica down redirects at the placement primary, never serves.** `effective_primary_for` returns `None` when no replica of the room is live; the redirect falls back to `primary_for` so a node that does not hold the room points the client at the (dead) placement primary — correct retry backpressure — rather than serving orphaned writes it would never replicate. (A node that *does* hold the room is itself always-live, so it leads rather than hitting the `None` fallback.)
- **No split-brain fence yet — the accepted 6a gap, closed by Unit 6b.** Leadership is un-fenced: a recovered stale primary immediately reclaims its rooms with no epoch check, so it could serve a write it missed while down; and a noisy single-link liveness signal can transiently false-promote a follower whose *outbound* link to a live primary blips, dropping that primary's best-effort `Replicate` frames (incremental replication, no retransmit ⇒ possible op loss on the false leader). Both are the split-brain window **Unit 6b** closes with an epoch/term field on the `Replicate` frame (fences a stale primary) + log reconciliation on takeover — the same shape the Unit-4 log anticipated ("fencing lands with Unit 6, breaking the wire then"). Deferring it matches the majority-ack unit shipping with its documented static-membership gap.
- **Server-only, no wire change** — all in `crates/server/src/{membership,registry,runtime,session}.rs`; no `crates/core/src` touch (the epoch field is 6b), so CI miri is non-required/unaffected. Tests (`crates/server/tests/failover.rs`, 12) use in-process injected liveness so they run under Miri (targeted server Miri clean); single-node + steady-state all-live regressions lock byte-identical behavior. Local review (high) surfaced the non-owner-all-down serve hazard (fixed + regression-tested) and confirmed the transient-blip op-loss as the acknowledged 6b fencing gap.
- **Next: Unit 6b** (epoch/term split-brain fencing + log reconciliation on takeover — core-touching: an epoch field on `Replicate` + `Membership`), then **Unit 7** (gossip discovery, which builds on the failure-detection/liveness signal 6a established). The election gate being resolved, both are cs-implement-buildable with no further human ruling.

## 2026-07-13 · Binary Blobs Slice 4 / #265 · SDK blob surface — framing, the None signal, and boundary entropy
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Binary Blobs — the SDK blob CRDT surface forwarding the three core functions (`set_blob` #262, `set_blob_ref` #264, `get_blob`) across FFI/Python/Go/wasm. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change; records the marshalling/framing choices, since none is dictated by the core signatures.
- **`BlobRef` wire framing (the FFI `get_blob` buffer).** id[16] · `u32`-LE mime_len + mime · `u64`-LE size · a `u8` present flag · (if present) `u32`-LE inline_len + inline bytes. The same length-prefixed little-endian shape the marks/diff buffers use, so the Python/Go decoders reuse their existing readers. A present flag (not a zero-length inline) distinguishes an empty-but-present inline from an absent one — though the producers never mint an empty inline, the framing keeps `Some(vec![])` and `None` distinct.
- **The doc-surface edits carry the `set_blob` `None` out-of-band, via `i32` + an out-param.** `crdtsync_doc_set_blob` returns `1` inlined / `0` over the inline ceiling (`None`) / `-1` bad handle, writing the ops into `out_ops` — the over-ceiling case must be distinguishable from a successful-but-inert edit (both would otherwise be empty ops). `set_blob_ref`/`get_blob` take the same `i32`+out-param shape for symmetry. Python maps `0`→`None`, Go→`(nil,false)`, wasm→`undefined`.
- **The client-surface edits return the Ops frame (mirror the xml client edits), and the `None` collapses into "enqueues no op".** Routed through `enqueue_ops` like every client edit, an over-ceiling `set_blob` yields empty ops → an empty-*ops* Ops frame with nothing added to the outbox — identical to any inert client edit (a bad path, a no-op delete). There is no separate over-ceiling signal on the client surface (reads/None-detection live on the doc surface); the docstrings say "enqueues no op", not "returns an empty frame", because the frame is a well-formed empty-ops message, not zero bytes. No client-surface `get_blob` — reads stay doc-surface, as the xml split does.
- **Inline-handle entropy is injected at the SDK boundary; the core stays getrandom-free.** `set_blob` mints the handle from `Host` entropy, so ffi and wasm add `getrandom` (the `js` feature for wasm's crypto RNG) behind a tiny `FfiHost`/`WasmHost`; `now_unix_millis` answers `0` because the blob path never reads the clock. Only crdtsync-core is dep-minimal — the bindings add mature crates freely.
- **The 16-byte id crosses the C ABI as a fixed-count pointer (no length), read as exactly 16 bytes** — mirroring `crdtsync_doc_new`'s client id. Embedded NUL bytes in a handle are safe because the C side never runs `strlen`; Python passes it as a `bytes` buffer (ctypes gives the raw pointer, not a truncated C string), Go takes a type-safe `[16]byte`.
- **wasm surfaces `size` as a JS `Number` (`f64`), not a `BigInt`** — mirroring the web `File.size` idiom. The `f64` mantissa is exact to 2^53 bytes (8 PiB), far beyond any real blob, so the ergonomic Number wins over BigInt; the FFI/Python/Go paths carry the full `u64` verbatim.
- **SDK/FFI-only, zero `crates/core/src` change** — the three path fns already exist. CI miri is core-only → non-required/unaffected; the FFI blob suites are Miri-clean locally (`getrandom` is shimmed under Miri). The byte-upload HTTP convenience helper (a thin `POST /blobs` client) and ACL-per-reference-site (the **human design gate**) are the only Binary-Blobs work left; the CRDT surface is complete through the SDK.

## 2026-07-13 · Binary Blobs Slice 3 / #264 · ref-only BlobRef producer — caller-supplied handle, no entropy, no size guard
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Binary Blobs — the large-blob half of the op producer, complementing the inline `set_blob` (Slice 2a #262). No ARCHITECTURE end-state change; records why the two producers split and what the ref-only path deliberately does not do.
- **`path::set_blob_ref(doc, path, id: [u8;16], mime, size) -> Vec<Op>`** sets a `Scalar::BlobRef { id, mime, size, inline: None }` via the same `emit(…, cur.set(key, …))` seam `set_blob` uses. The bytes live in the store (uploaded out of band via `POST /blobs`, #263), so the op carries only the handle.
- **No entropy, unlike `set_blob`.** The id is the caller-supplied handle the upload route already minted and returned — not freshly drawn from `Host` entropy. Minting a second id here would name a blob the store never stored. So the ref-only producer takes no `Host`; it is a pure function of its arguments.
- **No size guard, unlike `set_blob`.** `set_blob` rejects `> INLINE_MAX` because those bytes would ride the op; a ref carries no bytes, so it names a blob of any size and returns the ops unconditionally (never `Option`). The size is metadata the caller learned from the upload.
- **`get_blob` reads both producers unchanged.** It clones the `BlobRef` regardless of `inline`, so a ref-only ref round-trips (id/mime/size, `inline: None`) with no reader change — confirmed by test, no gap. Overwriting an inline slot with a ref (or the reverse) is an ordinary LWW scalar replace.
- **Pure core, no store/route touch.** All in `crates/core/src/path.rs` (+ `tests/blob_path.rs`); `BlobRef` reused unchanged. Pure in-core tests run under Miri (no fs/socket). ACL-per-reference-site remains the deferred **human design gate**; the SDK blob API (upload + these setters) is the next slice.

## 2026-07-13 · Binary Blobs Slice 2b / #263 · HTTP upload/fetch route — verifier-gated, own listener, put_fetchable persists every blob
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Binary Blobs — the over-the-wire byte channel over Slice-1's store (#259). No ARCHITECTURE end-state change; records the route surface, the auth gate chosen, the config seam, and the store method the route forced.
- **Route:** `POST /blobs` (axum `Bytes` body, `Content-Type` → the blob's mime, default `application/octet-stream`) → `BlobStore::put_fetchable` → `200 {"id":"<hex>","size":N,"inline":bool}`. `GET /blobs/{id}` parses the 32-char hex handle (malformed → `400`, never a panic) → `get` → the bytes as generic `application/octet-stream` (the store persists no mime, so octet-stream is the honest content type) or `404`. Upload body cap `MAX_BLOB_BODY` = 8 MiB → axum's `413`.
- **Auth = the verifier seam only, not a new signed-token model.** The route authenticates the `Authorization` credential through the *same* `Verifier` the data/admin planes use (missing/unknown → `401`), mirroring the schema-register gate. It deliberately does **not** run the `Authorizer`: a per-blob authorization needs a new `Action`/`Resource` variant, and both are matched exhaustively in `acl.rs` (`action_token`, `to_schema_action`, `ResourceMatch::matches`), so inventing a blob resource here would ripple a half-designed auth scope through the policy engine. ACL-per-reference-site is the deferred **gated** follow-on. (Revises the Slice-1 log's "signed-token HTTP route" wording: the credential seam already in place is the gate, no separate token issuer.)
- **`put_fetchable` — the route forced a second store entry point.** Slice-1 `put` returns a small blob (≤ `INLINE_MAX`) inline and never writes it, so `get(id)` would `404` a small handle. The HTTP fetch channel must round-trip *every* uploaded handle, so `put_fetchable` content-addresses and persists the bytes regardless of size while still reporting `inline` truthfully (a client may skip the fetch for a small blob it just uploaded). `put` stays for the later op-producer path, where inline bytes ride the ref.
- **Config + wiring: its own opt-in listener.** Served on `CRDTSYNC_BLOB_ADDR` (opt-in exactly like `CRDTSYNC_ADMIN_ADDR`), store root `CRDTSYNC_BLOB_ROOT` else `<CRDTSYNC_DATA_DIR>/blobs` else a clean startup error. `main` now boxes every plane's serve future into one `try_join_all` (data always, admin + blobs opt-in) rather than the prior nested data/admin `try_join!`.
- **Server-only, no `crates/core/src` change** — all in `admin.rs` + `blobs.rs` + wiring (`lib.rs`/`main.rs`) + `tests/blob_http.rs`; `BlobRef` in core reused unchanged, so CI miri is non-required/unaffected. The pure id-parse unit test runs under Miri; every socket-binding / fs-touching test carries `#[cfg_attr(miri, ignore)]`. Deferred hardening: a per-request/idle timeout on the blob plane (the admin plane's total-request timeout is the wrong tool for a legitimately-slow large upload).

## 2026-07-13 · Binary Blobs Slice 1 / #259 · content-addressable local-FS blob store — the bytes-at-rest layer
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Binary Blobs — the store half only (bytes at rest). No ARCHITECTURE end-state change; records the concrete on-disk shape and what is deliberately deferred.
- **Public UUID handle, internal sha256 address — independent by construction.** `BlobStore::put(bytes, mime)` mints a fresh random 16-byte UUID (system entropy, the `getrandom` idiom the anon-actor path already uses) as the `BlobRef.id`, and content-addresses the bytes by sha256 internally. The handle never encodes the hash, so holding a ref cannot probe whether the store already has the content. Identical bytes share one `objects/<sha256-hex>` file — natural dedup — under distinct public handles.
- **The inline threshold rides the ref, never the store.** A blob at or below 4096 bytes (`INLINE_MAX`) is returned as `BlobRef { inline: Some(bytes), .. }` and never touches the filesystem; a larger one is persisted with `inline: None` and fetched by id. `get(id)` therefore serves only stored (non-inline) blobs — inline ones live in the ref (#60) — and returns `None` for an unknown id, never a panic.
- **Durable across reopen, crash-consistent.** The UUID → sha256 map is persisted one file per handle under `refs/<uuid-hex>` (the 32-byte sha) and rebuilt into the in-memory index on `open`. Objects and refs are written with the same atomic tmp+rename+dir-fsync discipline as the durable op store, and the object is written before its ref, so a crash can only orphan an unreferenced object (harmless), never dangle a ref at a missing object. A corrupt/truncated ref surfaces as an error, not a panic.
- **Server-only, store layer only.** All of it is `crates/server/src/blobs.rs` + its test; `BlobRef` in core (#60) is reused unchanged, no `crates/core/src` change — so CI miri is non-required/unaffected. Pure sha/hex logic runs under Miri; fs-touching tests carry `#[cfg_attr(miri, ignore)]`. Two review agents cleared correctness (crash-ordering, the 4096 boundary, reopen, partial reads) and flagged only that hex/`unhex` duplicate the durable store's *private* helpers — kept a local copy, matching the codebase's settled per-module hex idiom (store.rs and runtime.rs each carry their own) rather than introducing a shared util module for one caller.
- **Deferred:** the op/wire ref producer, the signed-token HTTP upload/fetch route, and per-reference ACL are later Binary-Blobs slices; an S3 backend, dedup ref-counting / GC, and range requests are v0.5.

## 2026-07-13 · Cluster Unit 5 / #258 · majority-ACK durability — quorum = floor(R/2)+1 counting self; withhold the client ack, never a false-ack timeout
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Horizontal-Scaling "majority-ACK replication" — the durability half over Unit 4's leader→follower mirror. The leader now gates a client's write-ack on a quorum, reading the per-`(room, follower)` watermark Unit 4 built. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change; records the quorum math, the withhold mechanism, and what is deliberately deferred.
- **Quorum = majority of the replica set, self counted.** A room's replica set is `replicas_for(room)` = the primary (self) + followers, size R; a majority is `floor(R/2) + 1`. Self, having committed the write, is the implicit one — so the leader needs `floor(R/2)` **follower** acks at or past the write's server sequence (via `Replication::watermark`). R=3 → majority 2 → 1 follower; R=5 → majority 3 → 2 followers. Single-node (no membership) or a self-only replica set (R=1) is a majority of one, satisfied by self alone — the ack is immediate, **byte-identical to before the gate** (regression-tested).
- **Withhold the `Accepted`, release on the ack that meets quorum.** The leader's write path no longer queues `Accepted` straight to the author's outbox for a replicated main-stream write; it parks a `(room, seq, conn)` record in `Registry::pending_acks`. Each follower `ReplicaAck` (`record_replica_ack`) re-checks that room's withheld writes and releases every one the fresh watermark now carries to a majority (`Cmd::PeerAck` then flushes the outbox). A branch write (not mirrored yet), a no-op resend (nothing fresh to replicate), and the single-node / self-only case release at once.
- **A below-quorum write is never falsely acked — no timeout.** With no failure detection until Unit 7 gossip, a write a majority never acknowledges is correctly **never** acked: the honest first-cut limitation, not a timeout that acks a non-durable write anyway. A withheld ack whose author disconnects is dropped (`pending_acks` purged on `disconnect`), so a permanently-stalled room retains no orphaned records.
- **Gate rests on the from-start-follower sequence equality.** `hub.seq(room)` is a monotonic count across the room's whole history (`base_seq + log.len()`), stable under compaction, so a follower present from the start and fed every commit reaches the same sequence the leader does and its `through_seq` meets `write_seq` exactly. A **late** follower with no history (backfill is best-effort/deferred, Unit 4) legitimately never reaches the write's sequence, so its writes stay withheld — the same deferred backfill/reconciliation the epic already parks for a later unit, not a regression here.
- **Server-only.** Gating logic + tests live in `crates/server` (`registry.rs`, `runtime.rs`); the `Accepted` frame already exists, no `crates/core/src` change — so CI miri is non-required/unaffected. In-process quorum tests run under Miri; the two loopback end-to-end tests carry `#[cfg_attr(miri, ignore)]`. Two review agents cleared the majority math and flagged the `pending_acks`-on-disconnect leak (fixed + regression-tested) and a defensive drop-safe gate; the compaction/late-follower and no-failure-detection findings are the deferred-backfill/Unit-6-7 scope, matching spec.
- **Unit 6 (election / failover) remains a confirmed HUMAN DESIGN GATE**, and Unit 7 (gossip discovery) depends on the Unit 6 failure-detection ruling — neither is a buildable NEXT. The cluster frontier is human-gated at Unit 6.

## 2026-07-13 · Cluster Unit 4 / #257 · leader→follower op replication — reuse the WS relay transport; no epoch field; Unit 6 confirmed a human design gate
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Horizontal-Scaling "majority-ACK replication" — the leader→follower half. The leader mirrors a room's committed ops to its follower replicas, so a redirect (Unit 3) lands on a node that already holds the state. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change; records the concrete frame shape, transport reuse, and what is deliberately deferred.
- **Two node-to-node frames, not client frames.** `Message::Replicate { room, branch, ops, base_seq }` (core `protocol.rs`, tag 24 — reuses the op codec, so the wire and the durable log share one encoding) leader→follower; `Message::ReplicaAck { room, through_seq }` (tag 25) follower→leader. Both are **node-to-node** — the core client surfaces neither (no `take_*` drain) and the server `step` rejects a client-sent one as a `ProtocolViolation`, the same direction-guard pattern as `Redirect`. The actual peer processing is off the client-session path: `deliver` intercepts an inbound `Replicate` and applies it; the leader's outbound peer task consumes the `ReplicaAck`. Wire compat broken freely (pre-release, new tags).
- **Reuse the WS relay transport — no second listener/codec** (the transport question ARCHITECTURE left open). A node dials each other member over the **same WebSocket transport clients use**, as a relay connection: an empty-`app_id` `Hello` already resolves to `Resolution::Relay`, so the follower's existing inbound handler accepts the peer with no new accept path. The one piece missing was the **outbound dial** — a minimal per-member peer-connection task (`runtime.rs`) that dials, sends the replication frames the registry routes to it, reads the follower's acks back into the registry as `Cmd::PeerAck`, and redials on drop. Chosen over a dedicated intra-cluster listener/codec because the relay path already carries everything needed; a second transport would duplicate the framing, handshake, and accept loop for no gain.
- **Primary tracks a per-`(room, follower)` ack watermark, but nothing gates on it yet.** `crates/server/src/replication.rs`: the leader queues one `Replicate` per follower in `replicas_for(room)` minus self after a commit advances the room's head, and records the watermark each `ReplicaAck` reports. This is the state **Unit 5** (majority-ACK durability) reads to decide a write is safely replicated — Unit 4 builds the tracking; **client acks are not gated on it**. Replication is **best-effort**: a frame for a backed-up or unreachable follower is dropped, not retransmitted (backfill/reconciliation is Unit 5).
- **No epoch/term field.** `Replicate` reserves **no** speculative epoch/term for future fencing. Pre-release breaks compat freely — when Unit 6 (election) lands it will break the wire and add fencing then, so a placeholder now would be dead weight guessing at Unit 6's design.
- **`base_seq` carried, not yet consumed; replication is main-stream only.** `base_seq` (the leader's compaction floor) rides the frame so a future snapshot-based catch-up can align a late follower's sequence space; Unit 4 replicates the whole log from the first op, so a fresh follower's own head already equals the leader's and `through_seq` needs no adjustment. **Branch replication is out of scope** — a follower has no copy of the fork a branch diverges from (branch lifecycle is not mirrored), so a branch write is not replicated and a branch `Replicate` is dropped rather than misapplied.
- **Peer connections are unauthenticated in Unit 4 — a known, deferred trust boundary.** The relay peer path applies a `Replicate` gated only on `Membership` (this node holds the room as a follower), not on peer identity — there is no cluster-member authentication yet, so the reused relay transport cannot cryptographically distinguish a real peer from a client forging a `Replicate`.
