A follower does not serve replicated rooms to clients (Unit 3 redirects them), so the blast radius is a replica-local write, not client-visible divergence. **Peer authentication / fencing lands with Unit 6** (election/split-brain), which the epic's bottom-up order already places after replication; noted here so the boundary is auditable rather than silent.
- **Single-node ⇒ no replication (byte-identical regression).** Every replication path is gated on `Membership`: a node with no membership leads nothing, dials no peer, queues no frame, and behaves exactly as today — regression-tested. Core wire touched (`protocol.rs` + `client.rs`) — CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) gates; targeted Miri (`protocol_replicate`/`protocol_redirect`/`client`) clean. Socket-touching loopback tests carry `#[cfg_attr(miri, ignore)]`; the frame logic itself is covered by in-process two-node tests that run under Miri.
- **Unit 6 (election / failover) is a confirmed HUMAN DESIGN GATE.** The election mechanism (Raft vs a custom epoch-lease), split-brain fencing / epoch, failure-detection ordering against Unit 7 gossip, and log reconciliation on takeover are all **unspecified** in ARCHITECTURE §Horizontal-Scaling — directional, not designed. Do not cut Unit 6 without a human ruling. Unit 5 (majority-ACK durability) is the next ready unit.

## 2026-07-12 · Cluster Unit 3 / #256 · request routing — a non-leader redirects a room to its leader (leader = the placement primary, pre-election); redirect over proxy; client-surfaces-target / transport-reconnects
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Horizontal-Scaling "Leader Model" (line 793: "Clients can connect to any node; wrong node proxies or redirects to leader"). No ARCHITECTURE end-state change: the design offers **proxy OR redirect**, and this unit builds the redirect half; the proxy alternative is recorded as a deliberate follow-on (Unit 3b). This is where the held-but-unrouted placement view (Unit 2) first changes runtime behavior.
- **Redirect, not proxy — the simpler MVP.** A node that is **not** a room's leader answers a Subscribe (or a write / durable version mutation that reaches it) with `Message::Redirect { room, leader_addr }` instead of serving the room; the client reconnects to `leader_addr` and re-subscribes there. Redirect chosen over transparent proxy because it needs **no inter-node connection** — the node reads its own placement view and points the client at the leader, rather than opening a leader↔follower link and forwarding (which depends on the Unit 4 replication connection). Transparent proxy (the node forwards to the leader) is a deliberate follow-on, **Unit 3b**.
- **Leader = the placement primary, for now.** In the static cluster (Units 1–2) a room's leader is deterministically `Membership::primary_for(room)` — the HRW placement primary — with **no election yet**. Routing uses the primary as the leader; Unit 6 (election/failover) will later change *who* the leader is, and this routing then follows the elected leader rather than the raw placement primary. `!is_primary_for(room)` (equivalently: the primary is not self) is the redirect trigger.
- **The `Redirect` frame + direction guard.** `Message::Redirect { room: Vec<u8>, leader_addr: Vec<u8> }` on the core wire (`crates/core/src/protocol.rs`, tag 23) — length-framed room + advertise address, so either may be empty; decoding is total (truncation/trailing → `ProtocolError`, never a panic). Wire compat broken freely (pre-release, new tag). Direction: **server→client only** — the client `receive` accepts it, the server `step` rejects a client-sent one as a `ProtocolViolation`, mirroring the existing per-message direction guards.
- **Client surfaces the target; the transport reconnects — the split.** `ClientSession::receive(Redirect)` buffers `(room, leader_addr)` into a drainable `take_redirects()` (a `Redirect` value, not a `ClientError`), exactly the `onUpdateRequired`/`onOpsRejected` split: the **core client holds no socket, so it cannot reconnect itself** — it exposes the redirect target and the transport-owned layer does the actual socket reconnect. The **SDK reconnect wiring** (FFI + Python/Go/wasm draining `take_redirects` and reconnecting to `leader_addr`) is a follow-on SDK slice, not this unit.
- **Single-node ⇒ never redirects (byte-identical regression).** `step` gains `membership: Option<&Membership>`, threaded from the `Registry`'s held view. `None` (single-node, no peers) — or a solo membership, or a room this node *does* lead — serves the room exactly as before (subscribe/ingest/persist unchanged). Only a genuine non-leader redirects. A follower does **not** serve a room's ops/subscription/version-write directly in this MVP; **follower read-serving** (a follower answering reads without a redirect) is a later optimization, deferred. The redirect guard covers the durable write paths — Subscribe, an ops write, and version create/rename/delete — so a follower never diverges a room it does not lead; version *reads* (list/fetch) are unreachable on a follower (no channel binds) and left for the read-serving slice. Core wire touched (`protocol.rs` + `client.rs`) — CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) gates; targeted Miri (protocol/client suites) clean.

## 2026-07-12 · Cluster Unit 2 / #255 · static membership config (env, single-node default) + a `Membership` node-view over the Unit-1 placement; address→NodeId derivation; held-but-not-yet-routed
**Changed:** realizes the static-join half of ARCHITECTURE §Horizontal-Scaling "Cluster Discovery" (line 807: "static join via CLI flag, or gossip-based"). No ARCHITECTURE end-state change: the static-membership feed into placement is exactly the designed discovery half; gossip liveness stays Unit 7. Records that the config carrier is env vars (mirroring the existing `CRDTSYNC_*` seams), not a `--join` CLI flag.
- **Static membership from env, single-node the default.** `crates/server/src/main.rs`: `CRDTSYNC_CLUSTER_PEERS` (comma-separated advertise addresses) joins a cluster; self id from `CRDTSYNC_NODE_ID` (explicit) or `CRDTSYNC_ADVERTISE_ADDR` (derived); `CRDTSYNC_REPLICATION_FACTOR` overrides the per-room replica count (default 3, rejects 0). Mirrors the optional `CRDTSYNC_WEBHOOK_URL`/`CRDTSYNC_POLICY_FILE` pattern: **unset peers ⇒ single-node, no membership, every room served locally — zero behavior change.** A malformed peer list (blank entry), a blank/absent self id when peers are set, or a non-positive factor is a clean startup `io::Error`, never a panic.
- **`Membership` — the node's view over the shared placement.** `crates/server/src/membership.rs`: holds self `NodeId` + the canonical `{self} ∪ peers` member set and builds the Unit-1 `Cluster`. Exposes what routing (Unit 3) + replication (Unit 4) consult — `members`/`self_id`/`is_self`/`replicas_for`/`primary_for`/`owns` (self in the room's replica set) / `is_primary_for` (self is the room's leader). Every query is the shared `Cluster` placement evaluated for self's id, **never an independent computation** — so two nodes built from the same peer set (differing only in which member is self) compute the identical replica set for a room and each answers `owns`/`is_primary` correctly for its own id. This cross-node agreement is the load-bearing property (spec `crates/server/tests/membership.rs`, 17).
- **Address→NodeId derivation is deterministic + portable.** `NodeId::from_addr(addr)` = the trimmed advertise-address bytes, a pure function of the address. Every node configured with the same peer address string derives the identical id, so the cluster agrees on placement; trimming absorbs peer-list padding. Self's explicit `CRDTSYNC_NODE_ID` is likewise trimmed (and empty-as-absent), so a padded/blank env value can never diverge from a peer's derivation or slip through as a zero-length id.
- **Held, not yet routed.** Threaded onto `ServeConfig`/`Registry` as `Option<Membership>` (`None` = single-node) with a `set_membership`/`membership()` seam, exactly as the schema registry / webhook sink are threaded. This unit **holds + exposes** membership + placement; it does **not** change routing/subscription/replication — a single-node (no-peers) server behaves exactly as before. Runtime routing on the view is Unit 3, where placement first changes behavior. Server-only (no `crates/core/src`), no new dep — CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) unaffected.

## 2026-07-12 · Cluster Unit 1 / #254 · room→replica-set placement by rendezvous (HRW) hashing over a consistent-hashing ring; portable FNV-1a+SplitMix64 weight
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Horizontal-Scaling §Room-Based Sharding ("consistent hashing on `room_id` for deterministic placement, horizontal scaling, balanced distribution") as the pure placement function every later cluster layer (routing, replication, failover) consults. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change: §Room-Based Sharding names "consistent hashing on `room_id`" for the deterministic/balanced property; this unit records that the mechanism satisfying it is rendezvous (HRW) hashing, not a literal vnode ring.
- **Rendezvous (HRW / highest-random-weight) hashing, not a consistent-hashing ring.** `crates/server/src/placement.rs`: `Cluster::replicas(room_id, n)` scores every member for the room and returns the `n` highest-weight members, primary (leader-candidate) first; `Cluster::primary` is the top one; `NodeId` wraps an opaque node id/address. HRW chosen over a ring: no virtual-node ring to construct/size/tune, balanced distribution and minimal reshuffle come for free, and the score-sorted order yields the leader-first replica ordering directly. §Room-Based Sharding's "consistent hashing on `room_id`" is the *property* (deterministic, balanced, minimal-reshuffle placement); HRW is a simpler mechanism that provides it, so no ring is built.
- **Deterministic + portable hash — the load-bearing property.** Every node must compute the identical placement with no shared coordination state (§Constraint: "Cluster layer must be internal", no Redis/Postgres). Weight = a per-room FNV-1a seed over `room_id`, continued FNV-1a over the node id, then a SplitMix64 finalizer to avalanche the bits so weights spread evenly and stay uncorrelated across rooms. Fixed-width `u64` wrapping arithmetic only — **no per-process seed** (`DefaultHasher`/`RandomState` would silently break the cluster), no entropy, no floats — so the value is identical on every process and platform. The member set is canonicalized (sorted + de-duplicated) so input order is irrelevant; equal weights break by node id, giving a total order every node agrees on.
- **Guaranteed properties** (spec `crates/server/tests/placement.rs`, 16): determinism (repeated calls, differing construction order, and duplicate members all agree); balance (10k rooms over 10 nodes — each within 20% of a fair share, for both primary ownership and replica membership); minimal reshuffle (a join/leave moves ~1/(k+1) of primaries, and a room's replica set changes only if it hosted the departed node — a modulo baseline in the same test churns nearly everything); N-clamp (N > member count → all members with no duplicate/panic; empty set or N=0 → empty; single node owns every room); stable leader-first order (the head is the primary for any N, and a larger replica set is a growing prefix of a smaller one).
- **Scope.** Pure, standalone placement — it does not yet wire into the running `Hub`/`Registry` (routing is Unit 3). No membership protocol (Unit 2), no consensus/replication/election (Units 4–6), no wire. Server-only (no `crates/core/src`), no new dependency (hand-rolled stable hash, keeping core dep-minimal untouched) — CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) unaffected.

## 2026-07-12 · Awareness auth-filter / #252 · presence fan-out gated on the recipient's read authority (reusing `peer_may_read`); room-level scope, zone/branch scope deferred
**Changed:** closes ARCHITECTURE §Awareness "Auth-Aware Filtering" (line 850) — awareness is not pure broadcast; the server filters per recipient. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change: the design already names auth-filtered presence with a "see" permission; this unit records that the "see" gate *is* the recipient's room read authority and locks the property in with a dedicated spec suite.
- **Awareness fan-out reuses the exact op-redaction read gate.** Every awareness delivery passes `registry::peer_may_read` — the same per-recipient `Action::Read` check the op fan-out already applies (§Per-recipient read redaction, #83) — so awareness and ops agree on who may read a room and a "see" grant is never a second, divergent policy. Gated paths: an `AwarenessSet` broadcast (the fan-out recipient loop), a per-key `AwarenessClearKey` and actor-wide `AwarenessClear` removal (both via the `peer_may_read`-filtered `fan_out_removals`, covering the grace-sweep and timed-TTL clears), and a joiner's presence replay — the Subscribe `Action::Read` gate refuses an unauthorized joiner before it replays anything. The gate is symmetric: one read check on each recipient means an unauthorized peer neither receives others' presence nor is a recipient its own presence would leak to; a peer that loses read mid-session stops receiving further sets/clears at once (identical to op fan-out).
- **The gate already existed; this unit is the spec suite + board close.** The `peer_may_read` gate on awareness landed with the schema-`@auth`-composition work (#176) alongside the op-redaction gate, not as un-filtered code — the "auth-filter still queued" board note (KANBAN line 174) predated it and was stale. The unit adds `crates/server/tests/awareness_authz.rs` (5 tests, `Acl`-driven deny + revocable-authorizer mid-session revoke) as the regression lock for a privacy-critical property (a leaked cursor is a real defect), fixes the stale note, and records the Done entry. Server-test-only diff — no `crates/core/src`, no server `src` change — so CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) is unaffected.
- **Room-level scope is the shipped seam; zone/branch scope stays deferred.** The read authority checked is room-level (`Resource::Room`) — the built authz seam. ARCHITECTURE §854 "Branch and Zone Scoping" (a cursor in a private *zone* withheld from clients without that zone's access, anchors targeting Elements in mutually-accessible zones) needs the not-yet-built Zones enforcement seam; it is explicitly out of scope here and remains gated on Zones, as does per-`(room, branch)` awareness scoping.

## 2026-07-12 · Webhooks / #253 · outbound `WebhookSink` over the engine event bus — best-effort, off the commit path
**Changed:** realizes the §Versioning "event bus = webhook substrate" item over the already-built event bus (#191). No ARCHITECTURE end-state change: the `EventSink` trait + hub fan-out already exist; this adds the second built-in sink (after `AutoVersionSink`), server-only, no core touch.
- **`WebhookSink` (server `crates/server/src/webhook.rs`) implements `EventSink`.** On each room-bearing lifecycle event it serializes a JSON body and offers it to a bounded (1024) mpsc queue; a separate spawned task owns the reqwest client and drains the queue, POSTing off the hot path. `on_event` only does a non-blocking `try_send`, so a slow/failing/absent endpoint never blocks or panics the hub commit path — mirroring the `AutoVersionSink` passive-observer precedent.
- **Delivery model = best-effort, at-most-once, no cross-restart ordering.** A full queue (endpoint fallen behind) drops the event rather than stalling emission; a failed POST (transport error, timeout, or non-2xx via `error_for_status`) is logged and never retried; a single serial worker preserves in-run FIFO order but nothing survives a restart. An honest lossy relay, not a durable queue — a receiver that needs every event reconciles out of band.
- **Worker runtime placement.** The registry actor runs on a `current_thread` runtime with only the time driver (no I/O reactor), so the delivery worker is spawned in `serve_with_authorizer` on the main multi-thread runtime (I/O-enabled) *before* the registry thread; the sink holds only the channel `Sender` (Send) and is moved into the registry thread to register on the hub. The registry thread thus emits without ever touching the network.
- **Event JSON shape.** A serde tagged object: `{"type": "<kebab-event>", …fields}` — `version-created {room, name}`, `version-renamed {room, from, to}`, `version-deleted {room, name}`, `compacted {room, floor}`, `subscribed {room}`, `after-restore {room, branch}`, `before-publish {room, branch}`. Byte-valued names render as UTF-8 text (lossy for a non-UTF-8 name, matching how the rest of the server surfaces names). Roomless transport events (connect/disconnect) and the reserved `before-migration` are not delivered — the same room-bearing filter `AutoVersionSink` applies. The optional shared secret rides the `X-Crdtsync-Webhook-Secret` header (sent over TLS, verified by the receiver), never the body.
- **Opt-in config, zero cost when off.** `ServeConfig.webhook: Option<WebhookConfig>` (URL + optional secret); `main.rs` reads `CRDTSYNC_WEBHOOK_URL` / `CRDTSYNC_WEBHOOK_SECRET`. Unset URL registers no sink and spawns no worker, so a deployment that wants no webhooks pays nothing per event — mirroring the optionally-wired admin plane / schema registry. Server may add mature deps freely: `reqwest` (rustls TLS, no system OpenSSL) + `serde`, neither reaching the dep-minimal core.
- **Spec** `crates/server/tests/webhook.rs` (4, hermetic — an in-process axum capture server on a loopback ephemeral port, never real outbound network): a version-create is POSTed with the expected shape + secret header, a compaction carries its floor with no secret header when unconfigured, no sink registered delivers nothing, a dead endpoint past the queue capacity never blocks or panics the hub. Server-only diff (no `crates/core/src` → CI miri unaffected/non-required).

## 2026-07-12 · Branches Unit 7 / #251 · schema-aware branch/version diff — server `Hub::diff_*` over two decoded snapshots (reusing the core diff engine); client query surface deferred to 7b
**Changed:** the last branch-layer unit — a diff between two branch HEADs / named-version snapshots (§Versioning-and-Branches line 630, "Schema-Aware Diff"). No ARCHITECTURE end-state change: the diff *computation* already exists as the core engine (6a-v `core::path::diff`, the structural/value `Change` set + `diff.rs` renderers); this unit only feeds two branch/version snapshots into it at the server and records the exposure boundary.
- **`Hub::diff_versions(room, a, b)` and `Hub::diff_branches(room, a, b)` → `Result<Vec<Change>, DiffError>`.** `diff_versions` decodes both named versions' captured `version_state` (the stored whole-replica bytes); `diff_branches` materializes each branch via the existing `materialize_branch` (Unit 3/4 — a live-log fork's shared base ++ divergent tail, a snapshot fork's owned base, or `main` via `export_room`) then decodes it. A shared free `diff_states(old, new)` helper decodes two encoded states and runs `core::path::diff` — so a branch against its fork source yields only the divergence, and the branch-state assembly is reused, never duplicated.
- **No diff semantics rewritten — schema-aware = the existing engine.** The `Change` set + `diff.rs` renderers already produce text char-level / xml structural / map·register·counter·marks value diffs; this unit forwards two snapshots into that engine unchanged. No missing renderer case surfaced. `diff_branches` pays a state-encode-then-decode round-trip (materialize returns bytes, `diff_states` decodes them) — an accepted reuse tax over duplicating the branch-materialization assembly; a diff is not a hot path.
- **Edge cases are clean errors, never panics** (`DiffError`, a plain enum with `Display`+`Error`, matching the server's `auth.rs`/`acl.rs` error convention — no `thiserror`): an unknown version → `UnknownVersion(name)`, unknown branch → `UnknownBranch(name)`, an encoded state that does not decode → `Decode`; a snapshot against itself → an empty change list (`path::diff` over two decodes of the same bytes is naturally empty, no special-case).
- **Exposure decision: the server-side `Hub::diff_*` computation is the unit; the client/SDK query surface is deferred to Branches Unit 7b.** Returning a diff to a *client* has no wire frame today — exposing it needs either a **new client-initiated diff-query wire frame** or routing through the **admin/control plane** (HTTP), the same client-wire-vs-admin-plane design gate as Unit 6b. Inventing a client wire frame silently is out of scope, so Unit 7 is scoped to the server method + test coverage and the query surface is parked as **Unit 7b** with the exposure question flagged. (The FFI `crdtsync_diff`/`crdtsync_diff_decode` boundary #113/#232 already marshals a *core* `Change` list; 7b is the distinct server-snapshot-pair query, not the core diff codec.) Server-only diff (no `crates/core/src`), so CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) is unaffected. Spec `crates/server/tests/branch_diff.rs` (9). **With Unit 7 done the branch layer is functionally complete** — remaining branch work is 6b + 7b (both on the exposure gate) + cross-branch merge (out of v0.x, ARCHITECTURE line 636).

## 2026-07-12 · Branches Unit 6 / #250 · branch-*subscribe* SDK surface across the four bindings; branch-management ops deferred to 6b (client-wire vs admin-plane exposure gate)
**Changed:** exposes the client-facing branch surface across the SDKs (§Versioning-and-Branches; §SDK surface). No ARCHITECTURE end-state change — this forwards an already-built client capability and records the honest exposure boundary for the rest.
- **Only branch-*subscribe* is forwarded — it is the sole already-client-reachable branch capability.** Unit 2 (#244) put the `branch` on the `Subscribe` frame and `ClientSession::subscribe_branch(room, branch)`; Unit 6 just carries that to the SDK user. FFI `crdtsync_client_subscribe_branch(client, room, room_len, branch, branch_len, out_channel)` mirrors `crdtsync_client_subscribe` (empty branch → default/active via `as_slice`'s `Some(&[])`; null handle → empty-buffer sentinel, no channel written); Python `Client.subscribe_branch`, Go `(*Client).SubscribeBranch`, wasm `subscribeBranch` — each a faithful mirror of that layer's existing `subscribe`. Default (empty branch) stays main/active-scoped, so existing callers are unchanged. No new wire, no core change (SDK/FFI-only → CI miri non-required/unaffected).
- **Branch-management ops (fork / publish / restore-as-branch / list-branches) are NOT client-reachable today — exposing them is a design gate, deferred to Unit 6b.** They live only as server-side `Hub`/`Registry` methods (`crates/server/src/{store,registry,lib}.rs`); there is **no client wire frame** carrying them and no `ClientSession` method — a client cannot trigger them over the existing sync WS. Forwarding them would require either a **new client-initiated branch-management wire frame** or routing through the **admin/control plane** (HTTP, like schema registration §5b-ii — restore/publish are admin-ish operations). That client-wire-vs-admin-plane choice is a genuine design decision, not a mechanical SDK forward, so Unit 6 is deliberately scoped to subscribe-branch only and the management surface is parked as **Branches Unit 6b** with the exposure question flagged for a design look. Building it here would have meant inventing a client wire frame — explicitly out of scope.

## 2026-07-12 · Branches Unit 5 / #249 · publish/draft — read-only published-HEAD repoint, old-state-as-version rollback, `BeforePublish` fires; per-user branches are the primitive
**Changed:** publish/draft (§Versioning-and-Branches line 618) + per-user branches (line 622) over the Unit-4 active-HEAD + branch-write machinery. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (the design already named the publish/draft semantics — edit on `main`, sync a `published` branch's HEAD for read-only consumers, republish repoints, old published snapshots stay reachable as versions; and named per-user forks as the same primitive); this logs the concrete server-side shape and closes the last reserved branch engine event.
- **`published` is a read-only snapshot fork, not a live stream.** `Hub::publish(room, published)` (`Registry::publish` wraps it to drive the auto-version drain; default target `PUBLISHED_BRANCH = b"published"`) materializes the **active editor branch's** current whole-replica state (`main` by default via `export_room`, or a restored HEAD folded from its own stream) and points the `published` branch's HEAD at it — a snapshot fork owning that state as its base (reusing the Unit-4a `branch_bases` machinery). Read-only consumers subscribe `(room, published)` and are served that base while editors keep writing `main`; the editor's later writes are invisible on `published` until the next publish. Republish repoints the base to the newer editor state.
- **Old published state stays reachable as a version — keyed on `(source branch, seq)`.** Each publish first captures the published state as an immutable named version `publish/<published>/<source>@<seq>` before the repoint, so every published state (including the first) stays reachable for **independent rollback** of published state vs editor state (reusing the named-versions capture, via a new `create_version_from_state` seam that snapshots an explicit state rather than the room's live `main` doc). The name carries the *source branch* as well as its head — a branch's state at a given head is fixed, so two publishes of the same `(source, seq)` reuse the name (a no-op the existing version covers), while the same head number on a *switched* editor branch (after a restore) stays a **distinct** rollback. (Caught by a review agent: a seq-only key silently dropped the second source's rollback; regression test added.)
- **Read-only enforcement = a durable `Branch.published` flag.** A client `Ops` write to a `published` branch is refused recoverably — `OpsRejected{Forbidden}`, the same idiom as an authz denial (the author keeps its ops and surfaces the rejection, no connection close) — gated by a `published: bool` on the durable `Branch` record (a trailing byte in the `.branches` file). A published branch never diverges, so `repoint_published` drops any stale tail a name reused from a former writable fork left behind, and — the safety net — the load path drops a tail persisted under a published branch's name, so an orphaned tail (a repoint whose best-effort tail removal failed) never folds onto the published base after a restart. (Caught by a review agent: a partial-rollback tail hazard + the orphan-after-restart vector; both closed with a regression test.)
- **`BeforePublish` fires today — the last reserved branch engine event.** It fires *before* the repoint (so an `autoVersion: [{on: before-publish}]` trigger captures at the publish point); `AutoVersionSink` maps it to `TriggerEvent::BeforePublish` (already present in core), and `Registry::publish` drives the post-op auto-version drain — mirroring how Unit 4b wired `AfterRestore`. The branch/migration engine-event reservations are now **fully consumed on the branch side**; only `BeforeMigration` remains, for the migration layer. Server-only diff (no `crates/core/src`), so CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) is unaffected.
- **Per-user branches are the existing primitive, not new machinery.** A `user/<id>` branch forked via `fork_branch`/`fork_branch_from_version` edits in isolation over a shared base — Unit 3 already gives isolated per-branch write + fan-out, so this is thin convenience + test coverage proving isolation (neither user's writes reach the base or each other; the base is unchanged). Per-user *authorization* (who may fork/own `user/<id>`) is the ACL layer (slice 4, gated), explicitly not this unit.

## 2026-07-12 · Branches Unit 4b / #248 · restore-as-branch — active-HEAD switch, audit version, first-class replayable, `AfterRestore` event
**Changed:** restore-as-branch (§Versioning-and-Branches line 614) over the Unit-4a fork-from-snapshot base. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (the design already named restore-as-branch's semantics — fork from a snapshot, switch HEAD, preserve the old branch, audit version, first-class log entry); this logs the concrete server-side shape.
- **Active HEAD = a durable per-room default-served-branch pointer.** `Hub.active_branch: room → branch` (durable `<room>.active`, absent ⇒ `main`) is the branch a *default (unnamed)* subscribe follows. `session::step`'s Subscribe resolves an empty branch to `hub.active_branch(room)` (replacing the old empty⇒`main` normalize), while an explicitly named branch — including `main` — is taken as given. The resolved branch is stored on the channel, so a channel bound *before* a restore keeps its branch: an offline op in flight against the old HEAD carries the old branch's channel and lands on the old branch via Unit 3's branch-scoped write, never on the restored state. A new plain subscribe *after* the restore follows the restored branch.
- **`Hub::restore_as_branch(room, version, new_branch)`** forks `new_branch` from the version's snapshot (Unit 4a `fork_branch_from_version`), captures an **audit version** of the pre-restore live (`main`) state, switches the active HEAD, and emits `EngineEvent::AfterRestore`. It rewrites no history and resets no sequence — the old branch (`main`) is untouched, immutable, still subscribable by name. Durable throughout, so the whole switch **replays on reload** (the `.active` pointer + the restored branch's `.branches`/`.bbase` + the audit `.versions` all come back; a `.active` naming a branch no longer registered falls back to `main`). Deleting the active branch resets the HEAD to `main`, so a default subscribe is never left dangling.
- **Audit version name keyed on `(branch, captured main seq)`** — `audit/restore/<branch>@<seq>`, branch bytes verbatim. Keying on the captured sequence (not the branch name alone) means a branch name **reused after a delete** still audits each restore: a later restore captures a moved-on `main` under a new sequence; a degenerate repeat at the identical sequence (identical state) is a no-op the existing audit already covers. (Caught by a review agent: a name-only key silently skipped the second restore's audit; regression test added.)
- **`AfterRestore` fires today.** The event-bus variant (#191) reserved for the branch layer now fires from `restore_as_branch`; `AutoVersionSink` maps it to `TriggerEvent::AfterRestore`, and `Registry::restore_as_branch` drives the post-op auto-version drain — so a governing schema's `autoVersion: [{on: after-restore, …}]` trigger captures the restored state, closing the parked branch-trigger item. `BeforePublish` stays reserved for the Unit-5 publish/draft layer. Server-only diff (no `crates/core/src`), so CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) is unaffected.
- **Known edge (noted, not fixed):** restore is not atomic — a store IO error after the fork commits but before the HEAD switch leaves `new_branch` created but not active; a retry hits `Ok(false)` (branch exists) and needs a manual `delete_branch` first. No corruption (main untouched, old branch intact). Acceptable pre-release single-node.

## 2026-07-12 · Branches Unit 4a / #247 · fork-from-snapshot — a branch whose base is a named version's snapshot (the base machinery Unit 3 deferred)
**Changed:** lands the shared-base-below-a-fork-point machinery Unit 3 deferred (DECISIONS 2026-07-12 · Unit 3). A branch may now fork from a **named version's snapshot** (§Versioning-and-Branches "storage = only divergent ops past the fork" + Named Versions #86–#92), not only a live point in `main`'s log. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (the design already allowed a branch's base to be a snapshot state); this logs the concrete base-resolution + storage shape.
- **Storage shape = the branch owns a copy of the version state; only its divergent tail is otherwise stored.** `Hub::fork_branch_from_version(room, new, version)` resolves the named version's covered sequence + its encoded whole-replica state and records the branch pointer at `fork_point = version.seq` (via the always-present `main` as the fork source, so the source-branch existence check is satisfied). The version's encoded state is copied into the branch's **owned base** — `Hub.branch_bases: room → branch → Vec<u8>` in memory, a durable `<room>_<branch>.bbase` file (state verbatim, whole-file read; room+branch hex-joined like `.blog`) — so the branch survives the source version's later deletion. The presence of a base entry is what marks a branch a snapshot fork, routing its catch-up; a live-log fork (Unit 3) has no entry and reads `main`'s log as before.
- **`catch_up_branch` serves the owned base ++ tail, never `main`'s post-version ops.** For a snapshot fork, a fresh subscriber (below `fork_point`) is served the base with the tail folded into it as one whole-replica `Catchup::Snapshot { seq: fork_point + tail.len() }` (decode base → apply tail → encode; CRDT fold is order-independent) — a self-contained stream, so it never reads `main`'s log and a `main` write past the version never leaks in. A subscriber already past the base (`last_seen ≥ fork_point`) is served just the divergent tail as `Catchup::Ops`. The seq the snapshot reports equals the branch head, so a reconnect at that seq serves nothing new — the same self-consistent numbering as a compacted room.
- **Lifecycle: base persisted before the pointer; dropped with the branch.** The `.bbase` lands before the `.branches` pointer commits (a crash never leaves a snapshot fork whose base is missing), rolled back on a pointer-persist error. `delete_branch` drops the base (memory + `.bbase`) alongside the tail, so a re-fork of the name inherits no stale base. Reload seeds `branch_bases` from the `.bbase` files; the head recompute (`fork_point + tail.len()`) already handles a snapshot fork's tail. Server-only diff (no `crates/core/src`), so CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) is unaffected. **Deferred to Unit 4b:** restore-as-branch (active-HEAD switch + audit version) + the `AfterRestore` engine event.

## 2026-07-12 · Branches Unit 3 / #246 · branch-scoped subscription + log resolution (shared base ++ per-branch divergent tail)
**Changed:** makes a `(room, branch)` subscription actually serve that branch's stream — wiring the Unit 2 wire carrier (#244) and the Unit 1 fork points (#245) into real branch-scoped catch-up, write, and fan-out. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (the design already named `(room, branch)` the replication unit and "storage cost = only divergent ops past the fork"); this logs the concrete stream-resolution + per-branch storage shape and the unknown-branch behavior.
- **A branch's stream is the shared base ++ its own divergent tail — the base is never duplicated.** `catch_up_branch(room, branch, last_seen_seq)` composes `main`'s retained log records with sequence ≤ the branch's fork point (read straight from `main`'s log, the shared immutable history) followed by the branch's own ops past the fork. Sequence numbering is the branch's: a base record keeps its `main` sequence (≤ fork point); a tail record at index `i` sits at `fork_point + i + 1`, so past the fork the sequence space diverges (same number, different op on `main` vs the branch) — sound because `(room, branch)` is the replication unit and a subscriber's `last_seen_seq` is within its own branch's space. `main` (the empty branch) is the whole existing log via the unchanged `catch_up`.
- **Forced refinement of Unit 1's fork contract: the fork point is clamped to the source's head.** Unit 1 stored `fork_point = at` as a pure pointer with no head validation. Log resolution shows a fork point past the source's head is unsound: the branch's sequence space would carry a gap (no ops between the head and `at`), the client (which advances `last_seen_seq` by *counting* delivered ops) would never reach the true head and re-fetch its tail on every reconnect, and — worse — the source's later writes into that gap would leak into the branch's base (`base_end = min(fork_point, head)` grows with the source), diverging the branch. `Hub::fork_branch` now clamps `at` to the source branch's current head, so a branch shares only history that exists; the engine already forks at the head, so real flows are unaffected. Unit 1's fork-past-head pointer tests were updated to establish real history first.
- **Storage shape: a per-`(room, branch)` divergent-op tail keyed in the hub, only the divergence persisted.** `Hub.branch_logs: room → branch → BranchLog { ops, seen }` holds only the ops past a branch's fork point; the shared base lives once in `main`'s log and is never copied — realizing "storage cost = only divergent ops past the fork." A durable `<room>_<branch>.blog` append-log (room + branch each hex-encoded, `_`-joined; the main-log record framing) mirrors `.log`; the branch head is recomputed as `fork_point + tail.len()` on reload, so a crash between persisting the tail (`.blog`) and the head pointer (`.branches`) never leaves the head trailing the ops on disk. A branch delete drops its tail (memory + `.blog`) so a re-fork of the name never inherits stale ops.
- **Branch-scoped write + fan-out.** An `Ops` write on a channel bound to a non-`main` branch appends to that branch's tail via `Hub::ingest_branch` (deduped against the branch's own seen set, persist-before-commit) and advances that branch's head — never `main`'s log, whose head is untouched. `Response.broadcast_branch` carries the write's branch so `Registry::deliver` fans out on `Session::channels_for_stream(room, branch)` — a branch write reaches only that branch's subscribers, a `main` write only `main`'s; the two streams never cross. The channel→subscription map gained the branch dimension (`Subscription { room, branch }`, empty normalized to `main`); room-scoped fan-outs (awareness, stranded-peer eviction) still use the room-only `channels_for_room`.
- **Unknown non-main branch → refused, never silently served `main`.** `step`'s Subscribe resolves the branch against the registry: `main` always resolves; a named branch absent from the registry is refused with `Error{UnknownRoom}` ("unknown branch", non-closing so the client can subscribe to a valid branch) rather than binding `main`'s stream — silently serving `main` would cross replication units. A branch must already exist (forked via `Hub::fork_branch`, Unit 1) to be subscribed; `Registry::hub_mut` exposes the hub for that engine-side fork (no client-facing wire message forks a branch in this unit).
- **Deferred (noted).** Shared-base **compaction below a fork point** is out of scope (fork-from-snapshot / restore-as-branch is Unit 4): `catch_up_branch` serves the retained base, so a freshly forked branch on an uncompacted base catches up in full, but a branch whose base was compacted past its fork point (or a below-floor joiner) is served an incomplete stream with no snapshot fallback — the correct fix needs the Unit-4 base-at-fork snapshot machinery. The op-version **range-check / catch-up translation** stay keyed on `main`'s high-water, and **awareness / version / ACL** stay room-scoped (all branches) — branch-scoping them is deferred; no test exercises a branch under compaction or a versioned branch write. Server-only diff (no `crates/core/src`), so CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) is unaffected.

## 2026-07-12 · Branches Unit 1 / #245 · per-room branch registry + durable model (pointers only; log resolution deferred)
**Changed:** first foundational unit of the branch layer (§Versioning-and-Branches). A branch is a named pointer into the op log — `Branch { name, fork_point, head }` + a per-room `BranchRegistry` defaulting to `main`, with fork/list/rename/delete pointer semantics and durable persistence beside the room. This unit tracks the pointers only; moving ops between branches / forking the actual log storage / branch-scoped subscription is Unit 3's log-resolution job. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (the model matches §Versioning-and-Branches as written); this logs the concrete registry + persistence shape.
- **Default `main` is synthesized, not stored — only forks are persisted.** The registry always holds `main` (fork_point 0), so a room's branch state is materialized lazily on the first fork: a never-forked room carries no per-room entry and writes no `<room>.branches` file, and load re-synthesizes `main` around whatever forks the file holds. This keeps the "a room that never forks behaves exactly as today" invariant structural (zero ceremony) rather than a special case, and makes `main`'s undeletability/unrenamability an invariant the persisted set can't violate.
- **`main`'s head tracks the room's server-sequence log head; fork/head positions are the room's history counter, not a cross-replica Lamport clock.** The single-node hub's per-room history position is its server sequence (`Room::head`), so `main.head` is overlaid from it at read time (derived, never persisted). ARCHITECTURE says "HEAD lamport"; the concrete high-water realized here is the server sequence — exact per-op Lamport resolution is deferred to Unit 3's log resolution, which is the layer that actually consumes fork points. `fork(new, from, at)` takes the fork point explicitly (the caller's history position), so Unit 3 can pass whatever the resolution layer decides without a model change.
- **A `<room>.branches` store record mirrors the versions index + the `.meta` record (pre-release break, no migration).** Alongside `.log` / `.snap` / `.versions` / `.meta` the store writes a `.branches`: per fork the length-prefixed name then two 8-byte little-endian history positions (fork_point, head). It lands atomically (temp → flush → rename → dir-flush) via the shared `atomic_write` / `remove_if_present`; an empty fork set removes the file. `load` **total-decodes** it: any framing shortfall discards the whole set (loading as no forks → the default `{main}`), never an error, never a panic — the record is a durability cache over the synthesized default, not a source of truth. Hub mutations persist-before-commit with rollback (mirroring the named-versions surface), so the set never reflects a fork the disk rejected.
## 2026-07-12 · Branches Unit 2 / #244 · the `branch` dimension of `(room, branch)` is reserved on the `Subscribe` frame (per-subscription), not `Hello` (per-connection)
**Changed:** adds `branch: Vec<u8>` to `Message::Subscribe` and records it on the client's per-channel room view, a forward-compat wire carrier for the `(room, branch)` replication unit (§Versioning-and-Branches / §Networking). The server branch-scoping that resolves it is Branches Unit 3; here the field is round-tripped and defaulted only. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change — the design already named `(room, branch)` the replication unit and the `Channel` handle the `(room[,branch,zone])` abstraction; this logs where the field lives and why it is reserved before the feature.
- **On `Subscribe`, not `Hello` — the subscription, not the connection, names the branch.** A connection opens once with `Hello` but multiplexes several room subscriptions over its lifetime, each on its own `Channel`; the replication unit is `(room, branch)`, so `branch` rides exactly where `room` does — per-`Subscribe`. Putting it on `Hello` would bind one branch per connection and defeat multiplexing distinct branches over one socket. This mirrors the earlier per-connection reservations (`Hello`'s `app_id`/`schema_version`, the zone envelope field): reserved on the wire before the feature (cheap now, painful after adoption), each at the frame whose scope it belongs to.
- **Empty branch is the default `main`.** The field is length-framed beside `room` in the hand-rolled codec (dep-minimal core, no serde); an existing client that names no branch sends an empty byte string and is `main`-scoped, so `subscribe(room)` stays unchanged and `subscribe_branch(room, branch)` is the explicit form. The client records the branch on the room view (`branch()` accessor) and re-sends it on `resume`.
- **Server carries and ignores it (Unit 3 scope-boundary).** `step` binds the room and does not scope the log or rooms on the branch — a non-empty branch subscribes exactly as `main` does. Branch-scoped log resolution is Unit 3; this slice is the wire + client carrier only. Break wire compat freely (pre-release, new field). Core + a one-line server destructure change; CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) gates.

## 2026-07-09 · Unit 8i / #243 · a write that lifts a room's op-version high-water past a joined enforcing peer's reach evicts that peer with `UpdateRequired`
**Changed:** closes the 8e-deferred stranded-peer item (KANBAN "Deferred within Unit 8"). The handshake range-check (8e/#189) gates a joiner only at subscribe; after 8g the reachability basis is the room's op-version high-water. A joined enforcing peer admitted at version V could later be stranded when a higher-version write raises the high-water past its back-compat reach — fan-out fail-closes its down-drop (no divergence), but the peer received no signal and silently stopped updating. It is now told: after an ingest in `Registry::deliver` lifts `max_op_version` (a pre/post delta over the acted-on room), each already-joined enforcing subscriber of the governing app is re-checked with the exact `subscriber_reaches_governing` predicate the subscribe gate admits on, and a now-unreachable peer is sent `Error { UpdateRequired }` and dropped from the room (`Session::drop_room`), mirroring the subscribe-time refusal. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change — this logs the eviction seam and the trigger re-framing.
- **Admission and eviction share the one reachability predicate.** The subscribe gate refuses on `!subscriber_reaches_governing(reg, governing, session, high_water)`; eviction re-checks the same predicate against the lifted high-water, so a peer the gate would refuse at the new high-water is exactly the peer eviction strands — they never disagree. Only a **breaking** gap the new high-water opens past the peer's version evicts; a back-compatible lift (the peer down-reaches it), the writer of its own lift (reaches the new high-water trivially, so the predicate protects it — no self-eviction), and a relay / foreign-app / versionless peer (a different version space, `governing_target` → `None` → reaches) are untouched.
- **The trigger is a high-water-raising write, re-framed from the pre-8g "subscriber lift."** The board's original wording keyed the strand on a later higher-version *subscriber* lifting the room. After 8g a mere subscribe no longer changes reachability (the gate keys on the op-version high-water, not the sticky awareness floor), so the real lift is an actual higher-version write that raises `max_op_version`. The re-check fires there — a same-or-lower write moves nothing and re-checks nobody.
- **Fail-closed, minimal blast radius.** The evicted peer's already-delivered state is unchanged; it just stops receiving fan-out and must re-subscribe after updating. `Error` names no channel, so one frame evicts a peer however many channels it held the room on. Server-only diff (no `crates/core/src`), so CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) is unaffected. The type-scope applicability filter and faithful container-field migration stay deferred.

## 2026-07-09 · Unit 8h / #242 · per-room governing metadata (app-binding + op-version high-water) is durable across a restart and a dormant sweep
**Changed:** closes the two durable-metadata items 8g/8d left deferred (KANBAN "Deferred within Unit 8"). Each room's governing metadata — its `{app_id, version}` binding and its op-version high-water — now persists beside the room's store state and is restored on load, so the range-check and the catch-up translation the metadata drives survive a restart without under-refusing or serving untranslated catch-up. No ARCHITECTURE end-state change (persistence was always the intent for both — 8g/8d shipped noted, not by design); this logs the durability seam and its one deliberate behavior sharpening.
- **A per-room `<room>.meta` record, extending the store format (pre-release break, no migration).** Alongside the `.log` / `.snap` / `.versions` files the store now writes a `.meta`: a 1-byte governing present-flag then the length-prefixed app id + 4-byte version, then a 1-byte high-water present-flag then the 4-byte version. It lands atomically (temp → flush → rename → dir-flush), and the write-or-remove scaffolding is extracted with `compact`/`write_versions` into shared `atomic_write` / `remove_if_present`. `load` **total-decodes** it: an absent, truncated, or malformed record loads as `None` (never an error, never a panic), so an old store or a torn write degrades to the standing rebuild-from-log / bind-on-subscribe reconstruction — the record is a durability cache, not a source of truth.
- **The high-water is restored past what the replayed tail yields (fixes the compacted-restart under-count).** `Room::max_op_version` is folded on ingest and persisted whenever it grows; on load the persisted all-time high-water dominates the value the replayed post-compaction tail rebuilds (`max_op_version.max(persisted)`), which is exact since compaction never lowers it. A compacted room whose high-water-setting op was folded into the snapshot before the restart now keys the range-check at the true high-water, so a below-gap joiner is refused after a restart instead of admitted to un-reachable content.
- **The binding rides a hub-level durable mirror, not `Room`, so a bound-but-never-written room needs no empty replica.** `Hub` holds a `governing: HashMap<RoomId, (app,version)>` — the durable mirror — seeded from the store on load and updated by `bind_governing` **only when a store is attached**. `Registry::with_store` seeds `room_apps` from the persisted binding; `bind_room_app` and the `deliver` binding lookup fall back to the hub's durable binding when the live map has no entry. So a populated room a dormant sweep dropped or a restart has not yet rebuilt is still governed by its persisted app — its first subscriber is served **translated** catch-up (the fix), and a foreign first subscriber cannot seize or mistranslate it. A store-less hub leaves the mirror empty, so the pure in-memory dormant-rebind behavior is unchanged (the one deliberate sharpening: with a store, a durably-bound room's incumbent survives dormancy rather than rebinding to a first foreign subscriber — correct, since the persisted log is the incumbent's data).
- **Best-effort persist, fail-safe.** The metadata write is best-effort at both seams (ingest fold, bind) — the binding and high-water are derivable, so a write failure degrades to the sound rebuild-from-log fallback rather than failing the data path (the op log stays the authoritative persist-before-commit seam). Server/store-only diff (no `crates/core/src`), so CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) is unaffected. Stranded-peer eviction on a version lift, the type-scope applicability filter, and faithful container-field migration stay deferred.

## 2026-07-09 · Unit 8g / #241 · handshake range-check keys on the room's op-version high-water, not the sticky TTL-grace governing floor
**Changed:** realizes the 8e-deferred follow-up (KANBAN "Deferred within Unit 8") — the range-check now decides reachability against the room's **actual op-version high-water** rather than the sticky governing floor `reconcile_room_apps` lifts to the highest version ever *present*. Fixes a fail-closed false-positive; no ARCHITECTURE end-state change (the intended gate always was "reach the room's worst-case op version" — the floor was an over-approximation of it), so this logs the precision fix and the forced compaction/snapshot corollaries.
- **The high-water, not the floor, is the true worst-case op version.** A transient higher-version peer that subscribes once and leaves without ever writing lifts the sticky floor (deliberate for the awareness-TTL grace) but folds no op into the room. The old gate `reachable(reg, app, governing_floor, client)` then refused a returning lower-version client `UpdateRequired` even though every stored op is at or below its reach and could be served in full. Keying on the room's max logged op version — `reachable(reg, app, high_water, client)` — is strictly more precise and still guarantees fan-out only ever down-translates across invertible edges (a joiner admitted at the true high-water down-reaches every op the log holds). An empty log / no governing-app op → `None` high-water → no op-version constraint, never refused on this basis.
- **The high-water is a persistent per-room fact, not a live-log scan — it survives compaction (forced).** Compaction drops the retained log while the merged snapshot still embodies the compacted ops' (possibly higher) versions. A max over the *live* log would read `None`/under-count exactly on a compacted room and wrongly admit a below-gap joiner the snapshot would then serve unreachable content — a fail-open the naive "max over `logged_versions`" would introduce. So `Room` carries a `max_op_version: Option<u32>` folded on ingest and left standing by compaction; the accessor `Hub::max_op_version` reads it. Relay/foreign-app ops are untagged (`None`) and excluded, so a plain max over the governing app's tags is correct.
- **The cold-start snapshot is sourced from the high-water too (forced by the loosened admission).** `catch_up_snapshot` projected the snapshot from the governing floor; that was safe only because the old, stricter admission reached the floor. Once admission keys on the high-water, a floor above the high-water (a phantom higher-version peer) makes the floor-sourced projection resolve an unreachable chain and fall back to serving the snapshot **verbatim** — divergence for a below-high-water joiner. The snapshot embodies content at exactly the high-water, so it is now projected `from = high_water`: admission (`reachable(high_water, client)`) then exactly matches the projection chain, so it is always invertible and never falls to the divergent verbatim path. This also fixes a latent pre-existing bug — a newer joiner to a room whose floor was lifted above its content was served un-migrated content under a mistaken floor source.
- **Sticky `room_apps` binding unchanged; stranded-peer eviction and durable-across-restart high-water stay deferred.** The binding still governs awareness TTL + which app's chain is used — only the *version the range-check and snapshot compare against* changed. Re-checking/evicting an already-joined peer on a version lift remains deferred (the gate is still subscribe-time only). The high-water is in-memory, rebuilt from the retained log on restart, so a compacted room's high-water can under-count across a store restart — the same durable-metadata gap as the deferred durable room binding (the snapshot persists `base_seq` + state, no version); pre-restart soundness there was never reliable (it depended on which peer happened to be present). Server-only diff (no `crates/core/src`), so CI miri (`-p crdtsync-core`) is unaffected.

## 2026-07-09 · Schema Unit 9b-SDK / #240 · `take_rejected` SDK surface — the FFI+SDK forwarding of `onOpsRejected`, mirroring 9a's error-code surface
**Changed:** realizes the SDK half of ARCHITECTURE §Schema's `onOpsRejected` hook (Unit 9) — the deliberate follow-on 9b (#239) flagged, mirroring how 9a surfaced 8e's wire/server `onUpdateRequired`. Pure plumbing over the landed core mechanism; no `crates/core/src` change, no scope change.
- **A drain, not a callback registry — matching `take_repairs`.** `crdtsync_client_take_rejected(client, out) -> i32` drains `ClientSession::take_rejected()` into one buffer the SDK decodes; each SDK exposes a drain-returns-list, the same shape `take_repairs` already established, rather than inventing a callback surface. `1` on success (empty → a bare `u32` zero count, never a null buffer), `-1` on a bad handle or null `out`; the buffer is caller-freed via `crdtsync_buf_free`, like every buffer-producing entry point.
- **Encoding: count + per-batch channel/reason/ops, reusing 9a's mapping and the op-encode helper.** The buffer is a `u32` count, then per `Rejected` the channel (`u32`), the reason discriminant (`i32` via 9a's `error_code_discriminant` — the same mapping, not a second one), and the ops (a `u32` op-count then per op a `u32`-length-prefixed `encode_op` byte string — the existing op encoder the ops paths already use, so a refused op crosses the boundary carrying its bytes for the app to show/discard/export). Each SDK decodes it into an idiomatic value list and maps `reason` to its exported `ErrorCode` (9a already exported it per language): Python `take_rejected() -> list[Rejected]` (a `Rejected` NamedTuple `channel`/`reason: ErrorCode`/`ops: list[bytes]`, both exported), Go `TakeRejected() []Rejected` (struct `Channel`/`Reason ErrorCode`/`Ops [][]byte`), wasm `takeRejected()` → an array of `{ channel, reason, ops }` (`ops` an array of `Uint8Array`). FFI/SDK-only diff — CI miri unaffected/non-required; harnesses in all four languages receive an `OpsRejected` frame and assert the drain yields the batch, an empty drain is empty, and a bad handle / null out is `-1`.

## 2026-07-08 · Schema Unit 9b / #239 · authored-op rejection becomes a non-fatal `OpsRejected` frame — the server refuses ops without closing, the client drains them from its outbox for the app to export
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Schema's `onOpsRejected` hook (Unit 9, ARCHITECTURE §389) as the core-wire + server + client-core mechanism; the SDK surface (9b-SDK) is a deliberate follow-on, mirroring how 8e (wire/server `onUpdateRequired`) landed separately from 9a (its SDK surface). No scope change.
- **Authored-op rejection is non-fatal, not a connection close.** The prior Ops-Write path replied `forbidden("write denied")` — an `ErrorCode::Forbidden` `Error` frame that a client surfaces as `ClientError::Server`, i.e. a fatal outcome. But `onOpsRejected` is explicitly app-recoverable ("shows / discards / exports" the ops, session continues), and an op the server won't accept must not sit acked-forever in the offline outbox — the client needs to learn it was rejected to drain/export it. So the Write-deny reply becomes a new sender-directed, non-fatal frame; the connection stays open, the ops are neither ingested, acked, nor fanned out. Only the **authored-ops Write** rejection changes — every other `forbidden`/`violation` (subscribe, awareness, version) stays fatal, since only authored ops sit in the outbox needing recovery.
- **Carrier: op-id sequences + a reason code, not echoed op bytes.** `Message::OpsRejected { channel, seqs: Vec<u64>, reason: ErrorCode }` (wire tag 22). `seqs` are the refused ops' per-client `OpId.seq` — the client resolves them against its own outbox, which still holds the op bytes, so echoing whole ops back would be redundant. `reason` reuses the 9a `ErrorCode` (`Forbidden` for the revoked write). An explicit seq **list** (not a `{from,to}` range) is the honest carrier: it names exactly the refused ops, represents an empty rejection naturally (an empty `Ops` batch → empty `seqs`), and needs no monotonic-contiguity assumption about the outbox. Codec is length-framed (count-prefixed u64s), total-decode → `ProtocolError` never a panic, mirroring the `Versions` idiom; round-trip + truncation-at-every-cut covered. Direction guards mirror `Accepted`/`SchemaAdvert`: client `receive` accepts it, server `step` rejects a client-sent one as a protocol violation.
- **Client model: drain from the outbox into a drainable rejected buffer.** `receive(OpsRejected)` partitions the channel's outbox — the refused ops (matched by seq) move to a session-level `rejected: Vec<Rejected>`, the rest stay queued. This satisfies both halves of "app shows/discards/exports": the ops **leave** the outbox (so `resend` never loops them forever, distinct from `Accepted{through}` which prunes *accepted* ops) but are **kept retrievable** with their bytes and the reason. `take_rejected() -> Vec<Rejected>` drains the buffer (mirrors `take_repairs`), each `Rejected { channel, reason, ops }`; the SDK slice (9b-SDK) forwards it to an `onOpsRejected` callback. The buffer is at the session, not the room, so one drain surfaces rejections across every channel.
- **Scoped to the authz-revoked trigger; schema-invalid folds into 9c.** The pinned trigger is auth-revoked-while-offline (`authorized(Write)` denies → `reason = Forbidden`). An enforcing-server *schema-invalid* rejection would emit the same frame with a different reason, but there is no producer-ingress validation point yet, and inventing producer-validation semantics overlaps 9c's open design question (given repair-closure, schema constraints normalize at read, never reject at merge — so what a producer rejects *on* is unpinned). The frame carries an arbitrary `ErrorCode`, so 9c can add the schema-invalid trigger without a wire change.

## 2026-07-08 · SDK Unit 9a / #238 · the client receive contract yields the server error code — a breaking C ABI signature change surfacing `onUpdateRequired`
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Schema's `onUpdateRequired` hook (Unit 9) on the SDK surface. First slice of Unit 9; no scope change. The carrier already existed end to end — `Message::Error { code: ErrorCode }` (wire tag 3), `ClientSession::receive` yielding `ClientError::Server { code }`, and `ErrorCode::UpdateRequired` (wire tag 6) the `onUpdateRequired` signal — but the FFI collapsed every receive error to `0`, so an SDK could not tell a malformed frame from a server refusal. This slice is pure plumbing across the boundary.
- **The receive FFI grows an out-param, not a new return contract.** `crdtsync_client_receive(client, msg, msg_len, out_error_code: *mut i32) -> i32` keeps its `1 applied / 0 undecodable-or-refused / -1 bad-handle` return; on a `ClientError::Server { code }` it writes the code discriminant to `out_error_code` and returns `0`. Every other outcome leaves `out_error_code` untouched (the null-out idiom, mirroring `crdtsync_client_actor`), and a null `out_error_code` skips the write. So an SDK pre-seeds a "none" sentinel (`-1`) and reads a written discriminant only on a server refusal — distinguishing "malformed frame" from "server said UpdateRequired/Forbidden/AuthFailed." **This is a breaking C ABI signature change; pre-release, so callers (the three SDKs + FFI tests) were updated in place, no compat shim.**
- **The integer mapping mirrors the wire tags, chosen for identical cross-SDK decode.** `0` ProtocolViolation, `1` UnsupportedVersion, `2` AuthFailed, `3` UnknownRoom, `4` Internal, `5` Forbidden, `6` UpdateRequired — the same order as `protocol::error_code_tag`, but re-stated as an FFI-local `error_code_discriminant` (an ABI contract distinct from the wire codec, which they happen to coincide with). Each SDK re-declares the enum in its own idiom (the established `Side` precedent): Python `ErrorCode` IntEnum + a `ServerError(RuntimeError)` that `receive` raises; Go an `ErrorCode int32` type with a `NoErrorCode = -1` sentinel, `Receive` returning `(int, ErrorCode)`; wasm a `#[wasm_bindgen]` `ErrorCode` enum thrown from `receive` (`Result<bool, JsValue>`).
- **No core change — the mechanism was already covered.** `receive` already yielded `ClientError::Server { code }` for an `Error` frame (core test `a_server_error_surfaces_to_the_caller`), so no `crates/core/src` edit was needed; the diff is FFI/SDK-only and CI miri (which does run on `-p crdtsync-ffi`) was exercised on the new FFI test locally.
- **`onOpsRejected` + producer validation deferred.** `onRepaired` is already surfaced (`take_repairs`, #233 + #235/#236/#234). `onOpsRejected` (9b) needs a *new* wire frame the server emits on refusing authored ops — no existing carrier — so it is a later slice. Producer-side reject-before-send (9c) needs a design look first: given repair-closure (schema constraints normalize at read, never reject at merge), what a producer edit rejects *on* — enforcing-server producer-ingress validation vs a client-local pre-check — is not yet pinned.

## 2026-07-08 · Zones 1b-ii-a / #237 · cross-zone enforcement splits — anchor rejection is a static read-time check, move rejection needs an op-apply seam
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Zones' "reject cross-zone move/anchor at schema validation" (Unit 1b). Implementation forced a split of 1b-ii into an anchor half (shippable now) and a move half (gated); no scope change, both remain in-scope.
- **Anchor rejection is a pure additive `validate()` check — no op-reject.** A `RangedElement` whose two `RangeAnchor` endpoints resolve to different zones is flagged `ViolationKind::CrossZoneAnchor { id }` during the read-time `validate()` walk (over `doc.ranged_elements()`, id-sorted so replica-identical) and repaired as `RepairKind::Dropped` — reads absent, exactly the `DisallowedChild`→`Dropped` normalization. This fits the confirmed enforcement model: a CRDT can't reject a concurrent op at merge, so schema constraints are read-time normalization over merged state, never op-rejection. Marks/comments/highlights are all conventions over the one ranged primitive, so covering `RangedElement` covers them; a same-zone or unzoned-baseline range is untouched.
- **Move rejection is gated on an op-apply-seam decision (1b-ii-b).** A `move_xml` crossing a zone boundary is **not** statically detectable from the materialized tree — after the move the node simply sits well-placed in its new zone (zone membership is positional, per 2026-07-04), and there is no in-place read-repair that relocates it. Detecting it needs the move relation (`base` birth-parent vs current parent), which `validate()` does not consume, and enforcement must keep the move out of the per-zone streams entirely. So it needs a human/design call: **where** the move is refused — emit-side in `move_xml`, fold-side as a deterministic silent drop in `TreeMoves.redo` (mirroring the cycle-drop, but requiring `Schema` + id→path→zone threaded into the deliberately schema-free "pure edges" tree-move layer), or a connection-level `Forbidden` — and **whether** the semantics is recorded-but-not-applied (convergent) or op-never-admitted. This is the same op-apply seam that gates Zones Unit 2 (per-zone lamport streams).

## 2026-07-08 · Doc-level ACL slice 3a · authority is an evaluation-layer view over content-neutral storage; creator-id is a document property, revoke authority is actor-id-scoped
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Ownership's authority foundation on the slice-2 evaluator. First sub-slice of slice 3; no scope change.
- **Authority is decided over the merged view, never rejected at merge.** A CRDT can't reject a concurrent revoke op, so provenance-based revocation is a pure decision over merged state, exactly as deny-overrides is. The tuple set stays content-neutral (`acl_tuples()`/`acl_tuple()` drop a tuple on ANY revoke, authority-blind — required by "no merge change"); authority is applied only by `evaluate_with_authority` over `acl_records()`, which carries each tuple's grow-only union set of revokers. A tombstone is honored iff **any** recorded revoker was authorized. Security decisions must use the authority path; the raw live set is deliberately authority-blind. `AclRecord{tuple, revoked_by}` + `decide_capability_with_authority`/`evaluate_with_authority` are the authority-aware counterparts of slice 2's calls (which stay unchanged, as-present).
- **creator-owns is synthesized, not stored — and the creator id is a document property, not an actor property.** The creator implicitly owns `/` via a synthetic root `Own` tuple folded into the decision (no explicit grant, the un-granted root of the authority chain). The creator's `ClientId` is a caller-supplied **parameter** to the authority evaluator, not a field on `AclActor` and not persisted: core hosts no identity provider (the `AclActor` precedent), and "who bootstrapped this doc's authority" is a property of the *document*, not of the *querying actor* — so a separate param.
- **Revoke authority is actor-id-scoped — membership-derived ownership fails closed.** A revoke by `R` of grant `T{grantor G, path P}` is honored iff `R == G`, `R == creator`, or `R` owns `P` via an **actor-id `Own` grant**. Path-ownership from a `Group`/`Authenticated`/`Anyone` subject does NOT confer revoke authority: core knows the revoker's id (the op author) but not its group/class membership, so letting a class `Own` confer revoke power would let an arbitrary actor inherit it. Membership-derived ownership fails closed (its revoke disregarded). A local `/code-review` caught the initial impl forcing `authenticated: true` on the revoker actor (so class subjects matched) — a real hole in the load-bearing property; fixed + regression-tested (class + group). Group/role-aware authority (with real memberships) is a later server concern.
- **The recursive chain is explicitly deferred to 3b.** 3a checks revoke-authority ownership as-present, non-recursively — so an owner whose ownership was itself authoritatively revoked can still authorize a revoke within this slice. Closing that (the multi-hop attenuated delegation walk) is 3b-i; it is the depth-≥2 generalization of 3a's depth-1 rule, so 3a's honored/ignored outcomes stay valid as the base case.

## 2026-07-08 · SDK Unit 6b-i · FFI xml gets two surfaces — doc (ops-returning) + client (enqueue/ack), because the outbox guarantee is only reachable client-side
**Changed:** first slice of Unit 6b (the C ABI the four language bindings forward to). Establishes the FFI edit pattern for all of 6b. No scope change.
- **XML edits are exposed on BOTH the doc and client surfaces.** The doc surface (`crdtsync_doc_xml_*`) matches the existing `list_*`/`text_*` ops-returning shape — it emits the ops but has no outbox. The #124 guarantee — an SDK edit must be acked and resent — is reachable only through `ClientSession::enqueue_ops`, so a second **client surface** (`crdtsync_client_xml_*`) routes authored ops through the outbox. An SDK forwards xml edits via the client surface (so they ack/resend like every other edit) and reads via the doc surface (which, matching the existing minimal client read surface, is the only place reads live — the client surface is edits-only). Every later 6b edit slice (marks 6b-ii) follows this doc+client split; read-only capabilities (diff, `marks_at`, `take_repairs`) need only the doc surface.
- **Inert edits frame a zero-op `Ops` frame, not nothing.** A held-channel inert client edit sends a zero-op frame, consistent with the shipped atomic-transaction empty-frame convention — the boundary stays uniform rather than special-casing "no ops" as "no frame."
- **`xml_move` is the sole multi-path C ABI fn** (two paths + two indices), null-checking both — the C ABI otherwise addresses one path per call. The core façade fn is `xml_move_child`.

## 2026-07-08 · SDK Units 6c/6d/6e · the four-SDK fan-out completes Unit 6 — uniform doc/client split, a shared change-decoder gap surfaced per language
**Changed:** the Python/Go/wasm bindings for the xml/marks/diff/schema surface; completes Unit 6 (and the XmlElement epic). No scope change.
- **The doc-vs-client split is uniform across all four SDKs.** Every binding exposes edits on both a doc surface (returning ops, the `list_*`/`text_*` shape) and a client surface (routing through `ClientSession::enqueue_ops`, so an SDK edit is acked/resent), and reads on the doc surface only — because the C ABI exposes xml-tag / children-len / marks-at solely there. This is the pattern 6b-i set at the C boundary, now consistent up through every language.
- **Each language's change decoder had the same latent gap — a diff over mark-bearing snapshots errored.** The per-language diff change decoders were written against diff tags 0–7 (pre-5d), so the 5d mark-change variants (`MarkAdded`/`MarkRemoved`/`MarkChanged`, tags 8/9/10) and the `elementref` scalar were unhandled — a real bug reachable once xml/marks diffs exist. Each binding extended its decoder + added a round-trip regression test (a caught behavioral bug gets a test). The exhaustive-match discipline (no wildcard) that protects the wasm `change_to_js` doesn't extend to a hand-rolled decoder in another language, so the gap had to be closed per SDK.
- **SDK-only PRs need not wait on the miri gate.** The `miri` job runs `-p crdtsync-core` and is unaffected by a Python/Go/wasm-only diff (and is non-required in branch protection — a pending miri leaves a PR `UNSTABLE`, not `BLOCKED`). So the three SDK PRs merged on their green language job + the workspace `test` job rather than paying the ~1h40m core-Miri wait. Core/ffi changes still wait on miri — it is meaningful only where core UB is possible.

## 2026-07-08 · SDK Unit 6b-iv · FFI schema/repair completes the C ABI — schema-bind is doc-surface (no enqueue), `take_repairs` reuses the length-framed list convention
**Changed:** fourth + final slice of Unit 6b; completes the C ABI. No scope change.
- **`set_schema` is doc-surface, not client-surface.** Binding a schema is local runtime state — it authors no CRDT op, broadcasts nothing — so unlike the xml/marks edit slices it has nothing to enqueue and lives entirely on the doc surface. `take_repairs` is a read, likewise doc-surface. So 6b-iv adds no client surface (the simplest 6b slice).
- **`take_repairs` reuses the single-buffer length-framed list, not an array of `CrdtBuf`.** The `onRepaired` drain returns one buffer: a `u32` count then per path a `u32`-length-prefixed `encode_repair_path` byte string — the same convention `marks_at` (6b-ii) and the diff change-list (6b-iii) use for a variable-length structured return. Draining reseeds the repair baseline, so a standing repair surfaces exactly once across calls — the settle-point contract holds through the FFI (regression-tested).
- **Expose the decode side (`crdtsync_repair_path_decode`), matching 6b-iii.** A boundary validator that round-trips (identity on well-formed, error on malformed) an untrusted repair-path buffer, mirroring `crdtsync_diff_decode`'s choice to put the decode at the C boundary rather than leave it in each SDK — so all four SDKs validate the same way instead of re-implementing the parse.

## 2026-07-08 · SDK Unit 6b-iii · FFI diff — `crdtsync_diff` pre-existed, the slice's real deliverable is the boundary decode
**Changed:** third slice of Unit 6b. No new diff surface — reconciles the 6a-v façade with the already-shipped diff FFI. No scope change.
- **Don't duplicate `crdtsync_diff`.** The Schema-Aware-Diff work (#113) already exposed `crdtsync_diff(old, new) -> CrdtBuf`, which is exactly `diff_encoded`. So 6b-iii adds only the missing inverse: `crdtsync_diff_decode` — the boundary read of `core::path::decode_changes`, turning encoded diff bytes back into the structured change list the language bindings marshal. The new capability 6a-v added over the old diff FFI was the decode, and that is the whole slice.
- **Decode is total across the FFI frame.** A diff crosses an untrusted boundary, so `crdtsync_diff_decode` wraps the decode in `catch_unwind` and maps truncated/garbage/empty → status 0 + empty out, null out → -1 — never a panic across the C frame, matching the crate's existing 1/0/-1 out-param idiom.

## 2026-07-08 · SDK Unit 6b-ii · FFI marks follow the doc+client split — authoring rides the client/enqueue surface, `marks_at` the doc surface
**Changed:** second slice of Unit 6b; forwards the marks façade over the C ABI. No scope change — applies 6b-i's established pattern.
- **Marks split by read-vs-write, per 6b-i's rule.** Mark authoring (`mark`/`mark_set_value`/`mark_delete`) emits ops, so it rides the client surface (`crdtsync_client_mark_*`) through `enqueue_ops` — the #124 ack/resend guarantee. `marks_at` is a read → the doc surface. This is the general rule 6b-i set: edits → client/enqueue, reads → doc.
- **No invented crossings.** `Side` crosses as an int (0/1) matching `relative_position`; the `Scalar` value and the `mark_id` (`ElementId` bytes) reuse the existing scalar/id crossing conventions; `marks_at` reuses the established variable-length structured-return shape. The FFI adds no new encoding — every value crosses the way the crate already crosses its kind.

## 2026-07-08 · Doc-level ACL slice 3b-ii · provenance-bounded deny closes the deny-as-backdoor gap — authority-scoped deny, creator immunity, fail-closed in the fixpoint
**Changed:** final core provenance slice; completes the doc-ACL evaluator. Realizes ARCHITECTURE §Decision-Flow's "provenance-bounded deny." No scope change.
- **A deny binds only within its author's authority — the anti-backdoor property.** 3a/3b-i honored a `Deny` as-present with global deny-overrides, which let a subordinate's or peer's deny suppress a superior's grant — i.e. a deny could do what a revoke may not (revocation is provenance-gated; an ungated deny is a backdoor around it). 3b-ii scopes a deny to grants the deny author has authority over (validly owns the grant's path or an ancestor, at/above the granter). An out-of-authority deny is disregarded. Crucially this is a REFINEMENT, not a reversal: the in-authority deny cases all still fire — slice-2 deny-overrides (same-authority deny beats allow), superior `deny own` carve-outs, and "deny beats static/default grants always" (a deny always trumps a schema role-grant or token role, which have no doc-ACL provenance to be bounded by). Only the cross-authority doc-ACL-vs-doc-ACL case changed.
- **Creator-deny immunity.** creator-owns-`/` is modeled as an ordinary `Own` tuple (3a), so naive deny-overrides would let a subordinate's `Deny(Own)` cancel it. The creator's root authority is immune — no one is above the creator, so no subordinate deny binds it.
- **Deny-provenance folds into the 3b-i least-fixpoint, fail-closed.** A deny's authority is itself an ownership, which is a rooted-unrevoked grant — so deny-scoping is contingent on the same fixpoint that computes rooting/revocation. A deny whose authority is contested resolves fail-closed (an ambiguous deny does not bind), order-independent, Miri-clean on cyclic provenance. The evaluator is now the complete core doc-ACL decision function; the server enforcement wiring (slice 4) consumes it.

## 2026-07-08 · Doc-level ACL slice 3b-i · authority is a rooted recursive walk solved as an iterative least-fixpoint — no native recursion, fail-closed on forged cycles
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Ownership's attenuated recursive delegation on 3a's foundation. First sub-slice of 3b; closes the 3a-deferred hole. No scope change.
- **A grant is valid only if rooted at the creator.** An ALLOW tuple confers authority iff its grantor validly owned the grant's path or an ancestor — recursively, bottoming out at the creator (the un-granted root who owns every path; the synthesized creator-owns-`/` needs no grantor). An unrooted grant (self-granted, forged, or whose granting chain never reaches the creator) is inert. This is the depth-≥2 generalization of 3a's depth-1 grantor/owner check; 3a's honored/ignored outcomes are the base case, so its tests stay green.
- **Attenuation falls out of rooting.** To write any tuple on a path an actor must validly own it or an ancestor, so only ownership confers granting power (a mere reader can't delegate) and a grant can't exceed the granter's scope. Ownership is resolved from actor-id `Own` grants only (3a's fail-closed rule — a `Group`/class `Own` confers no delegable or revoke authority, since core knows an actor's id but not its memberships).
