- **Rooting and revocation are mutually recursive — solved as a least-fixpoint, not native recursion.** A revoke's authority is an ownership; an ownership is a rooted-and-unrevoked grant — so the two are defined in terms of each other. Computed as an iterative least-fixpoint: each pass recomputes `rooted`/`revoked` from the previous snapshot only, order-independent by construction (no reliance on record/DFS order), no native recursion (a crafted deep or cyclic provenance graph cannot stack-overflow — the concern the dispatch flagged), pass count bounded (`2N+2`). A forged self-referential cycle roots at no creator and confers nothing; a still-oscillating revoke is disregarded fail-closed (an ambiguous revoke never strips a grant). The verdict is a stable pure function of the merged set, not an artifact of the pass count → replicas converge.
- **Rooting gates only ALLOW grants; deny stays as-present (deferred to 3b-ii).** Applying rooting to a `Deny` would silently drop an unrooted deny — fail-OPEN, the wrong default for a deny. So denies remain honored as-present (3a behavior) and their provenance-scoping (bounded deny, creator-immunity) is 3b-ii. 3b-i keeps 3a's ownership proxy for "superior"; peer-vs-superior precision is 3b-ii.

## 2026-07-08 · SDK Unit 6a-vi · path façade schema-bind + repair — schema crosses as bytes, repair reports locations (value read normally), completes the 6a façade
**Changed:** sixth + final core slice of Unit 6; exposes schema binding + `onRepaired` over `core::path`. No engine change.
- **Schema binds by bytes, total-decode at the boundary.** `set_schema(doc, schema_bytes) -> bool` parses the bytes (`core::schema`, total-decode) then binds — a malformed schema returns `false`, never panics, mirroring every other SDK-facing byte boundary. The SDK crosses schema bytes, so the façade takes `&[u8]`, not a `Schema`.
- **`take_repairs` reports locations, not values — the value is read normally.** The façade surfaces `Document::take_repairs` as encoded path lists (`encode_repair_path`/`parse_repair_path` the boundary path codec). It deliberately adds NO repaired-value accessor: Schema Unit 2b made repair a read-time normalization, so the app observes the repaired value through an ordinary `path::get_*` read at the reported location. A value accessor would duplicate the read path and risk a stale cache. `take_repairs` is the `onRepaired` change-signal (locations that newly need repair); the read is the value.
- **6a is complete.** With schema-repair landed, `core::path` now covers the full xml/marks/repair/diff surface (attrs/children/move/marks/diff/schema) — the single path-addressed façade the four SDK bindings (6b FFI → 6c/6d/6e Python/Go/wasm) forward to, no per-binding reimplementation.

## 2026-07-08 · SDK Unit 6a-v · path façade diff surface — the SDK boundary carries encoded diff bytes, decode is the total-decode inverse
**Changed:** fifth slice of Unit 6; exposes the diff engine over `core::path`. No engine change.
- **The façade presents encoded bytes, because the SDK boundary only carries bytes.** `diff_encoded` folds `diff` + `encode_changes` into one call returning `Vec<u8>` — the shape the FFI/wasm cross opaquely, mirroring how `relative_position` returns opaque position bytes. The structured `diff` (→ `Vec<Change>`) stays exposed for in-core callers, but the SDK-facing primitive is bytes.
- **`decode_changes` is the load-bearing addition — total-decode.** `encode_changes` already existed (write side); the SDK read side needs to turn diff bytes back into structured changes, so `decode_changes(bytes) -> Result<Vec<Change>, DecodeError>` is the inverse, total on truncation/garbage (a typed error, never a panic) — a diff crosses an untrusted boundary, so the same total-decode discipline as `decode_op`/`decode_state` applies. Round-trips every `Change` variant (tree + mark). No change to what `diff()` detects — this slice is façade + boundary codec only.

## 2026-07-08 · Doc-level ACL slice 2 · the evaluator lands in core, deny-overrides with no specificity tiebreaker, roles are grants so no cycle
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Decision Flow's doc-ACL tier as a pure function. Second slice of the Doc-level ACL gate; records the load-bearing evaluation calls, no scope change.
- **The evaluator is core, not server — identity is injected.** The tuple set + its decision function are pure CRDT-state reads, so `decide_capability`/`evaluate`/`effective_roles` live in `core::acl` beside the slice-1 tuples, not in the server. Core hosts no identity provider, so the querying subject is an injected `AclActor{id, groups, roles, authenticated}` the caller (server) fills from its `Identity` — the same "core provides the rule, the caller provides membership" split the schema `@auth` parse (4b) established. The server's job is only to compose this tier into the path-carrying decision flow (step 4, `@auth` role→capability mapping), which needs the enforcement slice's `Resource` and stays out of core.
- **Deny-overrides with no path-specificity tiebreaker.** A matching `Deny` of a capability beats any `Allow`, on the same OR a broader path — a broader deny is an AWS-style hard floor a more-specific allow beneath it cannot re-open. So the verdict is `(any matching deny of the cap) → Deny`, else owner/allow, else Abstain. Path specificity is deliberately NOT a tiebreaker between allow and deny (it would turn a hard floor into a soft default and let a deep grant escape a broad denial). The tier *abstains* on no governing tuple (rather than denying) so the `@auth` tier composes above it before the terminal default-deny.
- **`Own` implies the sub-lattice; deny is capability-separated.** An `Allow(Own)` confers Read/Write/PublishAwareness/Own over the subtree (an owner needn't be granted each). Deny does not mirror this: `Deny(Own)` strips only ownership (a direct `Read` allow survives), `Deny(Read)` blocks reads even for an owner — denies target exactly their named capability, so the lattice implication is an allow-side convenience, not a deny-side amplifier.
- **Roles are grants, not subjects — so the cycle concern is structurally absent.** Honoring slice-1's types (`AclGrant::Role`, and `AclSubject` has no role variant), a `Role` grant is a per-doc role *assignment* to an actor/group, never to a role. Because no assignment targets a role, there are no role→role edges, so `effective_roles` is a single non-recursive pass with nothing to cycle — the "bound the delegation depth / detect cycles" concern the dispatch raised is answered by the type model, not by a depth cap. Turning the resolved roles into capabilities is the `@auth` server tier (decision-flow step 4), out of this core slice.

## 2026-07-08 · SDK Unit 6a-iv · path façade marks surface — a mark is path-addressed by its sequence but id-addressed for mutation, single-sequence spans only
**Changed:** fourth slice of Unit 6 (SDK surface); exposes value marks over `core::path`. No scope change.
- **A mark straddles two addressing models — the façade honours both.** The span endpoints are path-addressed (`seq_path` + index/side → a `RelativePosition` anchor, via the same resolution `relative_position` #137 already does), but the mark itself lives in the document annotation set keyed by an `ElementId`, not in the element tree. So `mark(...)` returns the minted id as opaque bytes and the mutators (`mark_set_value`/`mark_delete`) take that byte handle — a mark is created *by path* but mutated *by id*, because the annotation set has no path. This mirrors how other non-tree ids cross the SDK boundary as `ElementId` bytes.
- **Single-sequence spans only; the inert contract carries through.** Both endpoints resolve on one `seq_path` — cross-element mark spans (endpoints on different sequences) stay deferred (4b-ii, needs the cross-element anchor model). Any unresolvable anchor (non-sequence path, out-of-range index) yields empty ops + `None` id, the same emptiness-as-effect contract the earlier 6a slices established, so a caller broadcasts nothing when the mark can't be placed.
- **Schema-bind/`take_repairs` split out.** The old 6a-iv board line bundled marks with the `set_schema`/`onRepaired` façade; they share nothing (marks are annotation-set writes, schema-bind is a document-level repair binding), so the repair façade moved to its own slice (6a-vi) to keep each focused.

## 2026-07-08 · Zones Unit 1b-i · zone-membership resolution — longest-prefix over segment-split root paths, innermost wins, unzoned distinct from every zone
**Changed:** realizes the resolver ARCHITECTURE §Zones's cross-zone rules need; detection only, no scope change. Second slice of Zones Unit 1b (the enforcement wiring is 1b-ii).
- **Membership is a longest-prefix match over segment-split paths.** `zone::zone_of(schema, path_keys) -> Option<&str>` splits each parsed zone root string (1a) into path segments and returns the name of the zone whose root is the longest segment-wise prefix of the target path. Segment-wise (not raw-string-prefix) so `/content` does not spuriously govern `/contentiousthing`. `/` denotes the doc root (a zone rooted there governs everything unzoned below it).
- **Nesting is allowed; innermost wins.** Two zones where one root prefixes the other both match a deep path — the longer (innermost) root is the governing zone. This lets a coarse outer zone hold a finer inner one without a parse-time exclusion rule.
- **Unzoned is distinct from every zone — and from other unzoned space for crossing purposes.** `zone_of` returns `None` for a path under no zone root; `crosses_zones(a, b)` is true whenever the two resolve to different governing zones, treating `None` as its own partition — so a move from inside a zone out to unzoned space (or between two unzoned subtrees that a later zone will separate) counts as crossing. `same_zone` is its negation. Pure `&Schema`, total (any path → a decision, never a panic), order-independent (depends only on the declared roots, not their parse order) — so replicas resolve identically.

## 2026-07-08 · SDK Unit 6a-iii · path façade exposes xml move — the mover + destination are path-addressed, the move forwards to the core tree-move log
**Changed:** third slice of Unit 6 (SDK surface); extends the `core::path` façade over the XML tree-move (Unit 2). No scope change.
- **A move names two elements by path + an index.** `xml_move(doc, elem_path, new_parent_path, index)` resolves the mover and the destination parent to their element ids by path (`XmlCursor::id`) and forwards to the core `move_xml`, which appends to the Kleppmann lamport-ordered parent-edge log (Unit 2). The façade adds no new op — it is a path-addressed front for the existing tree-move.
- **Inert on any unresolvable or illegal move.** A non-element mover or destination, a destination that cannot hold the mover, or a cycle-forming move (an element into its own subtree, which the core move-log rejects) emits empty ops — the same emptiness-as-effect contract 6a-i/6a-ii established, so a caller broadcasts nothing when the move can't apply.

## 2026-07-07 · Doc-level ACL slice 1 · the tuple CRDT set mirrors RangedElement 3a — storage-only, grantor as an explicit op field
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Ownership's doc-level ACL tuple as CRDT-merged document state. First slice of the Doc-level ACL-as-CRDT gate; records two cuts, no scope change.
- **The tuple set is structurally a RangedElement set with an ACL-tuple payload.** A document-level CRDT set keyed by a stamp-derived id under a fixed `crdtsync\0acl` namespace (mirroring ranged's `crdtsync\0ranged`), held on `Document` beside `ranged`, with `AclGrant`/`AclRevoke` ops (codec tags 19/20 after the ranged ops), a state-codec section id-sorted after the ranged set, and the same laws: concurrent grants union to distinct ids, a revoke tombstones (retained, delete-wins) and buffers until its grant, a local revoke of an unseen id emits nothing. The only shape difference from ranged: a tuple is **immutable** (no `set_payload`/LWW) — create + revoke are its whole lifecycle — so the entry needs no per-field stamp.
- **`grantor` is an explicit op field the caller sets, not derived from envelope authorship.** ARCHITECTURE §Ownership calls the grantor "the tuple's author … un-forgeable, since the op carries `actor_id`", but the core op deliberately carries only `{id, stamp, target, kind, tx}` (2026-07-02 · core op vs. wire envelope) — `actor_id` is a wire/server-envelope concern. So the ACL op carries `grantor: ClientId` as an explicit field the client/server sets to the authenticated actor's id; core stores it faithfully. The un-forgeability §Ownership describes is the **server's** job (it gates who may emit a grant and stamps the true grantor), not core's.
- **Slice 1 is storage + merge only — the merge is content-neutral.** Core stores any tuple that arrives and merges the set; it performs no authority check — no provenance-based revocation (who *may* revoke), no delegation/attenuation, no deny-precedence, no evaluation of a decision. Those are the evaluator/delegation slices (2–3, server-side). This keeps the CRDT engine pure: it is a grow-only set of immutable tuples + tombstones, convergent on its own, with the policy layered above at the server boundary. STATE_VERSION 7→8 (break format freely, pre-release — no migration).

## 2026-07-07 · SDK Unit 6a-ii · path façade addresses xml children — the children sequence is index-addressed off the element's path; no grandchild navigation
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Portable CRDT Core / §Multi-Language Support (the SDKs forward the `core::path` façade). Second slice of Unit 6, extends 6a-i. No scope change.
- **An element's/fragment's children are addressed by naming the element then an index — not by extending the path with a child key.** Unlike an attr (6a-i, addressed by a further path key into the attrs Map), a child of the children List has no map key: it is placed in a sequence and index-addressed, exactly as `list_insert(doc,path,index,val)` addresses a list item. So the new fns take the element `elem_path` plus an `index`: `xml_insert_element` / `xml_insert_text` (born empty then filled in the same transaction) / `xml_child_delete` / `xml_children_len`. Both XmlElement and XmlFragment own a children List, so all four accept either.
- **The write side resolves the element from its holding map, not from the leaf slot.** The path names the slot *holding* the element (not the element's own map, as the attrs case landed on). So the descent lands on the holding map and a new `MapCursor::xml_children(key)` reads that slot — an `Element::XmlElement` or `Element::XmlFragment` — and yields an `XmlChildrenCursor` over its children List id (`XmlElement::children_id` / `XmlFragment::children_id`). Mirrors 6a-i's `xml_attrs_id` seam: resolve the target container off the live slot rather than re-deriving it. A precheck (`slot_ok(is_xml_node)`) makes a write on a non-element/fragment target inert (empty ops), and `xml_child_delete` additionally prechecks the index is a live child so a no-op delete never materialises or re-stamps the List (the `list_delete` no-materialise contract).
- **No grandchild navigation — a fresh child has no stable path key.** An inserted child is index-addressed and its index shifts under sibling edits, so it has no path key of its own; this slice addresses the children List (insert/delete/len at the element level), not a nested child's attrs/children. In-place edit *into* an existing composite child stays deferred (5d-i established there is no in-place xml-child edit cursor). Move/marks are later slices (6a-iii/6a-iv).

## 2026-07-07 · SDK Unit 6a-i · path façade descends into XmlElement attrs — an element's attrs are addressed as a keyed sub-namespace, dead ends zero-op
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Portable CRDT Core / §Multi-Language Support (the SDKs forward the `core::path` façade). First slice of Unit 6. Records two forced realizations; no scope change.
- **An XmlElement's attrs are addressed by extending the path, not by a new attr op.** `core::path` resolved only nested Maps by key; an XmlElement in a slot stopped resolution. The fix teaches both the read walk (`resolve_map`) and the write descent (`MapCursor::child`/`into_child`, contextual via `xml_attrs_id`) to descend a further key into an element's attrs Map — an element's attrs *are* an ordinary keyed Map, so the existing `register`/`get_int`/`set_bytes`/… fns reach an attr by naming the element then the attr key. No attr-specific op, no path-model change — the façade stays key-framed. A fragment carries no attrs, so a key past it is unresolved (read) / a dead end (write).
- **A dead-end write must zero-op at any depth — the emptiness of the returned op vec is a caller signal.** The path fns return the ops to broadcast; a caller keys "did my write land / needs broadcast" off op-vec emptiness (the `list_delete` no-materialize precedent). So a write past a fragment must emit nothing — at ANY depth, not just when the fragment is the first parent. A single-walk descent that emits create-through `MapCreate`s as it goes and only discovers a deeper fragment mid-walk would emit phantom ancestor maps before aborting, breaking the contract (a self-review caught exactly this: the shallow `[frag,x]` case emitted zero ops but `[outer,frag,x]` emitted one). The resolution is a read-only `writable(doc, parents)` pre-check that walks the parents and refuses before any emit — the same slot-check-then-emit shape `list_delete`/`list_delete_id` already use. The pre-walk is deliberate (a deep dead-end needs look-ahead before the first emit); it is not a redundant second walk to be optimized away.

## 2026-07-07 · Zones Unit 1a · parse the schema `zones` block — a zone is a name → subtree root path, parse-only and enforcement-inert
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Zones ("A zone is declared in the schema (`zones` block) as a name → a subtree **root path**; every element under that path is in the zone, by structure. Static, ships with the schema, like `@auth`."). First slice of Zones Unit 1; splits the board's "Unit 1 — zone declaration" into 1a (parse, this PR) + 1b (cross-zone move/anchor rejection, next). Parse-only, mirrors the marks-parse (4a) / xml-type-parse (5a) arc; no runtime behavior beyond the schema surface. No scope change.
- **A zone entry is a bare path string, not an object.** `zones: { "<name>": "/subtree/root" }` — the minimal honest shape for "name → root path" (§Zones names no other per-zone field). The auth precedent stores a grant path the same way (a raw string, structural validation only), so a zone reuses it: `Schema.zones: Vec<(String, String)>`, order-preserving like marks/awareness, with `zones()` / `zone(name)` accessors. An object shape (`{ "root": "/x" }`) was rejected as premature — pre-release forward-compat is a non-goal and §Zones gives nothing else to carry.
- **Path validation is syntactic only, sharing the auth path grammar.** `validate_path` (was grant-only, `on:`-hardcoded in its error location) is generalized to take the full field location; a zone root is validated exactly as a grant `on:` path (absolute `/` or `/seg/seg…`, no empty segment → `BadPath`). It is **not** resolved against the type tree — matching the auth `on:` precedent, which validates paths syntactically and defers structural resolution to check time. Membership resolution (which elements fall under a zone root) and cross-zone move/anchor rejection are Unit 1b, needing the resolved tree.
- **Duplicate zone names need no schema-level check.** A zone name is a JSON object key, so a repeat is a `DuplicateKey` parse error from `core::json` — same as marks/awareness (no `DuplicateMark` kind exists). Only `auth.roles` carries a schema-level `DuplicateRole` because roles are a JSON array, where duplicates are legal JSON. Total-decode holds: a non-object block → `NotAnObject`, a non-string root → `WrongType`, a malformed path → `BadPath`; `hostile_inputs_never_panic` covers the new arms. `tests/schema.rs` +8 cases.

## 2026-07-07 · XmlElement Unit 5d-ii · marks value diff — a set-diff over the RangedElement annotation set, folded into `diff()` after the tree walk
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Schema-Aware-Diff ("attrs / marks / Map / Register / Counter show value diffs") — the annotation half of Unit 5d, completing 5d and **Unit 5**. Records the variant shape + the merge-join + the scalar-only deferral; no scope change.
- **Marks get their own path-less `Change` variants, not a reuse of the path-addressed tree ones.** A mark annotates a *sequence* by anchors (`RangeAnchor { seq, pos }`), not a tree slot — it has no path. So three new variants — `MarkAdded { id, seq, name, value }`, `MarkRemoved { id, seq, name, value }`, `MarkChanged { id, seq, name, old, new }` — each carrying the mark's stable `id`, the `seq` element its anchors resolve against, the `name`, and the scalar value(s). `diff()` folds `diff_marks` in **after** the tree walk (still one `Vec<Change>`): tree changes first, then the mark set, each deterministic on its own, no cross-dependency (a mark's `seq` may name a tree element also reported — that's fine, the consumer applies both).
- **Set-diff by stable id via a merge-join, not a hash join.** `ranged_elements()` returns entries id-sorted, so `diff_marks` walks the two id-sorted mark slices with a merge-join (`i`/`j` indices, `Ordering` match, trailing drains): `Less` (old id absent from new) = removed, `Greater` (new id absent from old) = added, `Equal` with a differing scalar = changed. Total-ordered by `id.as_bytes()`, so two replicas that merged the same ops produce the identical ordered mark-diff regardless of `ranged_elements()`'s internal iteration order. A removed mark pulls its `value`/`seq`/`name` from the **old** snapshot (it's gone from new — a `tx.ranged().delete` tombstones it out of `ranged_elements()`); a `set_payload` is an in-both value change; a re-set to the same value is silent (consistent with the register `Value` diff). The first cut of `diff_marks` used two `HashMap`s + a re-sort of already-sorted input — review-caught as over-engineered and refactored to the merge-join.
- **Scalar-payload marks only; a composite (object) mark is a correct deferral, not a dropped change.** `mark_views` filters `ranged_elements()` to `RangedElement { payload: RangedPayload::Scalar(value), name: Some(name), .. }`. A composite-payload mark (object flavor, a nested Map body) is skipped — but it is **unconstructible via the public API**: `tx.ranged().mark()` takes a `Scalar` only, and `create_map/list/text` pass `name: None` (a non-mark composite annotation). So there is no reachable object mark to diff; deep-diffing a composite mark body is the same virtual-container reachability model deferred elsewhere, and lands with the object-mark construction ergonomics (folded into Unit 6). A plain `name: None` annotation is not a mark and is correctly excluded.
- **wasm `change_to_js` must grow with the enum — the exhaustive match is the guard.** The wasm crate is workspace-excluded but CI's `wasm-sdk` job builds it; its `change_to_js` matches `Change` with no wildcard arm (deliberate — a new variant becomes a compile error, not a silent skip). The three mark variants broke that compile until `markAdd`/`markRemove`/`markChange` arms + a `set_mark_head` helper (id/seq as `Uint8Array` from `as_bytes()`, name as bytes) were added. Review-caught as a CONFIRMED break; the fix is the reason the no-wildcard match exists.

## 2026-07-07 · XmlElement Unit 5d-i · XmlElement/XmlFragment structural diff — the tree half of schema-aware diff
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Schema-Aware-Diff ("XmlElement subtrees produce structural diffs; attrs … show value diffs"). First slice of Unit 5d. Records the integration + a scoping realization; no scope change.
- **The xml diff is pure wiring over the existing walk — no new `Change` variant, no path-model change.** `diff_elem` gained `(XmlElement, XmlElement)` and `(XmlFragment, XmlFragment)` arms. An XmlElement's attrs are a keyed Map → `diff_map` (value diffs at the attr's key path); its children are a sequence → `diff_list` (structural `ListInsert`/`ListDelete` by stable node id, index carried in the change, `SeqItem::Composite(XmlElement|Text)`). A fragment is its children alone. This fixes a latent `unreachable!` **panic**: two XmlElements fell through `diff_elem`'s `_` arm into `scalar_of`, so diffing *any* xml-containing document panicked — no xml diff existed before.
- **A changed tag is a replace, not a field diff.** A tag is part of an element's identity (`XmlElement::node_id` is `(map_id, key, tag)`-seeded), so a different tag at the same slot is a different element. The xml arm compares tags first and emits `Removed{XmlElement}` + `Added{XmlElement}` when they differ, rather than diffing two unrelated elements' attrs/children. (A slot that swaps element↔fragment is already a kind mismatch, handled by `diff_elem`'s top guard.)
- **Sequence-composite survivor recursion (and the index-stepped path it needs) is DEFERRED — it has no drivable state under the current edit API.** The instinct was to also recurse `diff_list` into a *surviving* composite child so an in-place edit of a nested element/text surfaces at an index path (aligning the diff path with `validate::Step::Key|Index`). But the public tx/cursor API exposes **no way to edit an existing children-list child across a snapshot boundary**: `XmlChildrenCursor` only inserts/deletes (a child's id is stamp-seeded, not re-derivable by key), and a plain List holds only immutable scalars. So a surviving composite whose *contents* change is unreachable — there is nothing to diff and nothing to test. Every *reachable* xml change is either an attr value diff (the element itself survives at a map slot, already recursed via `diff_elem`) or a child structural insert/delete (`diff_list`, index in the change, no path step). Adding survivor recursion + the typed-step path now would be untested speculative code; it belongs with the unit that introduces xml-child in-place editing. Review-caught: `diff_list`'s long-standing doc-comment falsely claimed a live-in-both composite's inner content "surfaces at that item's path" — vacuous before (plain lists hold only immutable scalars) but newly misleading now that xml children (which can hold composites) route through `diff_list`; corrected the comment to state the surviving composite is not descended, with the recursion noted as the follow-up. 5d-ii (the marks half — mark value diffs over the annotation set) is the remaining 5d slice.

## 2026-07-07 · XmlElement Unit 5c-iii-b · per-type cardinality drop — an over-cap child of an allowed type drops, keeping the lamport-oldest
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Schema repair table ("Exclusive collision → keep lamport-oldest", `children.<T>.max`) — the enforcement half of 5c-iii, now that 5c-iii-a parses the cap. Records the integration; no scope change. Completes 5c-iii and the 5c structural-repair arc (disallowed-child drop · orphan-inline wrap · cardinality drop).
- **A cardinality excess reuses the drop path, not a bespoke repair.** For each child type `T` declared with a `max`, `queue_xml_children` counts the element's children resolving to `T`; the lamport-newest instances beyond `max` are the excess, each reported at its sequence position as new `ViolationKind::ExcessChild { max }` → `RepairKind::Dropped` + `RepairId::Drop { path }`. Structurally identical to `DisallowedChild` (a child that drops from the read), so it joins that arm in `keyed_repairs` — no new `RepairKind`, no element resolution (a drop reads nothing). An excess child is not descended, exactly like a disallowed one: a dropped subtree's own violations vanish with it.
- **Keep-oldest by stamp, the same order a sequence `max` uses.** The survivors are the `max` lamport-oldest of the covering set; the newest drop. Child stamps come from the children `List` (`node_ids`, index-aligned with `values()`), total-ordered by `(lamport, client)`, so replicas that merged the same ops keep the same instances — an exclusive type (`max` 1) deterministically collapses to one. This mirrors the sequence-`max` `survivors` logic (repair.rs), applied per child type instead of over the whole sequence; `max` 0 (allowed but no instances) drops all.
- **Excess is orthogonal to disallowed/orphan.** Only children that *resolve* to an allowed type (`resolve_child_type` = `Some`) participate in a cap; unresolved children stay `DisallowedChild`/`OrphanInline` as before. `tests/xml_schema.rs` +8 (conforming single, second reported, drop-is-by-stamp-not-position, unbounded-never-excesses, all-but-oldest-of-three, reads-dropped, zero-cap-drops-all, replica-convergence). Read-only, deterministic, Miri-clean. The `RepairId` `Step::Index` churn note (5b-i/5c-i) applies unchanged — a sequence-positioned drop, same deferred node-stamp follow-up.

## 2026-07-07 · XmlElement Unit 5c-iii-a · per-child-type `max` parse — the `children` allowlist becomes an object keyed by type
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Schema repair table ("Exclusive collision → keep lamport-oldest", declared by **`children.<T>.max`**) — the schema surface the exclusivity repair (5c-iii-b) reads. Parse-only, enforcement-inert; first slice of 5c-iii. No scope change (the repair table already pinned the declaration home).
- **"Exclusive" is a per-child-type cardinality cap, not a separate flag.** ARCHITECTURE declares exclusivity via `children.<T>.max` (e.g. `children.Heading.max = 1` = "at most one heading"), reusing the same keep-oldest/drop-newest mechanism as a sequence `max`. So no `exclusive` boolean is added; the `children` allowlist instead carries an optional per-type `max`.
- **`children` (xml) changes from an array to an object.** 5a parsed an xml type's `children` as `["Span", "Para"]` (a plain `Vec<String>` allowlist, via `parse_type_name_array`). To hang a per-type `max` off each entry it becomes an **object** `{ "Span": {}, "Heading": { "max": 1 } }` → `TypeDef::Xml.children: Vec<(String, Option<u64>)>` (type name → optional cap; empty object = allowed, uncapped). A new `parse_xml_children` mirrors `parse_children`/`parse_attrs` (object iteration, `reject_unknown_fields` per child value allowing only `max`, a negative `max` → `BadRange`). `marks` stays an array (no per-mark constraint). Break the schema format freely (pre-release).
- **The rename ripples to every child-name iterator, mechanically.** `resolve_child_type`/`queue_xml_children` (validate) and `validate_references` (schema closure) iterated the child type *names*; they now iterate `(name, _)` and are otherwise unchanged. The `max` is stored and closure-checked's reference target (`require(ty)` per child) is untouched; **no enforcement reads `max` yet** — the cardinality drop is 5c-iii-b. `tests/schema.rs` +3 (`max` parsed, negative rejected, unknown field under a child rejected) and the negative-child tests repurposed to the object form; all xml test schemas across `schema`/`xml_schema`/`xml_marks` converted array→object.

## 2026-07-07 · XmlElement Unit 5c-ii · orphan-inline wrap — loose inline text reads wrapped in a synthesized block with a derived id
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Invariant Repair ("Orphan inline → wrap in declared default block" + "Element-creating repairs use derived ids") — the one repair that introduces structure. Records the integration; no scope change.
- **The wrap is *described*, not materialized — consistent with the whole (observation-only) repair system.** Core's repair layer never materializes a repaired read: `repairs()` returns descriptions (`Clamped{value}` a number, `Truncated{keep}` the surviving indices, `Dropped` a marker) that the SDK applies. So the orphan wrap follows suit: loose inline text under a type declaring `repair.orphanInline` reads as a new `RepairKind::Wrapped { block, id }` — the declared block type name + the **derived** wrapper id — which the consumer builds. No materialized tree is produced in core (there is no repaired-read projection for *any* repair kind; that is a cross-cutting piece, not 5c-ii's). This is the key realization: the element-creating repair fits the existing path-based Violation/Repair model as a *description carrying the derived id*, exactly as `Truncated` carries `keep` indices — it does not need a bespoke materialization.
- **The wrapper id derives from the orphan's own element id, so it is position-stable.** `ElementId::derive(orphan.id(), block_bytes, XmlElement)` — the orphan Text's element id is already a stamp-seeded derived id (`xml_child_id`), position-independent, so the wrapper id is deterministic across replicas (`the_orphan_wrapper_id_is_deterministic_across_replicas`) and a later op can target it. Because the id, not the sequence position, is the identity, `RepairId::Wrap { id }` keys onRepaired by that id alone — it does **not** carry the `Step::Index`, so unlike `Drop`/`Clamp`/`Keep` it is immune to the preceding-insert index churn (the deferred node-stamp follow-up those still need).
- **Validate distinguishes orphan text from a disallowed child at the same "unresolved child" branch.** `queue_xml_children` (5c-i) reported every unresolved child `DisallowedChild`; it now splits: an unresolved **text** child under a type with `orphan_inline` declared → new `ViolationKind::OrphanInline { block }` (carries the declared block name), everything else → `DisallowedChild`. The orphan is still not descended (its own type is the synthesized wrapper's concern). `tests/xml_schema.rs` +3 (reported, reads-wrapped-in-the-derived-block, deterministic-id); the 5c-i orphan carve-out tests still hold (orphan text is not a `DisallowedChild`/`Dropped`, a disallowed *element* child under an orphan-inline type still drops). Read-only, deterministic. Exclusive-collision demote (needs a schema `exclusive` flag) is 5c-iii.

## 2026-07-07 · XmlElement Unit 5c-i · disallowed-child drop — an xml child whose tag no type allows drops from the read
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Invariant Repair ("Disallowed child → drop") + §Schema repair table — the first of the three structural rules, over the xml children sequence. Records the integration; no scope change.
- **The "not-descended" child of 5b-i becomes a reported, droppable violation.** 5b-i's `queue_xml_children` left a child that `resolve_child_type` couldn't place (its tag in no allowed child type) silently un-descended. It now emits a `ViolationKind::DisallowedChild` at the child's sequence position via a `Work::Report` (the same tree-order stack item attrs use), still without descending it — a dropped child's subtree is not validated, so its own nested violations vanish with it. The child resolves exactly as before when its tag *does* match; only the `None` branch changed from skip to report.
- **Structurally identical to the attr drop (5b-i), so it reuses that path whole.** `DisallowedChild` maps to `RepairKind::Dropped` + `RepairId::Drop { path }` in `keyed_repairs` — the reading (absent) is identified by location, and a children position is a `Step::Index` the existing `element_at` xml traversal already handles. No new `RepairKind`, no element resolution (a drop reads nothing). The `RepairId` `Step::Index` churn note (5b-i) applies unchanged — a sequence-positioned drop, same deferred node-stamp follow-up.
- **Shared by elements and fragments.** `queue_xml_children` serves both the XmlElement and XmlFragment arms, so a disallowed child under either is reported; emits in sequence order (LIFO over the reversed push). `tests/xml_schema.rs` +7. Read-only, deterministic. Orphan-inline wrap (element-creating) is 5c-ii; exclusive-collision demote (needs a schema `exclusive` flag) is 5c-iii.
- **Review-caught (CONFIRMED correctness):** dropping *every* unresolved child preempted 5c-ii's orphan-inline **wrap**. A type declaring `repair.orphanInline` (parse-valid since 5a) with loose inline text under it means "wrap this text in that block," i.e. **preserve** it — but 5c-i's blanket drop reported it `DisallowedChild` → `Dropped` the moment such a schema was bound, before 5c-ii lands, losing content the schema asked to keep. Fixed by carving out the orphan case: `queue_xml_children` now also takes the type's `orphan_inline`, and a child that resolves to no type is left **untouched** (not reported, as pre-5c-i) when it is inline **text** and the type declares `orphan_inline` — deferred to 5c-ii's wrap. The carve-out is text-only: a disallowed *element* child under an orphan-inline type still drops (orphan-inline is about inline text, not stray blocks). Regressions `loose_inline_text_under_an_orphan_inline_type_is_not_dropped` + `a_disallowed_element_child_under_an_orphan_inline_type_still_drops`. Also fixed `RepairId::Drop`'s doc, which still named only attributes.

## 2026-07-07 · XmlElement Unit 5b-ii · mark-on-disallowed-type filter — a mark reads active only when the containing XmlElement's type declares it
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Schema repair table ("mark on disallowed type → drop") — the read-time complement to 5b-i's attr drop, over the mark read model (4b). Records the integration; no scope change.
- **The filter lives in `marks_at` alone — it is a read convention, not a Violation/Repair.** A mark whose name is outside the containing element type's `marks` allowlist is dropped from the `marks_at` read; the `RangedElement` stays in state and every raw annotation read (`ranged_on`/`ranged_element`) is unfiltered. The path-based Violation/Repair model (5b-i) can't express it — a mark is a whole-`RangedElement` annotation targeting root, not an element at a tree path, so there is no location to key an `onRepaired` observation on. So no new `ViolationKind`/`RepairKind`; the drop is a `continue` in `marks_at`'s grouping loop, symmetric with the boolean-off omission already there.
- **The allowlist resolves by the *same contextual top-down walk* `validate` uses, not by the `parents` up-walk.** New `validate::marks_allowlist(doc, schema, seq) -> Option<&[String]>` descends from the root — map slot → child type, list item → `items`, xml child → tag-matched `resolve_child_type` — and returns the `marks` of the XmlElement that *directly holds* `seq`. The up-walk alternative (`parents[seq] → children-list → XmlElement`, then resolve that element's type) was rejected: recovering the element's type still needs the contextual root→element resolution (the same tag can be two types under different parents), and the map-slot hop the walk must cross doesn't store the slot key in `parents`. Reusing validate's descent (its now-`pub(crate)` `resolve_child_type`/`expected_kind`) keeps the one contextual-resolution path — the filter can't drift from what validate enforces.
- **No XmlElement container → no allowlist → keep every mark.** `marks_allowlist` returns `None` (not "drop all") when `seq` sits in a map slot, a plain list, or a tagless fragment. This is load-bearing: every existing `tests/marks.rs` body is a top-level map-slot Text, so the filter must be a no-op there. A **fragment** (`tag: None`) also returns `None` — a bare document-root container carries no mark concept, so reading its empty `marks` as "forbid everything" would silently strip all inline marks under a fragment; only an XmlElement (`tag: Some`) restricts marks. (If a later unit wants fragments to forbid marks, it makes that explicit.)
- **Resolved lazily, at most once per call.** The allowlist depends only on `seq` (the enclosing element), not on `index` or any mark, so `marks_at` resolves it on the first named mark and reuses it — a `RangedElement` set with no marks pays nothing for the tree walk, and a set with marks walks once. `tests/xml_marks.rs` (7): drop-disallowed, keep-allowed, mixed (only allowed survives), keep-on-plain-text, keep-under-fragment, keep-under-disallowed-tag-element, raw-set-unfiltered. The deferred `RepairId` node-stamp key (5b-i) stays deferred — a mark drop carries no `RepairId` at all, so it is untouched here.
- **Review dispositions (high `/code-review`):** (1) *A mark under a disallowed-tag element keeps every mark* — the type walk descends a child only when `resolve_child_type` matches its tag, so a mis-nested element (tag outside its parent's `children`) is never reached and its text has no allowlist. **Intended, and consistent with 5b-i:** the validator likewise does not descend a disallowed child (its own attrs aren't checked either); the disallowed element is structural repair's concern (5c), which drops it — its text, and the marks on it, go with it. Pinned by `a_mark_under_a_disallowed_tag_element_is_kept`. (2) *An unreachable container keeps every mark* — during a reorder window (the mark + text arrived, the parent element's op has not) or after the element's removal, the walk finds no XmlElement over `seq` and returns `None` → keep-all. **Intended:** matches 4b's accept-and-store (a mark resolves against what has arrived), and drop-all would be the worse default — it would hide the marks the type *does* allow; the state is transient and self-heals when the container op lands. (3) *Per-index `marks_at` re-walks the tree* — a per-character render calls `marks_at` N times, each an O(tree) resolve; the lazy gate above zeroes it for mark-free reads, but a mark-heavy render still pays O(N·tree). This is the same per-index-vs-batch tradeoff 4b already recorded (per-index `marks_at` is O(N·M·seq) at render); the fix is the deferred batch `marks_on(seq)` that resolves the allowlist and buckets every span once — the per-index query stays the semantic contract. (4) *`marks_allowlist` re-implements the validator's descent* — the divergence-prone rules (slot→type, tag-match, kind-map) are the *shared* `resolve_child_type`/`expected_kind`; only the ~30-line walk skeleton is duplicated. Unifying it into one contextual `id → type` resolver is deferred to 5c, which needs the same primitive (disallowed-child drop resolves a child's type the same way) — extracting it now, before its second caller exists, would guess the wrong shape.

## 2026-07-06 · XmlElement Unit 5b-i · attrs schema enforcement — the validator descends xml attrs + children, disallowed/mistyped attr drops at read
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Schema repair table ("disallowed / mistyped attr → drop") + §Invariant Repair — the validate/repair engine (schema Unit 2) never recursed into xml subtrees (5a left it inert). Records the integration; no scope change.
- **The validator resolves element→type *contextually as it walks*, so the xml arm gets the type for free.** There is no element-id→type registry; the walk already carries `type_name` per `Work` item. The new `(TypeDef::Xml, Element::XmlElement)` / `(_, XmlFragment)` arms descend the attrs Map against the type's `attrs` allowlist and the children sequence against `children`, resolving each child's declared type by **matching its `tag()` against the tags of the allowed child types** (`resolve_child_type`) — contextual, so a tag reused across types disambiguates by the parent's allowlist. A text child matches an allowed text-kind type.
- **An attr key→type is structurally a Map slot→type, so a right-kind attr value reuses the built-primitive path.** A declared attr whose value is the correct kind is queued as ordinary `Work::Check` against its attr type — an out-of-range register/counter attr then falls into the existing `AboveMax`/`BelowMin` → `Clamped` path with no new logic.
- **A disallowed key and a mistyped value are *new, droppable* violations, not the existing non-repairable ones.** `UnknownSlot` (map) and `KindMismatch` map to `return None` in repair (reported, never fixed), but a bad attr must *drop* at read. So new `ViolationKind::DisallowedAttr` (key outside the allowlist) and `ViolationKind::MistypedAttr { expected, found }` (declared key, wrong-kind value — checked in the xml arm *before* recursing, so a mistype never reaches the generic `KindMismatch`), both → new `RepairKind::Dropped` + `RepairId::Drop { path }` (the reading — absent — is identified by location alone).
- **Children recursion is plumbing for nested attrs, not disallowed-child enforcement.** The arm descends every child that resolves to an allowed type (so a nested element's own attrs are validated) and simply does not descend a child that resolves to none — the disallowed-child *drop* is 5c. This keeps 5b-i scoped to attrs while sharing the tag→type resolver with 5c.
- **Read-only, deterministic, total.** The walk still never mutates and stays index/key-ordered, so replicas converge on the same violation set (regression `two_replicas_..._produce_the_same_violations`). `tests/xml_schema.rs`. The mark-on-disallowed-type drop is 5b-ii.
- **Review-caught (two fixes + one scoped-out):** (1) `element_at` (repair's path→element resolver) only walked Map/List, so a `TooLong` located *through* an xml element (a bounded text child) resolved to nothing and got no repair — a closure break. Fixed: `element_at` traverses XmlElement (attr via `Step::Key` into its attrs Map, child via `Step::Index` into its children List) and XmlFragment (children). Regression `an_over_max_text_child_reads_truncated_through_xml`. (2) attr violations were pushed straight to the output during the reversed attr scan, landing reverse-ordered and ahead of children — deviating from the documented sorted depth-first order (convergence held, but the contract didn't). Fixed with a `Work::Report` stack item (like `Work::UnknownSlot`), so a found-while-queueing violation emits in tree order; children are queued before attrs so attrs (sorted) precede children (sequence). Regression `disallowed_attrs_emit_in_sorted_key_order`. (3) A repair under a *sequence position* (an xml child of a bounded type — or, already on main, a bounded register list item) carries a `Step::Index` in its `RepairId`, so a preceding insert/remove shifts the id and can churn an `onRepaired` report though the reading is unchanged. This is **pre-existing** (list-item clamps already do it) and keying such a repair by a stable node stamp is the same follow-up for both cases — out of 5b-i's attrs scope; the `RepairId` doc now states the limitation honestly (keying every repair by `Element::id()` was rejected: a register/counter resolves to a `Scalar`, which has no id).

## 2026-07-06 · XmlElement Unit 5a · schema XmlElement/XmlFragment type parse — the missing type kind every enforcement rule needs
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Schema (the repair table's `children` / `attrs` / type-`marks` allowlists + `repair.orphanInline`) — the schema layer (Units 1–8) parsed types over map/list/text/register/counter only, so no enforcement rule of Unit 5 (disallowed/mistyped attr → drop, mark on disallowed type → drop, disallowed child → drop, orphan inline → wrap) had a type to read from. First slice of Unit 5; parse-only, enforcement-inert, mirrors the 4a / whole schema-parse arc. No scope change.
- **One `TypeDef::Xml` variant covers both an element and a fragment; the `tag` discriminates.** `Xml { tag: Option<String>, children: Vec<String>, attrs: Vec<(String, String)>, marks: Vec<String>, orphan_inline: Option<String> }`. `kind: "xml"` → an element (`tag` **required** — it names the element's tag, and the orphan-wrap repair mints a wrapper of a declared block *type* whose tag comes from here); `kind: "fragment"` → the tagless document-root container (`tag: None`, and `attrs`/`marks` structurally rejected, since a fragment carries neither — `reject_unknown_fields` allows only `kind`/`children`/`repair`). Modeling both as one variant keeps the kind→`ElementKind` map a pattern on `tag` (`Some` → XmlElement, `None` → XmlFragment) and avoids a parallel fragment variant with mostly-empty fields.
- **`children` is an allowlist of type *names* (an array), not List's single `items`.** An element's children sequence holds several types (block elements + text), so `children: ["Para", "Heading", "Span"]` — distinct from `List { items }` (one element type). `attrs` mirrors a Map's `children` (key → value type name); `marks` is an array of mark names. All three default to empty when absent.
- **Reference closure extends to marks.** `validate_references` now requires an xml type's `children` / `attrs` value types / `orphan_inline` block to be declared types (`UnknownTypeRef`), and its `marks` allowlist to name marks declared in the top-level `marks` block — a new `UnknownMarkRef` kind (the marks-allowlist analogue of `UnknownTypeRef`). So a parse-accepted schema still can't reference an undeclared type *or* mark, preserving the closure guarantee.
- **`repair.orphanInline` is nested under a `repair` object** (not a bare top-level type field) so the repair-directive namespace has room to grow (future per-type repair knobs) without colliding with structural fields; an unknown key under `repair` fails loud like every other level.
- **Enforcement is inert here.** `validate`'s `expected_kind` gains the two xml kinds (so an xml element of a declared xml type isn't a false `KindMismatch`), but no xml children/attrs/marks constraint is checked and the walk does not recurse into xml subtrees yet — that is 5b (attrs + marks enforcement) and 5c (structural repair). Total-decode holds (`hostile_inputs_never_panic` covers the new arms). `tests/schema.rs` +17.

## 2026-07-06 · XmlElement Unit 4b · the mark read model — marks are a read-time convention over the RangedElement set, no new op, no per-char storage
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Marks ("A mark is a RangedElement whose payload carries the mark name + value... the active marks on a character are computed from the set... per that name's declared flavor... No per-character mark storage... converges by construction"). Second/final slice of Unit 4; completes the XmlElement/RangedElement/marks epic. Records the integration the read forced; no scope change.
- **A mark is a named RangedElement — the name is a new field, not a payload convention.** `RangedCreate` / `RangedElement` / the `RangedEntry` state record gain a `name: Option<Vec<u8>>` (None = a plain 3a/3b annotation, `Some` = a mark). The alternative — a `{name, value}` Map payload (reuse 3b composite) — was rejected: it makes every boolean mark a heap container, and the read would resolve a payload map per covering range to filter by name. A field lets the read filter by name directly and keeps a boolean mark a bare named scalar. The value rides the existing scalar payload (`RangedInit::Scalar`) — its `payload_stamp` is the LWW clock, so no separate create-stamp is stored. An object mark's structured body is the 3b composite payload under the same name (the `mark()` helper authors a scalar mark; a composite-bodied mark is `create_map` + a name — a follow-up ergonomic).
- **The active marks on a character are a pure read over the set, no stored state.** `Document::marks_at(seq, index) -> Vec<ResolvedMark>` gathers every live (non-tombstoned) named range whose resolved span covers `(seq, index)`, groups by name, and combines per the name's schema `MarkFlavor`: **boolean** → present iff the highest-`payload_stamp` covering range says present (`scalar_is_present`: a `Bool` decides, any other scalar = present) — concurrent add+remove is LWW-by-stamp; **value** → the highest-`payload_stamp` covering range's scalar (else `Null`); **object** (also the default for an unschema'd or non-UTF8 name) → the id-sorted set of every covering instance, so overlapping comments coexist. `Stamp` is a total order (lamport then client), so the LWW `max_by_key` never ties across distinct ranges; output is name-sorted and object ids id-sorted → identical across replicas by construction. `core::marks::{MarkState, ResolvedMark}`.
- **Span coverage is `resolve(start) <= index < resolve(end)` — half-open, same-sequence.** Each anchor resolves through the annotated sequence via a presence-aware `resolve_position_present` (Text then List) that yields `None`, not a clamped boundary, when its anchor codepoint is absent. This is load-bearing: a `RangedCreate` is accept-and-store, so a mark can apply *before* the inserts carrying its span's codepoints — the plain `resolve_position` collapses an absent `After`/`Before` anchor onto `0`/`len`, which would make the mark spuriously cover the whole current text during the reorder window. `None` on either anchor → covers nothing until the codepoints arrive (matches 3a's "resolve yields nothing until the sequence arrives", extended to the individual codepoints). A cross-element range (`start.seq != end.seq`) covers nothing here — deferred to 4b-ii. An inverted or zero-width span covers nothing (fine).
- **`marks_at` returns only the marks *on* the character.** A boolean whose LWW-winning covering range is a remove combines to `Boolean(false)` and is omitted from the result — the read is "the active marks", so a removed mark is absent, never surfaced as a present-but-false entry (a consumer keying on a name's presence must never render removed formatting).
- **Anchor gravity IS the mark's expansion — the read is gravity-agnostic.** The caller picks the start/end anchor gravity (a `Side::Left` start / `Side::Right` end = grow-both; `Right`/`Left` = no-grow) from the schema's `expand` (4a); `resolve_position` already honors it, so a boundary insert lands inside or outside the resolved span with no new mechanism. Binding `expand` → authored gravity automatically is deferred; the read needs nothing for it.
- **`STATE_VERSION` 6→7.** The ranged record encodes `name` (a present-flag + bytes, `put_opt_bytes`/`opt_bytes`) before the tombstone flag; a mark's name and value round-trip because the RangedElement set round-trips (the mark set is the only source of truth — a snapshot preserves marks with no per-char storage, asserted by `marks_survive_a_snapshot`). Break compat freely (pre-release).
- **Deferred (4b-ii / Unit 5, not bugs):** a cross-element span (a comment across paragraphs); the object-flavor composite-body ergonomics beyond coexistence; auto-deriving authored anchor gravity from schema `expand`. **Rendering perf:** `marks_at(seq, index)` rescans the whole annotation set and re-resolves both anchors (each an O(sequence) walk) per call, so painting an N-char text with M marks is O(N·M·sequence) — correct, but a whole-document render wants a batch `marks_on(seq)` that buckets each range's resolved `[start, end)` once. Left as an additive read-surface optimization for the marks/diff surface work (Unit 5); the per-index query is the semantic contract and stays.

## 2026-07-06 · XmlElement Unit 4a · schema `marks` — model the declared-but-ignored block, value-shape deferred
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Marks + §Schema ("`marks` (name → merge flavor + anchor expansion + value shape)") — models the top-level `marks` schema block that was accepted-and-ignored (a reserved TOP_LEVEL_KEY). Parse-only, mirrors the awareness (3a #138) / auth (4b #145) precedents; no runtime behavior beyond the schema surface. First slice of Unit 4 (marks); the read model is 4b.
- **A mark declares a merge `flavor` (required) + an anchor `expand` (optional).** `flavor` ∈ boolean (LWW-by-stamp presence) | value (LWW value) | object (independent instances), per §Marks. `expand` ∈ none | before | after | both maps to the gravity of the range's start/end anchors (§Extensibility: "gravity = anchor expansion"); it **defaults to None** (conservative link-like: no growth unless declared), overridden per mark that should grow (bold = both). Both are string enums, rejected outside their vocabulary (`UnknownFlavor`/`UnknownExpand`), matching the auth `UnknownAction`/`UnknownEvent` style.
- **The mark's value shape is NOT modelled here — deferred**, exactly as grant value-shape enforcement was deferred past the auth parse (4b). 4a captures flavor + expand (what the read model 4b needs to combine marks); validating that a value/object mark's payload matches a declared shape is a later check-time concern.
- **Scope: the top-level `marks` block only.** The per-type `marks` allowlist (a type-def field — "Mark on disallowed type → drop", ARCHITECTURE repair table) is a separate enforcement concern, out of this slice.

## 2026-07-06 · XmlElement Unit 3b · RangedElement composite payload — a virtual-container range holding a Map/List/Text at a derived id
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §CRDT Model ("recursive payload") + §Marks (an object-flavored mark stores a structured value) — generalizes 3a's `Scalar` payload to a nested Element. Records the integration the code forced; no scope change.
- **The payload flavor is fixed at create: a leaf `Scalar` or a composite container kind.** `RangedCreate` carries `RangedInit { Scalar(Scalar) | Composite(ElementKind) }`; a composite payload is one of Map / List / Text (Register/Counter live in a Map slot, Xml nodes in a sequence — a structured payload nests them inside one of the three). A scalar payload keeps the 3a LWW path (`RangedSetPayload` is inert against a composite — a composite is edited through its container, never replaced). Changing flavor is a delete + create, like re-ranging.
- **The payload container installs at `payload_id = derive(range_id, "payload", kind)`, parent = the RangedElement**, registered in the same `maps`/`lists`/`texts` registries as any container and edited by the ordinary container ops targeting that id. Reuses `registered_handle` + the retention/displacement machinery wholesale — no parallel payload store. The id derives under the range id (itself a stamp-derived UUID under the `crdtsync\0ranged\0` namespace), so it cannot collide with a user map slot (whose parent is a user map).
- **A RangedElement is a virtual container in the reachability model.** `displaced_container` reports a *materialised* range (present in the set, tombstoned or not) as installed; `resolvable` treats its parent as the root. So a payload resolves through its range — an op targeting the payload buffers only until the range's *create* materialises it (single-op `ready` via `resolvable`, and `tx_group_ready` marks the payload created by an in-group composite create). **Delete-wins is a read-layer filter, not a reachability break:** a tombstoned range hides its payload from `ranged_payload`/`ranged_elements`, but the payload container stays reachable, so a peer edit that *raced* the delete applies to the retained-hidden container instead of buffering. This matters — `encode_state` serializes the buffer, so a permanently-buffered op (a range never un-deletes) would leak unboundedly and desync the deleting replica's snapshot from the editor's; applying to the hidden container converges both the reads (both hide the range) *and* the payload bytes. The payload container is never separately displaced on delete (per-slot displacement never propagates to a child), and `mark_displaced` seeds every materialised range's payload id (tombstoned included) so it decodes with the same installed flag on every replica.
- **`mark_displaced` (decode) seeds the installed set with each live range's composite payload id** — the payload is held by its range, not a map slot or sequence node, so the slot/node scans miss it; its own nested containers are then picked up by the map/list scans. A tombstoned range's payload is left out (stays displaced).
- **`STATE_VERSION` 5→6.** A ranged record's payload is tagged: `0` a scalar (value + LWW stamp, as 3a), `1` a composite (the container kind; the id is derived, the data rides the map/list/text registries + the parent-link section). Break compat freely (pre-release).
- **API:** `RangedPayload { Scalar | Composite { id, kind } }` read view (`RangedElement::scalar()` for the common leaf read) + `Document::ranged_payload(id)` (the composite handle) + `RangedCursor::create_map/list/text` and `payload_map/list/text` (each gated on a live range of the matching kind, mirroring the `set_payload`/`delete` local-emit guard). `creates_container()` now classifies a composite `RangedCreate` as `true` (its payload gets a keylessly-targeted derived id) and a scalar one as `false`.
- **Deferred:** Xml (element/fragment) payloads (a Map/List payload already nests them); anchor→index resolution; the shared cross-primitive fuzz oracle (3b carries its own convergence fuzz + snapshot round-trip).

## 2026-07-06 · XmlElement Unit 3a · RangedElement — a document-level keyed set with opaque anchors, accept-and-store creates
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §CRDT Model + §Marks (the RangedElement primitive) for the built sequences (Text/List); records the integration the code forced. Payload is a `Scalar` here — a composite/recursive payload is 3b. No scope change.
- **The annotation set is a document-level registry keyed by RangedElement id, not stored in the sequence it annotates** (ARCHITECTURE §CRDT Model). A `Document.ranged: HashMap<id, RangedEntry>`; "the ranges on this sequence" is `ranged_on(seq)`, a query filtered by an endpoint's `seq`. Concurrent creates union to distinct ids, so nothing is lost.
- **Endpoints are fixed at create; a re-range is delete + create.** The create op carries `start`/`end`; there is no set-endpoint op. The payload is the only mutable field (LWW-by-stamp). This keeps the op set minimal and the merge trivial (a keyed set of immutable-endpoint entries with an LWW leaf).
- **Delete wins over a concurrent payload change.** A deleted entry is tombstoned, not removed — retained in the set (and the snapshot) so a concurrent or late `RangedSetPayload` can't resurrect it, mirroring the sequence-tombstone rule.
- **A create is accept-and-store — it is NOT gated on its endpoints' sequences existing.** `apply` stores the entry with *opaque* anchors and never touches the named sequence, so applying a create before (or without) its sequence is harmless and converges; resolving an anchor to a live index is a separate read that simply yields nothing until the sequence arrives. Only `RangedSetPayload`/`RangedDelete` have a real dependency — the create that carries the entry — so those buffer until the ranged id is present (single-op `ready` + `tx_group_ready`), else the change would apply against a missing entry and be lost. This differs from `XmlMove`, which gates on its node because `apply_move` *needs* the materialised node; a ranged create needs nothing.
- **The RangedElement id derives from the create op's stamp under a fixed `crdtsync\0ranged\0` namespace** — globally unique (every replica agrees, concurrent creates differ) and, via the dedicated namespace, guaranteed distinct from any user map-slot id, so no new `ElementKind` is needed (a RangedElement is not a slot-holdable value).
- **`STATE_VERSION` 4→5.** The whole set (tombstoned entries included) persists after the tree-move placements, id-ordered; endpoints encode as `(seq id, RelativePosition)`, payload as a `Scalar`, plus the LWW stamp and tombstone flag. Break compat freely (pre-release).
- **Deferred to later slices:** a composite/recursive payload (3b); resolving an anchor to a concrete `(start, end)` index pair over the live sequence (a read helper for Unit 4/consumers); and RangedElement arms in the shared cross-primitive fuzz oracle (3a carries its own convergence fuzz + snapshot round-trip, and the set is independent of the primitive tree).

## 2026-07-06 · XmlElement Unit 2 (2a/#201, 2b/#202) · tree move — a lamport-ordered move log over Fugue placements, not a re-representation of children
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Tree Moves (Kleppmann 2021: lamport-ordered apply, undo-and-replay, one-parent/no-cycle/no-dup/deterministic). ARCHITECTURE pinned the *algorithm* but not how it maps onto crdtsync's children (a Fugue List of composite node values); this records the integration the code forced. No scope change.
- **The move log is a separate overlay, not a change to how children are stored.** A child stays a Fugue node in a children List (1c) whose value refs the child's registry element by its stable id (1d's composite `NodeRef`). A move never rewrites that; it *adds* a second placement (a Fugue node referencing the same element id) in the destination list and lets a lamport-ordered log (`core::treemove::TreeMoves`, 2a) decide which single placement of a node renders. This keeps identity + subtree free (they live once in the registry, keyed by the element id) and reuses List/Fugue wholesale. The alternative — making a node's parent a movable pointer and re-deriving the tree at read — would have rewritten every XML children read (fingerprint, diff, state codec, cursors); rejected.
- **Which placement renders is a reversible per-node `moved_away` flag on the List node, driven by a fold — not a tombstone.** Live reads skip a moved-away node; the Fugue tree keeps it (it still anchors positions). The document re-folds after each move (and after a delete of a placement): a node's live placement is the highest-stamped placement in its effective-parent's children list; all others are moved-away. This is provably the governing move because a cyclic move never lands a placement in an ancestor list, so it can't pollute the effective-parent list. The fold is full-O(placements) per move by design: one move's undo-and-replay can shift several nodes' effective parents, so a scoped refold would need the log to report the changed set (deferred).
- **The move log carries a static base-parent map (from the creates), so cycle detection sees the whole tree.** The log holds only moves, but a move under a node's *created* (never-moved) descendant is still a cycle; without the base edges the ancestor walk would miss it. `parent_of` falls back move→base; `is_ancestor` walks both. Base edges are re-derivable from the creates, so they are not persisted with the log.
- **Delete wins over a concurrent move.** A node with any tombstoned placement is hidden entirely (the fold), rather than resurrecting under the move's destination — a `ListDelete` re-folds. A move-to-trash model (delete as a stamp-ordered move) is the alternative; delete-wins is simpler, convergent, and matches user intent, and is recorded as the chosen semantics (revisitable if a trash root is wanted).
- **A cyclic move still inserts its (hidden) placement** (a later reorder may make it live), so a node's own subtree can hold an `Rc` back to it — a cycle. `Document::drop` now clears List nodes too (not only Map slots), since composite List nodes hold child `Rc`s and can close such a cycle; clearing maps alone leaked (Miri-caught).
- **A same-parent reorder discounts the node's own still-live slot** (`List::place_excluding`) so a forward move is not off by one; a move is only defined for a node with a children placement (a map-slot root is a consistent no-op).
- **2c (state codec) — the snapshot persists the move log + the placements it can't rebuild, and re-derives everything else.** `moved_away` is never encoded (a derived overlay recomputed from the replayed log), and the base map is not encoded either (re-derived on decode: a node's birth placement is the one whose `(list, stamp)` reproduces its element id, and its owner is the birth list's parent). Placements are stored **only when unrecoverable from the decoded list** — a moved node (more than one placement) or a node with a tombstoned placement (its composite value is dropped by tombstone compression). A node with a single live placement — created, never moved, not deleted — is reconstructed from its live children-list node, so a move-free XML snapshot carries zero placement records. On decode, after replaying the log and refolding, `reject_parent_cycles` is re-run: replay mutates the parent relation after decode's initial acyclicity check, so a crafted snapshot whose moves fold into a cycle is rejected at decode rather than hanging a later `resolvable` walk.

## 2026-07-06 · XmlElement Unit 1d · state codec — tagged sequence node values + a two-phase list decode + a per-slot displacement restore
**Changed:** realizes the persistence half of ARCHITECTURE §CRDT Model's XmlElement/XmlFragment; no scope change. Makes an XML tree round-trip through `Document::encode_state`/`decode_state`, replacing the `unreachable!` asserts 1a/1b left in the map-slot and sequence-node encode paths. `STATE_VERSION` 2→3 (format break, taken freely pre-release — no migration).
- **Every sequence node value is now tag-prefixed** (`list.rs`): the first byte is the `ElementKind` tag, so a scalar (tag 0, inlined as before) is told from a composite (tags 2..=7, a kind-tagged reference to the child's id) with no separate discriminant — the sequence codec now mirrors the map-slot codec. The per-node byte is negligible against the stamp+anchor already stored per node, and it lets a children List hold `XmlElement`/`Text` nodes. A bare `List::decode_state` and `Text` reject any composite reference (they are scalar-only); a register in a sequence node is `unreachable!`.
- **List decode became two-phase, like Map.** Because a sequence node may now reference a registry container, `List::decode_state_from` returns `(List, Vec<NodeRef>)` — the composite nodes hold a placeholder until the document resolves them once every registry exists. `read_state` builds all shells (counters, list shells + collected refs, texts, map shells, then the XML registries) and only then resolves map slots and sequence-node refs through the shared `resolve_ref` (extended with `XmlElement`/`XmlFragment` arms + the two XML registries). An element's attrs Map and children List are **not** re-encoded inside its record — they ride the map/list registries under their derived ids, and the decoded element shares those exact handles (`from_registry`), so an op targeting a half reaches the same container.
- **Displacement is per-slot, so the restore scan stays flat — it must not walk reachability.** Pre-XML, every container hung off a map slot, so `mark_displaced` scanned map live-values. Now a container can also hang off a **composite sequence node** (an XML child), so the scan additionally installs every list's live composite values; an XML node's attrs Map and children List are intrinsic to the node (never slot-held), so they follow the node's own flag in a single propagation pass after the map/list scans have settled each node. The scan installs a container iff *some* parent holds it live now, **independent of that parent's own reachability** — a nested child of a displaced ancestor keeps its own flag clear, so re-winning the ancestor restores the subtree. A reachability walk from the root is wrong here: it would inherit an ancestor's displacement down to a live child and lose the child's writes on a reloaded replica (the regression `a_nested_container_under_a_displaced_one_reconverges_after_a_snapshot` pins this). The XML node registries persist so a displaced XML subtree is retained across a snapshot exactly like a displaced counter/map.

## 2026-07-05 · XmlElement Unit 1b · create + attrs through ops — tag folds into the child id; the reused halves are first-class registry containers
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §CRDT Model's XmlElement/XmlFragment over the op layer; no scope change. First behavioral slice on 1a's in-memory types (#197): create an XML node in a map slot + edit its attrs. Two design points the op path forced, plus a re-slice.
- **The `tag` participates in the element's derived id** (`derive(derive(map_id, key, XmlElement), tag, XmlElement)`), not just as an immutable field. ARCHITECTURE already says "a retag is a replace, not a mutation" — over ops that must mean *distinct identity*: two replicas that concurrently create the same key with different tags would otherwise share one derived id and one retained handle, and whichever tag each saw first would stick → divergence. Folding the tag into the id makes them two elements the slot's LWW resolves (winner installed, loser displaced+retained), convergent by construction. A fragment is tagless, so its id is the plain `derive(map_id, key, XmlFragment)`.
- **An element's attrs Map and children List are registered in the document's own `maps`/`lists` registries** (flattened, not nested inside the XmlElement record), under ids derived from the element id. This is what lets attr edits reuse the existing `MapSet`/`RegisterSet`/`MapDelete` ops unchanged — they target the attrs Map by its derived id like any other map — and is why 1b needs no new attr op. The node also gets `xml_elements`/`xml_fragments` identity registries (retained across displacement like every container), and displacement propagates to the halves so a displaced subtree's Map/List read displaced too, keeping `resolvable` honest. Parent links `attrs→element`, `children→element`, `element→containing-map` make the halves reachable up to the root.
- **Re-sliced (was 1b=codec, 1c=ops): ops land before the state codec.** Each XML op slice is testable through the public op API + the convergence harness, whereas the state codec alone cannot build an XML tree to round-trip (no public constructor without ops). New order: **1b** create+attrs (this), **1c** children sequence (composite List nodes) + text runs, **1d** state codec (list-node ref generalization, tree registries, `STATE_VERSION` 2→3). Until 1d, no XML value reaches `encode_state`, so the map-slot / sequence-node XML encode paths stay the `unreachable!` asserts 1a placed.

## 2026-07-05 · Auto-version Unit 4 · schedule triggers `every: <duration>` — sweep-driven, arm-then-fire, no catch-up burst
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Auto-Version Triggers' "`every: <duration>` is a schedule, driven by the `Clock` seam + periodic sweep already used for the awareness grace window"; no scope change. Completes the auto-version trigger vocabulary (event triggers were Unit 3/3b).
- **The schedule fires from the existing sweep, off one `Clock` read.** `Registry::sweep` (the awareness grace/TTL sweep) gains a `fire_schedule_triggers(now)` pass after `reconcile_room_apps`, so schedules ride the same tick and clock the runtime already drives — no separate timer thread. Only bound rooms are considered (a relay room has no governing schema), and the schema is the room's *governing* binding (`room_apps`), not a connection's self-declared app — consistent with how `on:` triggers and awareness TTLs resolve.
- **Arm-then-fire, never on the binding sweep.** The first sweep that sees a `(room, schedule)` records its last-fire as `now` without capturing; it captures only once `now - last_fire >= interval`. So `every: 1h` does not snapshot the instant a room binds — it waits a full interval. Last-fire is tracked per `(room, schedule-origin)` in `Registry.schedule_fires`.
- **At most one capture per sweep — no catch-up burst.** When a schedule is due, last-fire is set to `now` (not advanced by `+= interval`), so a long gap between sweeps (a paused or slow server) yields exactly one capture on the next sweep, not one per missed interval. The schedule drifts by up to a sweep interval; a burst of retroactive snapshots is the worse failure.
- **A schedule's identity is `(interval, template)`, distinct from any `on:` origin.** `schedule_origin(millis, template)` is `every\0<millis>\0<template>` — its leading `every` field is no event kebab, so a schedule and an `on:` trigger that render the same name never share a retention window. Two schedules with the same name but different periods keep independent windows; `keep` prunes each via the same provenance retention as event triggers (Unit 3b).
- **A scheduled capture does not cascade, and a rebound room re-arms.** The sweep sets the sink's `draining` latch around its captures (as the post-delivery drain does), so a scheduled version's `VersionCreated` never re-fires an `on: version-created` trigger. `schedule_fires` entries for rooms no longer bound are pruned each sweep, so a room that goes dormant and later rebinds arms afresh rather than firing on a stale timer. The event-capture path was refactored to a shared `capture_version(room, name, origin, keep)` the schedule path reuses (name + origin computed by each caller).
- **Hardening (review):** a **zero interval is rejected at parse** (`parse_duration_millis`, core) — `every: 0s` would fire every sweep and flood versions, so it fails loud like any malformed duration. The fire decision **reads the last-fire map at sweep start and defers stamping** to after the loop, so two schedules sharing a key (same interval + name) do not shadow each other — both are considered and the tighter `keep` governs, exactly as the event-side name-collision rule. A **backward clock step re-arms** (`now < last` stamps `now` without firing) rather than stalling the schedule for the whole regression. The scan runs **unconditionally each sweep** (bounded by live bindings, cached schema parses) rather than behind the `is_armed` latch: arming happens *inside* `parsed_schema`, so a room upgraded to a schedule-bearing version under an injected awareness policy (which skips the other schema-resolving sweep pass) is armed only by this scan itself — gating it on `is_armed` stranded that schedule. The version-name contract is shared with event triggers: a name is an insert-if-absent handle, so a recurring schedule templates a uniquifier (`${timestamp}`); a static schedule name captures once, like a static event-trigger name (unchanged from #193).

## 2026-07-05 · Auto-version Unit 3b · retention window `keep` — durable per-version provenance + a monotonic capture ordinal
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Auto-Version Triggers' "`keep: N` prunes the oldest auto-versions of that trigger (the retention-window mechanism)", the piece split off Unit 3; no scope change. Closes the retention that three heuristics failed to do correctly in Unit 3's review rounds.
- **Retention is provenance-based, not name- or memory-based — it is the only sound design.** Each `Version` gains an `origin: Option<Vec<u8>>` (the authoring trigger's identity, `None` for a manual version) and a monotonic `ordinal: u64` stamped by the hub. `Hub::retain_by_origin(room, origin, keep)` keeps the newest `keep` versions of that origin (ordered by ordinal) and deletes the rest. This fixes every heuristic's flaw at once: it never matches a manual version (origin `None`) or a differently-named trigger (distinct origin), and it orders by capture, not the wall-clock name — so a backward NTP step cannot make the newest capture sort oldest and be pruned.
- **A trigger's identity is `(event, template)`, NUL-joined.** Two triggers that render the same name under *different* events (`on: subscribe` and `on: compaction`, both `snap/${timestamp}`) keep independent windows — the Unit-3-review collision where the smaller `keep` destroyed the other's captures. Two genuinely identical triggers share one window (correct — they are the same trigger). The identity is the retention key, decoupled from the rendered name.
- **Provenance + ordinal persist, so retention survives a restart.** The `<room>.versions` store record gains a 1-byte origin present-flag (+ the origin bytes when present) and the 8-byte ordinal — a format break taken freely pre-release, no old-file migration. On load, `Hub::version_ordinal` resumes past the highest persisted ordinal, so a post-restart capture never predates a restored one. This is exactly what the abandoned in-memory tally could not do (it reset across dormancy/restart, orphaning the persisted captures) — the reason provenance had to be durable, proven by a store-reopen test.
