- **`keep: 0` retains nothing → the capture is skipped (no create-then-delete churn); `keep: none` retains all (no pruning).** Retention runs on each capture; a *lowered* `keep` (or a removed trigger) takes effect on that trigger's next capture, not retroactively at a sweep — a bounded, documented lag, not unbounded growth (a trigger that stops firing stays at the `keep` it last pruned to). Manual `create_version` stays a 2-arg call (origin `None`), so its callers and every existing test are untouched; the auto path uses `create_auto_version(room, name, origin)`.
- **Renaming an auto-capture detaches it from its trigger's window.** A rename is a deliberate operator act — the version becomes curated, so `rename_version` clears its `origin`; a later capture's `keep` can never prune the preserved snapshot. Retention runs on a name collision too (`create_auto_version` returning `Ok(false)`), so the tighter `keep` still governs a shared provenance group rather than being skipped.

## 2026-07-05 · Auto-version Unit 3 · AutoVersion sink — event-driven capture (a passive recorder + post-delivery drain); `keep` retention split to its own unit
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Auto-Version Triggers' "auto-versioning is the first built-in sink" over the Unit 1 event bus (#191) + Unit 2 triggers (#192); no scope change. On a matching `on:` event, a room's governing schema drives `Hub::create_version` with the expanded template name. The `keep` retention window is sliced out to **Unit 3b** — it needs a store-format change (see below), so this unit is the capture mechanism.
- **The sink cannot capture from `on_event` — a sink observes *after* a moment commits, and capturing mutates the same hub the emit is running over (a re-entrant `&mut` on a `&self` fan-out).** So the built-in `AutoVersionSink` is a **passive recorder**: it copies each room-bearing event into a shared `Rc<AutoVersionState>` queue, and `Registry::deliver` **drains it after the delivery has committed**, resolving each room's schema, matching triggers, and driving the capture. This keeps the sink a pure observer (as the event-bus design requires) while the mutation runs at the registry's top level where `&mut Hub` is available. Trigger matching lives at the registry (not the sink) because the schema resolution it needs (`room_apps` → `parsed_schema`) is the registry's, not the sink's.
- **Only room-bearing events drive a capture; connect/disconnect are dropped.** `Subscribed`, `VersionCreated`/`Renamed`/`Deleted`, `Compacted` name a room to version; `Connected`/`Disconnected` carry only a `ConnId`, so a room-scoped auto-version has no target — a connect/disconnect trigger parses (Unit 2) but fires nothing here. Room-scoped connect/disconnect (expand a disconnect to the conn's subscribed rooms — an autosave-on-leave) is a deferred follow-on; `every:` schedule triggers are Unit 4's (Clock + sweep), inert on the event path. The clock is read once per drain, only when a room-bearing event occurred — the op hot path emits none and never reaches the drain, so it stays clock-free.
- **An auto-created version does not cascade.** A capture re-emits `VersionCreated`, which a `version-created` trigger would in turn capture — an unbounded loop. A `draining` flag on the shared state suppresses the sink recording during the drain, so a capture's own events never re-enter the queue. A *client's* manual `VersionCreate` still fires a `version-created` trigger (it is recorded outside a drain); only auto-created versions are suppressed.
- **`keep` retention is deferred to Unit 3b — it requires durable per-version provenance, not a heuristic.** Two heuristics were built and rejected under review, both unsound: a **name-pattern** prune (group a trigger's versions by matching its rendered template) deletes an operator's *manual* version that coincidentally fits the pattern, collides two triggers that render the same name, and orders by the non-monotonic wall clock (an NTP step-back prunes the newest capture); an **in-memory** per-trigger tally resets across room dormancy and a restart (orphaning the persisted versions → unbounded growth). Bounding a trigger's captures *exactly* needs the version index to record which trigger authored each version and a monotonic capture order — a `<room>.versions` store-format change. That is a coherent slice of its own (**Unit 3b**), so `keep` parses (Unit 2) but is **inert** here: every matching event captures, unbounded, like a staged/reserved feature. Shipping no retention (a documented limit) is correct; shipping a retention that silently deletes manual snapshots is not.
- **The recording sink is armed lazily in schema *resolution*, so a no-`autoVersion` deployment pays nothing per event and the arming subscribe is itself recorded.** The registry always installs the recording sink (auto-versioning is built-in, and whether a schema uses it is per-room and dynamic), but the sink records nothing until an `armed` latch is raised — set the first time `parsed_schema` resolves a schema declaring any trigger. Arming in `parsed_schema` (not, as a first cut did, in `bind_room_app`) is the fix for a subtle miss: a subscribe's schema is resolved for authorization *before* its `Subscribed` fires, so the very subscribe that arms the latch is still recorded — a room already populated at a fresh server's first subscribe (or a relay-populated room's first enforcing subscriber) captures on that first join, not only the second. Until armed, `on_event` is a cheap flag check with no allocation, honoring the event bus's "no sink, no cost."
- **A capture on a room with no state, or a persist failure, is best-effort — never aborts the delivery.** A subscribe to a not-yet-materialized room (subscribe does not create the hub room; only an ingest does) has nothing to version — `create_version` returns `Ok(false)`, skipped. A durable-store persist failure (`Err`) is logged to stderr (the operator wanted a snapshot that was not captured) but never propagates — auto-versioning is a server-internal observer with no client requester to surface an error to, unlike the client-driven `VersionCreate` path. **Deferred:** the room→governing-app binding (`room_apps`) is in-memory (rebuilt on subscribe), so like the awareness-TTL binding it does not survive a restart until a durable binding lands — an auto-version trigger resolves only for a bound room.

## 2026-07-05 · Auto-version Unit 2 · schema `autoVersion` parse — format pinned (kebab events, `<n><unit>` schedule → ms)
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Auto-Version Triggers' `autoVersion` block as a concrete `core::schema` parse; no scope change. The declarative triggers the AutoVersion sink (Unit 3) reads off the registered schema. Records the format choices ARCHITECTURE left to implementation.
- **`autoVersion` is a JSON array of triggers**, each `AutoVersion { trigger: Trigger, name: String, keep: Option<u64> }`. Exactly one of `on` (event) / `every` (schedule) per trigger — both or neither is `BadTrigger`, the same fused-discriminant shape as a grant's `allow`/`deny`.
- **Event names are kebab-case, spanning the whole staged vocabulary.** `connect`, `disconnect`, `subscribe`, `version-created`, `version-renamed`, `version-deleted`, `compaction` (fire today), plus the reserved `before-publish`, `after-restore`, `before-migration` (declarable now, fire once the branch/migration layers exist). A reserved event *parses and waits*, never errors (ARCHITECTURE); a name outside the vocabulary is a typo → `UnknownEvent`. The vocabulary aligns with the Unit 1 `EngineEvent` variants (`disconnect`/`version-renamed` included, added there).
- **`every` is a `<n><unit>` string normalized to milliseconds** — unit `s`/`m`/`h`/`d`, parsed to a `u64` ms count via `checked_mul` (overflow → `BadDuration`). Milliseconds is the unit the `Clock` seam + sweep already use (awareness TTL/throttle), so the schedule needs no later conversion. An empty/non-numeric count, missing/unknown unit, compound (`1h30m`) or fractional (`1.5h`) spec is `BadDuration` — a single unit only, matching the ARCHITECTURE examples.
- **`name` is validated non-empty only; template-variable checking is the sink's concern.** The template var set (`${timestamp}`, `${event}`, …) is open per ARCHITECTURE, so the parser does not enumerate it — validating would reject a future var. `keep` is an optional non-negative count (`Option<u64>`, negative → `BadRange`), `None` retaining all. Pure core, total-decode, mirrors the `@auth` (4b) / awareness (3a) parse; no serde.

## 2026-07-05 · Auto-version Unit 1 · engine event bus — one lifecycle-event seam; audit-log convergence deferred
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Auto-Version Triggers' engine event bus + §Debugging (event bus = webhook substrate) as a concrete server seam; no scope change. The substrate the AutoVersion sink (Unit 3), schedule triggers (Unit 4), and webhooks consume.
- **`EngineEvent` + `EventSink` are one fan-out seam the engine owns on the `Hub`.** The hub holds `Vec<Box<dyn EventSink>>` (empty by default — no sink, no cost) and emits after a lifecycle moment commits, so a sink observes settled state and cannot alter behavior (a passive observer, not an interceptor). Events emitted now: `VersionCreated`/`VersionRenamed`/`VersionDeleted` (only on a real change, never on the `Ok(false)` no-op), `Compacted { floor }` (only when a non-empty log was reclaimed — an empty-log compaction advances no floor and stays silent, matching the version no-op suppression), `Connected`/`Disconnected` (balanced — `Disconnected` fires for every removed connection, authenticated or not, so a connect/disconnect-pairing sink stays even), `Subscribed`. The `Registry` feeds the connection/subscribe events into the hub's seam (`Hub::emit`, `pub(crate)`) rather than growing a second sink list — one seam, both layers.
- **A `Subscribed` fires on the not-subscribed→subscribed *transition*, for any accepted subscribe (relay or enforcing).** The event keys on the room going from unsubscribed to subscribed across the step, not on post-step room membership — so a rejected re-subscribe of an already-mapped room (a protocol violation the session refuses) does not re-fire, and a client cannot flood sinks by spamming duplicate subscribes. The single acceptance fact is computed once and shared with the schema-governance `bind` (which additionally requires an *enforcing* version); the `Subscribed` reuses the already-owned room clone, so a zero-sink engine allocates nothing extra.
- **Reserved variants (`BeforePublish`/`AfterRestore`/`BeforeMigration`) are declared but never emitted by this unit** — a later branch/migration layer routes through the one seam without an enum break at its call sites, mirroring how the op envelope reserves fields ahead of adoption.
- **The audit `AccessLog` is NOT collapsed into `EventSink` in this unit — deliberate, convergence deferred.** `AccessLog`/`Audited` (#85) is structurally an `Authorizer` decorator on a different axis (it observes an authorization *decision* per check, borrowing the check's inputs), whereas `EventSink` observes engine *lifecycle moments*. Unifying them (an `EngineEvent::Access` variant + `Audited` forwarding to a shared sink) means threading one sink through both the authorizer-decorator chain and the hub — an ownership change larger than this unit warrants. `EventSink` ships as the general lifecycle seam; folding the access log into it (so there is provably one event seam) is a follow-up, noted not done. No behavior overlap in the meantime — the two observe disjoint moments.

## 2026-07-05 · Unit 8f/#190 · cold-start snapshot migration — the op seam's key rewrites at snapshot granularity, decoupled from the current slot value
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Mixed-Version Sync's per-recipient translation on the *cold-start* path, closing the last untranslated seam — an admitted older joiner below the compaction floor got the materialized snapshot verbatim (undecodable at its version) while the ops seam (8c/8d) was already translated; no scope change.
- **`Document::migrate_leaf_slots(fate)` is the op seam's `OpRewrite` at snapshot granularity.** Across every map, each leaf slot (scalar / register / counter, live or tombstoned) is `Keep`t, `Drop`ped, or `Rename`d per a per-key `SlotFate`; a live container (map / list / text) is always kept unre-keyed, mirroring `Chain::translate_ops`, which carries a container-create verbatim rather than tear its keyless subtree. `translate::translate_snapshot` decodes the below-floor state, runs the fate (each key probed through the same `translate_op` the ops seam uses, so the key rewrite is identical), and re-encodes only if anything changed — a same/newer/unknown-app/unreachable joiner takes the bytes verbatim. So a snapshot-served joiner converges byte-identically with a peer served the same history as a translated op delta.
- **Counter-registry migration is decoupled from the current slot value, because a counter is retained across displacement.** A counter's tally lives in the persistent registry keyed by the id its slot key derives (`derive(map, key, Counter)`), retained there even when a scalar/register displaces the slot or the slot is tombstoned (the #48 displacement-retains design). So the migration must act on that registry entry from the *key*, independent of whether the slot still holds the counter live: a **Drop** removes the registry entry regardless of slot body (else a displaced/tombstoned tally lingers as a phantom that a later re-write of the key re-adopts, diverging from an op-served peer whose `CounterInc` was simply dropped); a **Rename** captures the tally and merges it into `derive(map, newKey, Counter)` — the shared id the renamed increments land at — regardless of slot body. An earlier revision gated this on the slot value being a live counter, which missed the displaced/tombstoned cases.
- **A renamed register re-derives its id from the new key.** A `Register` carries an id derived from its slot key, encoded into the snapshot. Moving it verbatim under a rename would keep the old-key id, diverging from an op-served peer whose renamed `RegisterSet` derives the id from the new key — so the moved register is re-keyed to `derive(map, newKey, Register)`. (A scalar carries no id; a container is never renamed; a counter re-homes through its registry — so register is the one leaf body needing an explicit id re-derivation.)
- **Rename is two-phase with an isolated tally capture, so any fate is order-independent.** Phase one takes every mover out of its slot, capturing a renamed counter's tally as an *isolated* deep-clone (not its live handle) and removing the old registry id; phase two re-homes each — a register re-keyed, a counter merged into its new id's registry entry (summing on a cross-type key collision, as the ops would), the slot pointed at the merged handle. Capturing an isolated copy keeps a chained rename (`a→c`, `c→d` in one pass) from leaking `a`'s tally through `c`'s live handle into `d`; commutative PN-merge + LWW-by-stamp at the slot make both phases independent of the traversal (HashMap) order.
- **A deleted (tombstoned) container field is carried verbatim, not migrated as a leaf — faithful container-field migration is impossible at snapshot granularity.** A create-then-delete of a container leaves a tombstone slot (`value: None`) plus the displaced container retained in the registry. The op seam carries the create verbatim (resurrecting the container at the old key) and re-keys only the delete, so an op-served joiner of a *renamed* such field holds `{oldKey: live container, newKey: tombstone}`. A snapshot cannot reproduce that: the materialized tombstone has dropped the create's stamp, so the container can't be re-instated with the right LWW stamp. Rather than mis-migrate the tombstone as a leaf (the pre-fix bug — it re-keyed the tombstone and diverged both ways), `migrate_leaf_slots` detects container identity on a tombstone (`has_container_identity` — the registry still holds the deleted container at `derive(map, key, {Map,List,Text})`) and carries the *slot body* verbatim. Crucially the **counter registry at the key's derived id still migrates** — a key can carry a deleted container (in `self.maps/…`) *and* a displaced counter (in `self.counters`, encoded in the snapshot and decoded back on the cold-start path), which are separate identities; the counter is a phantom that must prune (Drop) / re-home (Rename) regardless of the slot being carried, or a snapshot-served joiner keeps a stale tally an op-served peer (whose `CounterInc` was dropped) does not. So the container-identity skip is scoped to the slot body only; counter handling is decoupled from it (the same decoupling the fifth-review fix applied to displacement). The residual op-vs-snapshot divergence for the *container* under this create-then-delete-then-rename corner is the deferred **element-set-aware container-field migration** (the same seam 8c deferred faithful container subtree elision to); a live container was already carried verbatim and converges.
- **Known limitation (deferred, the type-scope item):** the fate is key-local and type-blind, so a key that is a container in one version and a counter in another — a counter displaced *by a container* — is skipped as a container while its shadow registry counter is left un-migrated. This is the already-deferred type-scope applicability limitation (a rename/drop applies across all map types) compounded with displacement; it needs a per-recipient type-scope filter, tracked separately.

## 2026-07-05 · Unit 8e/#189 · handshake range-check — refuse an unreachable joiner before it subscribes; gate keys on the governing floor (a fail-closed overestimate)
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Schema Migration gate 4 (per-doc reachability) + §Mixed-Version Sync's `onUpdateRequired` at the subscribe seam; no scope change. Two forced realizations recorded (both deferred, both surfaced by the 8e review).
- **`ErrorCode::UpdateRequired` (wire tag 6) is the `onUpdateRequired` signal.** At subscribe, after read-auth, `session::step` refuses a joiner that cannot reach the room's governing version across a back-compatible path — returns the error with **no catch-up**, before the joiner becomes a subscriber (so it enters no fan-out set and receives no ops). Forward is always reachable; a back-compatible gap never rejects; a breaking gap rejects. This is what lets fan-out/catch-up down-translation assume every admitted down-recipient traverses only invertible edges.
- **Only an enforcing joiner of the governing app is range-checked; the exemptions match the translate seam exactly.** `subscriber_reaches_governing` consults `translate::reachable(reg, app, governing_version, client_version)` only when `session.app_id() == governing_app` and both carry a version; a relay, a foreign-app, or a versionless joiner is a different version space and is **never** refused (served verbatim, as the fan-out already leaves it). A broken chain (`reachable` → `Err`: a `MissingEdge`/`BadMigration` gap the registry can't bridge) refuses **fail-closed**. The enforcing-governing-app-speaker predicate is now one helper (`governing_target`) shared by the write-tag, catch-up-translate, and range-check sites, so the three cannot drift.
- **The gate keys on the room's governing version, which is a sticky high-water floor — a fail-closed overestimate of the room's true content version.** `reconcile_room_apps` lifts governing to the highest version ever present and never lowers it while the room stays live (deliberate, for the awareness-TTL grace design: a just-departed newer client's grace-held presence must not expire early under an older peer's shorter TTL). 8e newly repurposes that floor as the admission gate, so a transient higher-version peer that subscribes once and leaves without writing floors an all-v1 room at v2 and then a returning v1 client is refused even though every op in the log is v1 and could be served in full. Shipped **noted, not fixed**: this is a fail-closed false-positive (over-refusal costs availability, never diverges — the client recovers by upgrading), the safe direction. The precise gate keys on the room's **actual max op version in the log**, not the TTL-grace floor; decoupling them (a per-room op-version high-water) is a follow-up, and it must not regress the awareness-TTL floor.
- **The gate is subscribe-time only; a later version lift can strand an already-joined peer.** A v1 peer that joined a v1-governed room stays subscribed when a same-app v2 subscriber lifts governing to v2; fan-out then down-drops every v2 write to it across the breaking gap (fail-closed — no divergence) but it got no `UpdateRequired` and silently stops updating. Closing this needs a re-check + `UpdateRequired` eviction of already-joined peers on a lift; deferred.

## 2026-07-05 · Unit 8d · catch-up delta translation — heterogeneous delta, translated at the subscribe seam
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Mixed-Version Sync's per-recipient translation on the *catch-up* path, closing the interim 8c left (a late joiner's backlog was untranslated while the live stream was); no scope change.
- **`Catchup::Ops` carries `StoredOp`, not bare `Op`.** A catch-up delta is a slice of the room's heterogeneous log, so its ops can span versions (mixed-version writers) — unlike a live broadcast batch, which is one writer's single version. `catch_up` now returns the stored records (each with its creation `schema_version`) so the subscribe seam has the per-op source version to translate from. `Catchup::Snapshot` is unchanged — a below-floor joiner still gets whole-state bytes; migrating that snapshot to the joiner's version is 8f (cold-start).
- **Translation happens in `session::step`'s Subscribe handler, on the same app-scoping as the live fan-out.** `step` gained a `governing_app: Option<&[u8]>` param (resolved by `deliver` from `room_apps` for the two data-plane messages that consult it — a subscribe's catch-up and an ops write's tag); the handler translates the delta to `session.schema_version()` only when the joiner speaks the governing app. A relay joiner or a foreign-app joiner (its version a different space) takes the delta verbatim.
- **The version tag must be governing-app-scoped, or catch-up corrupts a foreign write.** A foreign-app connection may write into a governed room (delivered verbatim on the live seam, since its version is a different app's space). Ingest previously tagged *every* write with `session.schema_version()`, so a foreign op landed in the log stamped with a version meaningless in the governing app's chain — and catch-up, translating along that chain, would rewrite or drop it, diverging the joiner from what the live seam delivered verbatim. Fixed at the source: `step`'s Ops handler tags a write with its version **only when the writer speaks the governing app**, else `None` (relay-like). So every `Some(v)` tag in a room's log is in the governing app's space, and a foreign op passes verbatim on both seams identically.
- **An unbound room's catch-up is served verbatim; its governing app cannot be safely inferred from the joiner.** `room_apps` is in-memory and rebuilt as clients bind, so a first subscriber after a store restart (log restored, binding not) or a dormant-room sweep (binding dropped, log retained) meets a populated log with no binding. Inferring the governing app from the *connecting* app is unsafe: a foreign first subscriber would then translate the governing app's log along its own chain and corrupt it — worse than the live seam, which serves such a room verbatim. So `governing_app` is resolved only for a *bound* room; an unbound one serves the delta verbatim. **Known interim:** that first joiner's backlog is untranslated (a v2 joiner of a v1 log gets raw v1 ops) — it then binds the room, so every later joiner is translated. The robust fix is a **durable room binding** that survives a restart and a sweep, so the governing app is always known; deferred to its own slice.
- **A heterogeneous delta is translated in consecutive same-version runs, one resolved chain per source version.** `translate::translate_delta` takes the delta by value and segments it into maximal runs of equal stored version, driving `Chain::translate_ops` per run against a chain cached by source version, preserving log order and moving ops (no clone). A run is the right granularity: an atomic transaction is contiguous in the log and single-version, so it stays whole within one run and keeps its poison/destrand handling; a source whose chain to the target is broken or unreachable (a breaking down-gap) drops its run fail-closed, exactly as the live seam does, pending 8e's handshake refusal of such a joiner. Reuses 8a's `resolve_chain`/8c's `Chain`, so live and catch-up translate identically and a late joiner converges with a live peer at the same version.

## 2026-07-05 · Unit 8c · live fan-out translation — app-scoped, convergence-preserving, chain resolved once
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Mixed-Version Sync's "on fan-out, for each (op, recipient) the server composes the edge-rewrites … and sends the rewritten op" on the live broadcast seam; no scope change.
- **The source version rides the `Response`, not each broadcast op.** A broadcast is one ingest batch, so all its ops share the writer's version; `Response.broadcast_version` carries that one `Option<u32>` (set from `session.schema_version()`) rather than re-tagging every op. The fan-out reads it as the source and each recipient's `session.schema_version()` as the target. (Catch-up, whose delta is heterogeneous, reads per-op versions from the log's `StoredOp`s — that is 8d.)
- **Translation is scoped to the room's governing app on both ends.** Version numbers only compare within one app's chain. A migration chain belongs to the room's *governing* app, so the write is translated only when the *writer* speaks that app (a foreign-app connection's version is a different space), and only to recipients of that app; a foreign-app writer or recipient is left verbatim. This closes a corruption hole where a foreign-app write's version number would have driven the room's chain and inverted an op that was never authored under it.
- **A partly-translatable transaction delivers its survivors destranded — convergence over the atomic view.** A migration can drop a subset of a transaction's members (a member on a v2-only field, down to v1). The group can then never reach its `count` at that recipient, so its surviving members are **destranded**: each delivered with its `tx` tag stripped, applying standalone instead of buffering forever. Dropping them with the group (the earlier all-or-nothing choice) is a convergence bug — a representable member (a write to a field both versions model) that never reaches the recipient leaves it diverged from the correct down-projection of the writer's state, and no strand-avoidance justifies that: destranding avoids the strand *and* delivers the content. The transaction's atomic-view boundary is unavoidably lost at a recipient that cannot see the member that could not cross, but the underlying ops still merge, so state converges (the same property the core relies on — an atomic author and a non-atomic peer reach identical state). A fully-carried transaction keeps its tags and stays atomic. (Re-grouping the survivors under a fresh server-minted `count` to keep them atomic among themselves is possible but unneeded for convergence; deferred.)
- **The chain is resolved and parsed once, off the lock.** For each distinct target version among the room's same-app recipients, the migration path is resolved into a parsed `Chain` up front — the registry is locked only for that resolution, not across the fan-out — and the peer loop rewrites against the owned chains. The common case (a same-version, relay, or foreign-app recipient, or a relay write) is verbatim: no lock, no parse, and a single clone per channel.
- **A recipient the chain cannot serve drops the whole batch, fail-closed.** An unreachable (breaking-gap), gapped, or unparseable chain yields no ops for that recipient rather than a wrong op. The handshake range-check (8e) refuses an unreachable — and, since `reachable` returns an error for a gapped/unparseable chain, a broken — recipient outright before it subscribes; until then the drop is fail-closed, never a corrupt apply. **Known interim:** catch-up delivery is still untranslated (8d), so a mixed-version late-joiner's backlog and the live stream disagree until 8d lands — the immediate next slice.
- **A container-create is carried verbatim; the key-local rewrite cannot elide a subtree.** `Chain::translate_ops` never drops or key-rewrites a `MapCreate`/`ListCreate`/`TextCreate` — it emits the original op (the container-kind predicate is `OpKind::creates_container` in core, one source of truth next to the id-derivation sites; it is an *exhaustive* match with no catch-all, so a newly added container kind fails to compile until it is classified there — the predicate cannot silently drift). The rewrite is key-local, but a container's descendants (a list/text insert, a nested set) target the container's *element id* and carry no field key, so no migration step ever matches them. Dropping the create while the descendants survive strands them against a container that never arrives; rewriting the create's key repoints it away from descendants that derive their element id from the original key. Either way the subtree tears. Carrying the create as-is keeps it whole — a field the recipient's version does not model surfaces as an unknown slot its invariant repair elides, never a strand. This qualifies ARCHITECTURE §Mixed-Version Sync's "no state materialization": faithful subtree elision (dropping the whole container for a version that lacks it) needs per-recipient element-set awareness — the materialization this seam avoids — so it is deferred; the verbatim carry is the fail-safe until then.
- **A poisoned transaction's whole surviving subtree is destranded together.** Because every survivor of a poisoned group is destranded (previous bullet), a container-create *and* its in-transaction keyless descendants are all carried, each `tx`-stripped — the container arrives populated, not empty. Rescuing only the create while dropping its in-tx inserts would deliver an empty container and silently lose content the recipient can represent; delivering all survivors keeps the subtree whole. **Known interim (cross-batch):** the tear across *frames* — a container's create fanned out in one batch, an insert into it in a later batch — is out of a single batch's reach; per-op poisoning is scoped to one fan-out batch, so a container edit split across `Ops` frames is not covered until the element-set-aware refinement lands.
- **The batch is translated once per distinct target version, not once per recipient.** The rewrite depends only on the (source, target) pair, so `deliver` builds `translated_by_target: HashMap<u32, Vec<Op>>` once — one `translate_ops` per distinct target among the room's same-app recipients — and every recipient at that version reads the shared result. A same-version fleet of N peers costs one translation, not N.

## 2026-07-05 · Unit 8b · the heterogeneous op log — each op stored + persisted at its creation schema version
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Mixed-Version Sync's "the op log is heterogeneous and immutable — each op is stored tagged with its creation `schema_version`" as the concrete server storage shape; no scope change. The tag is the source version per-recipient translation (8c) rewrites from.
- **The log's unit is `StoredOp { op, schema_version: Option<u32> }`, not a bare `Op`.** `Room.log` and the store's `RoomLog.ops` both carry it; `None` is a relay op (no schema in force), `Some(n)` an enforced op at the writing client's version (always `>= 1`). The tag is the *writer's* version, captured per ingest batch from `session.schema_version()` — so a v1 client writing into a v2-governed room stores its op at v1, and a v2 recipient gets it up-translated, without any migration checkpoint having occurred. Heterogeneity comes from mixed-version *writers*, not only from mid-life migrations.
- **The store record gained a version prefix — a format break, taken freely pre-release.** A log record was `u32 len ‖ encode_op`; it is now `u32 version ‖ u32 len ‖ encode_op`, the version `0` standing for a relay op (`None`), which is unambiguous since enforced versions are `>= 1`. The core wire `encode_op`/`decode_op` is untouched (still shared with the client, stable); only the server's on-disk record framing widened. There is no format-version byte and no migration of pre-existing logs — crdtsync ships nothing, so an old dev log is simply discarded, not bridged.
- **One commit path, two entries: batch-tag for live ingest, per-op tags for replay.** `Hub::ingest(room, ops, schema_version)` tags a whole live batch (all its ops share the writer's version) and delegates to a private `ingest_records(Vec<StoredOp>)`; store replay (`install_room`) calls `ingest_records` directly with the records decoded from disk, so a heterogeneous log round-trips a restart with each op's *own* version rather than being re-tagged under one. Broadcast and catch-up still surface bare `Op` in 8b — 8c reshapes those two seams to carry the version and drive `translate_op`.
- **The tag source is the connection's negotiated version — authoritatively it belongs on the wire, deferred.** An `Op` carries no schema version (core keeps schema a wire/server concern), so at ingest the only server-side signal for an op's creation version is the writing connection's `session.schema_version()`. That is exact for the dominant case — a client authoring ops at the single version its build speaks — but mislabels an op *authored under an older version and resent from the offline queue after the client upgraded* (its payload is old-shaped, but the reconnected connection negotiates the new version). ARCHITECTURE's "ingest validates an op against its *own* creation version" points at the authoritative source: a **client-declared per-op (or per-Ops-frame) creation version on the wire**, which a later wire/SDK unit adds and `ingest` then reads instead of the session. 8b's storage/persistence/translation foundation is unchanged by that refinement — only the tag's origin sharpens from connection-inferred to wire-declared. The mislabel window (upgraded client draining a pre-upgrade queue) is a known limitation until then.
- **A corrupt log-record length is indistinguishable from a torn tail — pre-existing, format-inherent.** `decode_records` drops a trailing record whose length prefix outruns the remaining bytes as a torn write; a length bit-flipped larger than the file cannot be told apart from a genuinely half-written tail without a per-record checksum, which the format has never carried. 8b did not change this (only the record gained a version prefix); adding checksummed framing to tell corruption from truncation is a separate store-hardening concern, not this unit.

## 2026-07-05 · Unit 8a/#185 · migration translation engine — direction is the function, reachability shares the parse, versions are ≥ 1
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Mixed-Version Sync's "the server composes the edge-rewrites along the chain from the op's creation version to the recipient's version" as a pure server engine (`crates/server/src/translate.rs`); no scope change. The engine both the live fan-out seam (8b) and cold-start snapshot (8d) will drive.
- **The registry chain resolves directly into the core slice; direction is the function.** `SchemaRegistry` stores version `n`'s edge (`n-1 → n`) as opaque bytes, so the edge slice reaching `(low, high]` is `migration(app_id, v)` for `v in low+1..=high`, parsed — exactly the ascending contiguous slice `rewrite_up_along` / `rewrite_down_along` / `reachable_down` document as their precondition. `translate_op` picks up vs down by comparing `from`/`to` (identity when equal, no chain consulted); the slice is always assembled ascending and the core fn walks it in its own direction. No `Chain` newtype — the registry's contiguity-from-1 invariant already guarantees the shape.
- **Reachability shares `translate_op`'s parse rather than a cheaper compat-only path.** `reachable` fully parses each edge (via the same `edge_slice`) even though `reachable_down` needs only the compat flag. Deliberate: it keeps the gate's error classification (`MissingEdge` / `BadMigration`) bit-for-bit identical to `translate_op`'s, so the handshake gate (8c) and the fan-out translation can never disagree about whether a path is usable — the `Unreachable`-iff-`reachable`-false equivalence is by construction. The gate runs once per connection, so the redundant parse is not on a hot path.
- **Migration bytes are parsed lazily at fan-out, not validated at registration.** `SchemaRegistry::register` stores the migration body opaquely and never parses it — matching how the schema body is stored opaque and parsed lazily (`Registry::parsed_schema`, cached-even-when-`None`). An unparseable edge therefore surfaces as `BadMigration` on the first crossing op (fail-loud, never a corrupt apply), not at register time. Register-time / boot-time migration validation is a separate detection gate (ARCHITECTURE §Four Detection Gates 2–3), left to its own unit.
- **Both versions are real registered versions (`≥ 1`).** A chain starts at version 1 (whose link carries an empty edge — no predecessor), and the handshake resolves the version-0 dynamic sentinel to the head before an op is tagged, so 0 is never a creation version reaching the engine. A documented precondition, consistent with the core chain-contiguity precondition; `edge_slice` still walks overflow-free so a version at the top of the space cannot panic.

## 2026-07-05 · Unit 7d/#184 · edge + chain op-rewrite composition; down folds in reverse; reachability = all-edges-back-compat
**Changed:** finalizes the composition order 7c deferred, realizing ARCHITECTURE §Mixed-Version Sync ("compose the edge-rewrites along the chain") + gate 4 (per-doc reachability); no scope change.
- **An edge composes its steps; a chain composes its edges — up forward, down in reverse.** `Migration::rewrite_up` folds the edge's steps in declaration order; `rewrite_down` is `None` for a breaking edge and otherwise folds them **last-to-first** (inverting a sequence inverts its members in reverse). `rewrite_up_along` / `rewrite_down_along` do the same one level up over a chain of edges: up walks the chain forward, down walks it in reverse. A `Drop` short-circuits at either level (a dropped op has no image downstream). An empty edge / empty chain is identity.
- **Both chain fns take the ascending, contiguous chain; direction is the function, not the argument order.** The caller (Unit 8 fan-out) supplies the edge slice between the op's creation version and the target, ascending and contiguous (`edges[i].to == edges[i+1].from`); `rewrite_up_along` walks it forward, `rewrite_down_along` in reverse. Contiguity + ascending order is a **documented precondition**, not validated — the caller resolves the path from the registry chain, so re-validating here would duplicate that and invent an error type with no caller; kept a precondition until a consumer needs otherwise.
- **Reachability = every edge back-compatible.** `reachable_down(edges)` is true iff each edge has an inverse; forward is always reachable (no `reachable_up`). It is exactly the predicate `rewrite_down_along` gates on (returns `Some` iff `reachable_down`), and the one the handshake range-check consults to refuse an unbridgeable recipient (`onUpdateRequired`) — so a down-translation only ever traverses invertible edges. `rewrite_down_along` enforces the equivalence by checking `reachable_down` **up front**, before the fold — not by relying on the reverse walk to reach the breaking edge, since a `Drop` from an upper edge would short-circuit before it does, letting a per-op result disagree with the path's reachability. This mirrors edge-level `Migration::rewrite_down`, which gates on `compat()` before threading its steps.
- **Down step-order is correct-by-construction but not yet observable.** The only back-compatible steps today (addType/addField) have inverses that commute (independent key drops), so the reverse-fold's order cannot change an outcome under the current step set; the reverse is implemented for when non-commuting back-compatible steps (e.g. value transforms) land. Tests assert the observable behavior (drops, reachability, up-order via renames on breaking-but-forward edges).

## 2026-07-05 · Unit 7c/#183 · op-rewrite is a pure per-op key transform; type steps are inert; type-scope deferred to fan-out
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Mixed-Version Sync's "each migration edge carries a bidirectional op-rewrite … cheap structural surgery, no state materialization" as the code shape the `op::Op` model forces; no scope change.
- **Only the field steps rewrite ops; the type steps are inert on the op stream.** An `Op` is addressed by `target: ElementId` + a slot `key` (for the map-level kinds), and **never names a schema type**. So `AddType` / `RemoveType` / `RenameType` leave every op unchanged (up and down) — a type rename/removal is a schema-and-validation concern, not an op transform. Only `RenameField` (rewrite the key), `RemoveField` (drop the op on the removed slot, up), and `AddField` (drop the op on the added slot, down) touch ops. `rewrite_up` is total; `rewrite_down` is `Some` exactly when the step is back-compatible (mirrors `compat()`), `None` for breaking steps.
- **The rewrite is pure per-op, assuming type-scope; narrowing-by-type is deferred to the fan-out (Unit 8).** `Step::rewrite_up/down` take one op and act on its key with no schema/materialized-tree lookup — "no state materialization," exactly ARCHITECTURE's claim. But an op does not carry the *type* of its target element, so restricting a field rewrite to elements of the step's `ty` cannot happen here; that scoping rides the per-recipient fan-out seam (Unit 8), which already resolves elements. 7c is the transform; Unit 8 is the applicability filter.
- **Edge-level composition is deferred.** `OpRewrite { Keep(Op), Drop }` is per-`Step`; composing an edge's steps into one op-rewrite (and the ordering questions a rename-then-remove raises) is left to Unit 8, where the fan-out drives composition along a concrete version path. Keeping 7c to the per-step transform avoids pinning a composition order before its consumer exists.

## 2026-07-05 · Unit 7a · the migration-file format + the initial step-kind set (`core::migration`)
**Changed:** pins the concrete shape of a migration file, which ARCHITECTURE §Schema Migration names only at intent level ("built-in step kinds: rename / add / remove / wrap / setAttr / mapValues / …"); no scope change — realizes the format the code must parse. Foundation for the rest of Unit 7 (classification, op-rewrite, chain/gates).
- **A migration file is one edge, `{ from, to, steps }`, contiguous `to == from + 1`.** The server registry already stores migration bytes *per chain link* (the edge reaching each version) and the chain is contiguous from version 1, so a migration is a single forward step, not a multi-version bundle. Parsing rejects a gap / backward / self edge (`NonContiguous`) and a `from < 1` (`BadVersion`) — version 1 has no predecessor, so the lowest edge is 1→2. Both versions are `u32` (out-of-range → `BadVersion`).
- **The initial step-kind set is the six *structural* transforms**, each aligned to the existing `schema::TypeDef` model: `addType` / `removeType` / `renameType` and `addField` / `removeField` / `renameField`. These are the kinds expressible over the built primitives today. The **value-transform kinds (`wrap` / `setAttr` / `mapValues`) are deferred** — they operate over marks / attributes / XML, which are unbuilt; adding them now would be stub-only. They slot in with that layer.
- **Hand-rolled over `core::json`, reusing the schema type-def parser.** Same reason as Unit 1 (core is dep-minimal, `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`, no serde): parse against the `Json` value model. `addType`'s `def` reuses `schema::parse_type_def` (made `pub(crate)`) so there is one type-def parser — a bad def surfaces as `MigrationErrorKind::TypeDef(SchemaErrorKind)`, never a panic. Parsing is total (every input → a `Migration` or a `MigrationError`) and rejects an unknown key at every level (`UnknownField`), matching the schema parser's fail-loud discipline.
- **Model + parser only.** No op-rewrite, no back-compat classification, no application to a schema or document state — those are 7b–7d. Cross-reference validation (does a renamed type exist?) is deferred to apply time, where the target schema is in scope; 7a validates only the envelope and per-step well-formedness.

## 2026-07-05 · Unit 4c-ii/#176 · the schema `@auth` grant tier composes under the deployment authorizer, governed by the room
**Changed:** realizes ARCHITECTURE §Authorization's decision flow (the "schema role-grant" tier between explicit deployment allow/deny and default-deny) as the code shape it forces; no scope change. Completes Unit 4.
- **The layered decision is three-valued; a `bool` authorizer is a final word.** `authz::Decision { Allow, Deny, Abstain }` with a provided `Authorizer::decide`. Composing the schema tier *below* a deployment's explicit allow/deny but *above* default-deny is impossible with a `bool`: `false` cannot distinguish "explicitly denied" (must win over a schema allow) from "no opinion" (defer to the schema). So `Acl::decide` returns `Abstain` on no matching rule, and only an abstaining authorizer ever reaches the schema. A `bool` authorizer (`PermitAll`, a closure) inherits the default `decide` (never `Abstain`) — existing behaviour is unchanged when no schema governs.
- **The governing schema is the room's, not the connection's self-declared app.** An earlier cut authorized a connection's own reads/writes under the schema *it declared at Hello* (`connection_schema`). That is a cross-app privilege escalation: a foreign connection declares a permissive registered app and reads/writes a room another app governs. Fixed to resolve the **room's** governing schema (`room_apps`→`parsed_schema`), with the connection's own app as a bootstrap fallback *only* for a not-yet-bound room (its first subscriber, the incumbent-to-be) — the one case with no incumbent to escalate against. Fan-out redaction (`peer_may_read`) already used the room's governing schema, so both halves now agree.
- **`room_apps` is maintained under any awareness policy.** It was bound + reconciled only when no awareness policy was injected (an optimization: awareness TTL was then its sole reader). The authorization tier reads it unconditionally, so an injected-policy deployment left it empty → `governing_schema` returned `None` for every room → schema-granted peers were redacted from all fan-out. Binding is now unconditional; the sweep's `reconcile_room_apps` (also unconditional now) prunes dormant rooms, so the map stays bounded.
- **Audit logs the composed verdict via a new `observe` hook.** `Audited` wraps the *deployment* authorizer, but the final decision is made by the composition after the schema tier resolves an abstain. Overriding only `authorize`/`decide` either flattened the abstain (silently disabling schema grants) or logged the wrong (pre-schema) verdict. `Authorizer::observe(id, action, resource, granted)` (default no-op) is called once by `authorized()` with the final verdict; `Audited::observe` records it, `decide` forwards unchanged, and the control-plane `authorize` path (no schema tier) still logs directly. Every enforced access is logged once, with the verdict actually enforced.
- **Deferred (no carrier):** grant `on` path-scoping (the room-level `Resource` has no path — only whole-document `/` grants apply; a sub-path grant is left unenforced, never over-applied room-wide), `${…}` ownership templates (no ownership state), and group-subject schema grants (`core::schema` has no `Group` subject). These slot in with the doc-ACL / path-carrying `Resource` work.

## 2026-07-04 · Unit 4c-i/#175 · the `Authorizer` seam authorizes an `Identity`, not a bare actor
**Changed:** no ARCHITECTURE change — realizes the §Authorization decision-flow seam (4a captures claims, the evaluator consumes them) as the code shape it forces; sliced 4c into the seam (this PR) and the schema-grant tier (4c-ii).
- **`Authorizer::authorize` takes `&Identity`, not `&[u8]` actor.** 4a already threads a full `Identity { actor, roles, groups }` through `Session`; the evaluator can only match `Subject::Role`/`Group` against the claim set if the seam carries it. So every enforcement call site (`session.rs` Subscribe/Ops/AwarenessSet/version, `registry.rs` `peer_may_read`, `admin.rs` RegisterSchema) switches `session.actor()` → `session.identity()`; `audit.rs` records `identity.actor()` unchanged. The bare-actor signature would have left role/group grants unmatchable without a second lookup at each site.
- **`acl::Subject` grows `Role(String)`/`Group(String)`**, matched against `Identity::roles()`/`groups()`; policy tokens `role:<name>`/`group:<name>`. A role-grant turns on the *claim*, not the actor id — so `role:editor` allows any identity carrying that role, and deny-wins still overrides a broader role allow. An empty `role:`/`group:` name is a `PolicyErrorKind::Subject` parse error (a claim with no name matches nothing meaningful and is a policy typo, caught loud).
- **Sliced 4c into 4c-i (identity seam + acl Role/Group, this PR) + 4c-ii (schema `@auth` grant tier).** The seam widening is the deployment-ACL half — buildable and testable against hand-built identities now; feeding the room's resolved-schema grants into the evaluation is the next slice, gated on nothing new (Unit 5 already resolves the schema per room).



## 2026-07-04 · Unit 2b-2/#174 · `onRepaired` is a lazy observation of settled locations, diffed on the repaired reading — not an eager per-apply event
**Changed:** refines ARCHITECTURE §Invariant Repair's "`onRepaired` fires at apply" into the shape the implementation forced; no scope change.
- **Observation is a pull of settled state, not an eager per-apply event.** `Document::set_schema` binds an opt-in schema; `Document::take_repairs()` reports what the state has newly come to repair since the last call. An earlier design fired eagerly at each `drain_buffer` (per applied op): it was O(ops · doc) on a large catch-up (a full `validate` per op) and surfaced transient mid-delta violations as spurious events (an insert-then-delete within one delivery reported a phantom over-max). Computing lazily at the drain the consumer controls fixes both — only settled state is ever compared, so an appeared-then-resolved violation between drains is never reported, and cost is one walk per drain, not per op.
- **`take_repairs` reports located paths, not `Repair` values.** ARCHITECTURE already says "the repaired value is produced at read." Returning the `Repair` (with point-in-time `keep` indices) let a consumer cache an index list that a later unrelated sequence edit silently invalidated. Returning the located paths (`Vec<Vec<Step>>`) and having the consumer read the current value via `repairs()` removes the whole stale-payload class: there is no cached reading to go stale.
- **The diff key is the repaired *reading*, not the emitted indices.** A truncation is identified by its surviving node *stamps*, a clamp by its target value (both plus the element's path). So a re-clamp to the other bound, or a different surviving item, re-surfaces (the reading changed), while a pure index shift that keeps the same survivors does not (the consumer observes that sequence edit through a normal read). Keying on the full index-bearing `Repair` would over-fire on unrelated shifts; keying only on stamps would miss a changed survivor at the same index — the stamps-plus-value reading is the identity that catches exactly the material changes.
- **Path is a stable identity because a repairable element is never a list item.** A code-review finding argued an outer list's shift would re-path a nested truncation and spuriously re-fire. Rejected: a sequence node holds a scalar (`OpKind::ListInsert { value: Scalar }`), so no composite is ever a list item — a repairable element (register/counter/list/text) is only ever a map-slot value, and its path is all `Step::Key`, never a shifting `Step::Index`. The scenario is structurally unreachable.
- **Settle-point contract for atomic transactions.** `take_repairs` is empty while a local atomic transaction is open (`self.atomic.is_some()`), so a consumer polling mid-group never observes or baselines a transient sub-state the group does not commit; bind/drain at settle points. A violation that a remote `apply()` both introduces and resolves inside an open local atomic window is a between-drains transient and correctly unreported.
- **Known deferred (scoped to the client-integration unit):** a bound schema is runtime state, not part of a snapshot, so a replica rebuilt via `decode_state` observes nothing until re-bound; wiring `set_schema` through `ClientSession` snapshot adoption is that unit's job. Accepted costs: `take_repairs` re-walks the tree per drain (O(doc)) and diffs O(current · baseline) — fine for an opt-in schema at human drain cadence; incremental/scoped detection is deferred.

## 2026-07-04 · Unit 2b-1/#172 · read-time repair is a pure post-pass over the validator's violation set, not a schema-aware primitive
**Changed:** no ARCHITECTURE change — fixes the shape of the read-time normalization (§Invariant Repair) and how it slices.
- **Repair consumes `validate()`; it is not a second schema walk.** `core::repair::repairs(doc, schema)` maps each `Violation` to a `Repair`: `BelowMin`/`AboveMax` → `Clamped { value: crossed_bound }`, `TooLong` → `Truncated { keep }`. `KindMismatch`/`UnknownSlot` have no defined repaired reading and are omitted, so repair order is a filtered `validate()` order — deterministic for free. This keeps `validate` the single tree walker; repair adds no traversal logic, only a per-violation navigation for the `TooLong` case.
- **`validate` stays a pure path/kind report — no live handles leak into `Violation`.** A code-review finding noted `repairs()` re-navigates from the root per `TooLong` (redundant with the walk that already read each sequence's `len`). Rejected the coupling: threading `Element` (`Rc`) handles through `Violation` to save a bounded, only-on-violation re-walk would pollute the pure, inspectable violation type. The re-navigation cost is O(violations · depth) and materializes only on actual non-conformance (a repaired read is already exceptional).
- **Drop-newest order is the `(lamport, client)` stamp total order already in state**, read via `List`/`Text::node_ids` (index-aligned with the read values) — never the local clock — so merged replicas truncate to the same survivor indices (convergence test). `Truncated { keep }` lists the survivor *sequence indices* (ascending), computed by ordering nodes newest-first and dropping the first `len - max`.
- **Sliced 2b into 2b-1 (read repair pass, this PR) + 2b-2 (`onRepaired` at apply).** The read half is a pure function of merged state, buildable now; the apply-time event defers the open question of how a schema reaches the apply boundary.

## 2026-07-04 · Unit 2a/#170 · the state validator checks only model-expressible constraints, and is total on any decoded document
**Changed:** no ARCHITECTURE change — the shape of the schema *state* validator (the half moved out of Unit 1b), and one scope realization it forces on Unit 2b.
- **The validator reports only what the parsed `Schema` can express.** `core::validate::validate(doc, schema)` walks the materialized element tree and produces `Vec<Violation>` — map slot-allowlist (`UnknownSlot`), runtime-kind vs declared-type (`KindMismatch`), register/counter `Int` bounds (`BelowMin`/`AboveMax`), list/text `max` (`TooLong`). The `TypeDef` model carries no exclusivity and no disallowed-value/enum field, so those constraints are not checkable here — exclusivity stays XmlElement/marks-gated (already deferred), and **"disallowed-value drop" (listed as a Unit 2b repair) has nothing to validate against and cannot be built until a schema enum/disallowed-value field is added.** 2b is descoped to the repairs whose constraint the model expresses: scalar/counter clamp and sequence-`max` drop-newest.
- **`Violation` is the shared currency for repair.** It carries the located `path` (`Vec<Step>` of map keys / list indices) plus the offending value and the crossed bound, so 2b's read-time normalization has everything it needs without re-deriving it.
- **The walk is total on every decoded document, not just well-formed ones.** A valid tree is single-parent, so each element is reached once and every violation is reported. But a document decoded from a *crafted* snapshot can share or cycle its slot graph (decode's cycle guard only covers the separate `parents` map, not the slot-ref graph), so the walk is iterative over an explicit stack with an `ElementId` descend-once guard: an element's own constraint is checked on every reach (a shared leaf is still flagged under each slot) but its subtree is entered once, bounding work to the slot-edge count and making a cycle terminate. The tree location is an `Rc<PathNode>` parent-cons-list (extending a path is O(1); the `Vec<Step>` is materialized only when a violation is recorded) with an iterative `Drop`, so neither the walk nor the path teardown recurses off the stack at depth.

**Why:** the validator runs server-side over client-authored state, so "never panics / never overflows on any input" is a correctness requirement, not a nicety — a recursive walk or a recursive `Rc` teardown would let a deep or crafted document crash the process. Confining the checks to model-expressible constraints keeps the closure guarantee honest (every reported violation has a repair) and surfaces the missing disallowed-value field before 2b tries to build a repair with no constraint behind it.

## 2026-07-04 · Unit 3b-iv · server-side throttle is a leading-edge inbound cap, not a timer-driven trailing flush
**Changed:** no ARCHITECTURE change — the enforcement shape of `awareness.<kind>.throttle` (ARCHITECTURE §Throttle: "Client-side SDK debounces at throttle interval before sending. Server-side caps inbound — faster updates coalesce, keep latest only").
- **The server caps the outbound rate; it does not run a trailing-edge timer.** The first update, any update on an unthrottled kind, and the first update once the window has elapsed fan out at once and become the entry's stored value. An update arriving inside the window is *coalesced*: it refreshes the entry's last-seen time (so a fast stream does not TTL-expire mid-move) but does **not** replace the stored value or fan out. The stored value is therefore always what the room was last sent. **Delivering the trailing value is the client SDK's debounce, not the server's job** (§Throttle line 840 assigns debounce to the client) — so the server needs no per-entry timer, and the periodic sweep does no throttle work.
- **A joiner replays the last-broadcast value, so every peer and any joiner agree.** Because the stored value is exactly what was last fanned out (a coalesced value is dropped, not stored), a client subscribing mid-stream is replayed the same value existing peers hold — there is no window in which a joiner sees a peer's presence ahead of everyone else.
- **Fan-out excludes the originating connection (by `ConnId`), unchanged from the pre-throttle path.** An earlier revision that added a coalesced-flush path excluded the whole owning `ClientId`, which froze a second connection of the same client; removing the flush removes the divergence — a sibling connection (another tab) is a normal recipient again.

**Why:** an earlier design held the coalesced value and flushed it on the periodic sweep. But the sweep interval (default 1s) is far coarser than a cursor throttle (≈100ms), so the trailing value lagged up to a second; the held value also raced timed-TTL expiry (expire-before-flush could clear it unseen) and let a joiner replay a not-yet-broadcast value, disagreeing with existing peers. All three fall away once the server stops trying to own the trailing edge: the client debounce already delivers the final position on its next past-window send, so a server-side timer is redundant complexity. The cost — a misbehaving client that streams faster than its throttle and then stops leaves peers one window behind its true final position — is the intended defensive degradation, and is bounded by the throttle window.

## 2026-07-04 · Unit 3b-iii · a room's governing schema is a sticky per-room binding, not a per-sweep scan of live subscribers
**Changed:** no ARCHITECTURE change — the schema-resolution half of awareness timed TTL, and how a room binds to an app.
- **A room is governed by one app — the first enforcing app to bind it — for as long as the room stays live; a foreign app never seizes it.** The schema that times a room's presence out is resolved from the `{app_id, version}` bound in `room_apps`, seeded when an enforcing client subscribes and reconciled each sweep against who is present. Earlier attempts each traded one cross-app edge for another: a per-sweep scan of live subscribers left a ghost cursor once the last enforcer departed and was version-nondeterministic; a pure sticky binding let a foreign app grief-expire an incumbent; adding *successor takeover* (a present app inheriting a departed app's room) then let a foreign app seize the presence of an incumbent that had merely blipped into its grace window, and ratcheted the version to the highest ever bound. The resolved rule is the simplest safe one: **the incumbent app governs while the room is live (holds presence or has any subscriber); a foreign app subscribing is ignored** (so it can never grief-expire the incumbent, connected or grace-held). The governing version is the highest version of the incumbent seen while the room has held presence (the bound version is a floor a present higher version lifts), resetting only when the room goes dormant — so a rolling upgrade adopts the newer schema and a just-departed newer client's grace-held presence keeps its own longer TTL instead of expiring early under an older peer's. A version *downgrade* mid-presence (a rollback, or a newer version that drops a kind's TTL) is the transient mixed-version edge this trades away; per-entry version governance (each presence entry timed by the schema version that set it) is the exact fix, deferred as beyond the TTL bridge. A room with neither presence nor a subscriber is dropped, bounding the map. Binding is gated on the subscribe being *accepted* — a rejected/read-denied subscribe opens no channel and governs nothing.
- **An injected `AwarenessPolicy` is authoritative; the schema path is the default when none is injected.** The `Registry` holds `Option<Arc<dyn AwarenessPolicy>>` (was a `NoTimedTtl` default). `Some(policy)` governs expiry alone — one declaring no TTLs *suppresses* expiry — and `None` resolves TTLs from each room's schema. This makes the seam's meaning unambiguous (an injected no-TTL policy means "no expiry", not "fall through to schema") and confines the schema machinery (the room→app binding, its per-sweep reconcile and pruning) to the `None` path — so a server on an injected policy neither seeds nor grows `room_apps`.

- **A room is served by a single app; cross-app reuse is an unsupported configuration.** The above governs it *safely* — the first app wins until the room fully empties, then the next app rebinds — rather than perfectly. Perfectly governing two apps sharing one room would need per-app presence partitioning under one room, which the one-schema-per-room model does not carry; grief-resistance (a foreign or malicious app can never seize a live room's TTLs) is worth more than exactness in a config the engine does not support.
- **Parsed schemas are cached per `{app_id, version}` for the process lifetime (`schema_cache`, `Arc<Schema>`).** A registry link is immutable once locked, so a version's schema never changes — re-parsing its JSON every 1s sweep was pure waste. The cache also lets many rooms of one app share a single parsed copy (an `Arc`), not a deep clone per room.
- **The sweep skips the registry lock entirely when no room holds presence** — the idle server never contends the handshake path's mutex.

**Why:** presence lifetime is a room property, not a property of who happens to be connected this instant, so the schema that governs it must be a stable room binding — resolving it from the live connection set is both leaky (ghost cursors) and nondeterministic (version races). Caching the immutable parse keeps the per-second sweep cheap. Completes the schema→TTL bridge; unblocks 3b-iv (throttle/coalesce).

## 2026-07-04 · Unit 3b-ii/#167 · timed-TTL policy is an injected seam on the Registry, and the set path stamps last-seen
**Changed:** no ARCHITECTURE change — the enforcement half of awareness timed TTL.
- **The per-kind TTL is an injected `AwarenessPolicy` trait on the `Registry`, default `NoTimedTtl`.** The sweep needs "how long may kind K in room R stay silent," which for an enforcing server derives from the registered schema — but the pure expiry logic (last-seen tracking, silence comparison, per-key clear broadcast) is independent of *where* the TTL comes from. So the policy is a seam (like `set_clock`/`set_schema_registry`) with a no-TTL default that leaves every entry session-lifetime — existing behaviour and every non-enforcing server untouched. 3b-iii supplies the schema-backed impl.
- **`set_awareness` stamps a last-seen millis per entry; `Registry::deliver` reads the clock only for an `AwarenessSet`.** The entry tuple grew a `last_seen`, and `now` is threaded into `step`. `deliver` reads the clock lazily — only when the message is an `AwarenessSet` — so the op hot path never touches wall time, and Miri-run op tests never hit `clock_gettime`. Awareness tests that ran on the default `SystemClock` were switched to a `ManualClock` (the set path now reads the clock, which Miri's isolation blocks).
- **Expiry reuses the sweep + broadcasts `AwarenessClearKey` (3b-i), not the actor-wide clear.** One kind expiring leaves the actor's other entries and connection intact — the grace path's actor-wide `AwarenessClear` stays for disconnect.

**Why:** injecting the TTL keeps the enforcement mechanism proven against a `ManualClock` before the schema-resolution wiring (3b-iii) supplies real values, and the default `NoTimedTtl` means the seam is invisible until a schema drives it. Reading the clock only for awareness sets avoids a wall-time syscall on every op and keeps Miri green. Unblocks 3b-iii.

## 2026-07-04 · Unit 3b-i/#166 · timed awareness TTL gets a per-key clear on the wire, not a reuse of the actor-wide clear
**Changed:** no ARCHITECTURE change — refines the pre-implementation sketch. The board's Unit 3 note sketched "reuse `AwarenessClear`"; ARCHITECTURE §TTL is the authority ("Timed TTL cleared on expiry; removal broadcast", per entry), and awareness entries are per-kind.
- **A new `Message::AwarenessClearKey { channel, actor, key }` (wire tag 20)** drops a single one of an actor's entries, complementing the existing actor-wide `AwarenessClear`. Timed TTL expires one kind ("cursor") after silence while the actor's other kinds ("selection") and its connection live on, so the actor-wide clear is too coarse — it would drop presence the actor still holds. The core client's `receive` removes just that `(actor, key)`; a client that sends one is a protocol violation (the message only travels server→client, like `AwarenessUpdate`/`AwarenessClear`).
- **Sliced 3b wire → pure enforcement → schema wiring → throttle.** 3b-i is the forward-compat wire addition (cheap now, painful once adopted); 3b-ii is the pure sweep logic with an injected TTL; 3b-iii resolves the governing schema per room and feeds real TTLs; 3b-iv is throttle/coalesce.

**Why:** per-kind timed TTL is genuinely per-entry, so the removal broadcast must name the entry — the actor-wide clear cannot express "one kind expired." Adding the wire variant first keeps the envelope stable for the enforcement slices to target. Break compat freely (pre-release). Unblocks 3b-ii.

## 2026-07-04 · Unit 5c-iii-b/#165 · the app declaration is one C-ABI entry point mirrored across every binding
**Changed:** no ARCHITECTURE change — the SDK surface for the core `declare_app`.
- **A single C-ABI `crdtsync_client_declare_app(client, app_id, app_id_len, schema_version) -> i32`** carries the declaration; the Python/Go/wasm bindings are thin forwards (`Client.declare_app`, `(*Client).DeclareApp`, `WasmClient.declare_app`). An empty `app_id` is accepted as a relay declaration (`as_slice` maps len 0 to an empty slice), so a binding need not special-case "no app". The C ABI returns `1`/`-1` (bad handle) matching the crate's other mutating entry points; the higher-level bindings drop the code since a live wrapper handle never fails.
- **Binding coverage is a Hello-frame smoke test, not a re-test of the framing.** Core + FFI already unit-test the exact wire bytes; each binding test only asserts a declared app id appears in `hello()` and is absent for a bare client, proving the value crossed the language boundary.

**Why:** one ABI entry point keeps the four language surfaces in lockstep with no per-binding logic to drift, and accepting an empty `app_id` as a relay keeps the "no app ⇒ relay" default uniform from core through every SDK. Completes 5c-iii and the 5c arc.

## 2026-07-04 · Unit 5c-iii-a/#164 · the client declares its app through a setter, not a constructor argument
**Changed:** no ARCHITECTURE change — an implementation + slicing decision.
- **`ClientSession::declare_app(app_id, schema_version)` is a setter on the existing session**, not a new `new_for_app` constructor or a `new` parameter. `ClientSession::new(client)` has many call sites; a setter with a relay default (empty `app_id`, version 0) leaves every one untouched and keeps the bare-relay path the default a client falls into if it never declares an app. `hello()` reads the fields instead of hardcoding empty/0 (the placeholder left by 5c-i).
- **Sliced 5c-iii core → SDK.** 5c-iii-a is the pure, Miri-clean core API (setter + accessors + `hello` wiring), unit-testable with no bindings. 5c-iii-b exposes it over the C ABI + Python/Go/wasm — four language surfaces that share nothing with the core logic, so they slice off cleanly.

**Why:** a setter with a relay default keeps a client-facing API addition from rippling into unrelated construction sites and makes "no app declared ⇒ relay" the explicit default, matching the server's resolution (empty/0 ⇒ relay). Isolating the core API from the four-language SDK surface keeps each PR reviewable. Completes the data path of the handshake declaration; 5c-iii-b carries it to embedders.

## 2026-07-04 · Unit 5c-ii-b-2/#161 · one schema registry shared across the data + admin planes
**Changed:** no ARCHITECTURE change — the cross-plane wiring that completes 5c-ii, rebased onto the axum admin plane (#162).
- **A single `Arc<Mutex<SchemaRegistry>>` is shared by both planes.** `main.rs` creates it and threads it through `ServeConfig.schema` into `registry_actor` (which calls `Registry::set_schema_registry`, the data plane) and into `serve_admin` / `admin_router` (the admin plane, which writes it). One registry, both planes: a registration over the admin plane is at once visible to the data-plane handshake resolution. `admin_router`/`serve_admin` take the shared `Arc<Mutex<SchemaRegistry>>` rather than owning a fresh one.
- **`ServeConfig` drops `Copy`, keeps `Clone`.** It now holds an `Arc`, which is not `Copy`. It is only ever moved once (built via `..ServeConfig::default()` and handed to one serve call), so removing `Copy` is transparent at every call site.
- **The lock is scoped to the registry access on both planes, never across a user callback.** `register_schema` runs the verifier + authorizer lock-free and locks only for the `register` write; `step` locks only in the `Hello` arm around `resolve_handshake` (the data plane's sole registry read), so the `Auth` branch's verifier never holds it. A poisoned lock is recovered via `into_inner()` rather than propagated, so a panic under the lock in one plane cannot wedge the other — the read leaves the map intact and the write validates before it mutates.

**Why:** sharing one authority is the whole point of the unit — the handshake must resolve against what the admin plane actually registered. Scoping each lock to just the registry touch (auth lock-free) keeps a slow verifier on either plane from stalling the other, and recovering a poisoned lock keeps the two planes' fault domains independent. Completes 5c-ii. Unblocks 5c-iii (client declares real values).

## 2026-07-04 · Unit 5b-ii-2/#162 · the admin plane serves on axum, not a hand-rolled HTTP/1.1 parser
**Changed:** ARCHITECTURE §Schema Registration gains a transport note — the admin control plane is served with axum over hyper, not a bespoke parser. The route, credential carrier, and status contract are unchanged; the endpoint was always transport-agnostic ("HTTP admin endpoint").
- **The hand-rolled `http::parse_head` (#156) + `admin::dispatch`/`AdminResponse` (#157) are deleted, replaced by `admin::admin_router` + `serve_admin` on axum 0.8 / tower-http.** The admin plane is an untrusted network boundary; request smuggling and framing edge cases (conflicting `Content-Length`/`Transfer-Encoding`, chunked bodies, header limits) are precisely what a hand-rolled parser gets wrong, and hyper is battle-tested against them. Unlike `core::json`/codec — hand-rolled because core is dep-minimal and wasm-embeddable — the *server* crate already carries tokio, so axum adds no new runtime and never touches core.
- **The pure `register_schema` decision + its `RegisterOutcome`→status mapping (200/401/403/409) are untouched.** Only the transport changed: 400 (non-`u32` version), 404 (unknown route), 405 (non-POST) are now axum's routing, 413 is `DefaultBodyLimit::max(1 MiB)`, 408 is `tower_http` `TimeoutLayer` (the slowloris guard, formerly the 30 s per-request timeout). The credential is still the `Authorization` header verbatim; the registry sits behind a `Mutex` held only across the pure `register`, no `await` under the guard.
- **Registry state is per-router.** The status matrix is driven in-process via `tower::ServiceExt::oneshot` (Miri-friendly, no socket); cross-request state (idempotent re-POST → 200, changed body → 409, gap → 409) and malformed-framing → 400 are proven by socket tests against `serve_admin`.

**Why:** hand-rolling a parser at an untrusted HTTP boundary trades a mature, fuzzed implementation for bespoke code whose failure modes are security bugs — the opposite of the dep-minimalism rationale that justifies the core-crate hand-rolls. The server crate's existing tokio dependency means the swap costs nothing the runtime didn't already carry.
## 2026-07-04 · Unit 5c-ii-b-2/#161 · one schema registry shared across the data + admin planes via ServeConfig
**Changed:** no ARCHITECTURE change — the cross-plane wiring that completes 5c-ii.
- **A single `Arc<Mutex<SchemaRegistry>>` is threaded through `ServeConfig.schema`**, from `main.rs` into `registry_actor` (which calls `Registry::set_schema_registry`, the data plane) and into `serve_admin` (the admin plane, which writes it). One registry, both planes: a registration over the admin plane is at once visible to the data-plane handshake resolution.
- **`ServeConfig` drops `Copy`, keeps `Clone`.** It now holds an `Arc`, which is not `Copy`. It is only ever moved once (built via `..ServeConfig::default()` and handed to one serve call), so removing `Copy` is transparent at every call site.
- **`serve_admin` locks the registry per request, only around the synchronous `dispatch`** — never held across an `.await`. Registration is rare and the critical section is a pure map write, so a short lock per request is cheaper than any sharding.

**Why:** carrying the shared registry in the already-threaded `ServeConfig` avoids widening the serve-chain signatures with a new parameter, and the per-request lock keeps the admin plane's writes and the data plane's reads on one authority without either blocking the other. Completes 5c-ii — the handshake now resolves against what the admin plane actually registered. Unblocks 5c-iii (client declares real values).

## 2026-07-04 · Unit 5c-ii-b-1/#160 · the schema registry is injected into the connection Registry, not threaded through its constructor
**Changed:** no ARCHITECTURE change — an implementation decision for wiring resolution into the handshake.
- **`Registry` holds an `Arc<Mutex<SchemaRegistry>>` that defaults to empty and is overridden by a `set_schema_registry` setter**, in the mould of `set_verifier`/`set_authorizer` — rather than adding the registry to `Registry::new`. `Registry::new(server)` has ~29 call sites (mostly tests); an empty default means every existing connection resolves to `Relay` (no app registered) so behaviour and those call sites are untouched, and only the data plane that actually shares a registry opts in.
- **`step` takes `&SchemaRegistry` and resolves at `Hello`.** The resolution is part of processing the Hello message (where the client is validated and recorded), so it belongs in `step`, not split into the transport. `deliver` locks the shared registry and passes it in. A `Reject` returns an `UnsupportedVersion` error with `close`, so the connection is refused before it can subscribe; `Relay`/`Enforcing` proceed, and the `Session` records `app_id` + the resolved `schema_version` (`None` = relay) for later enforcement units to read.
- **Sliced b-1 (logic) from b-2 (cross-plane sharing).** b-1 is unit-testable end to end through `Registry::deliver` with an injected registry — no sockets, no serve chain. b-2 threads one shared `Arc<Mutex<SchemaRegistry>>` through the serve chain and the admin plane so a real registration becomes visible to the handshake.

**Why:** the setter-with-empty-default keeps a security-relevant change from rippling into dozens of unrelated test call sites, and makes the relay default explicit (no registry ⇒ relay). Putting resolution in `step` keeps the Hello logic in one place. Isolating b-1 lets the gate be proven against an in-memory registry before the cross-plane plumbing (b-2) shares the real one. Unblocks 5c-ii-b-2.

## 2026-07-04 · Unit 5c-ii-a/#159 · the handshake tier decision is a pure method on the registry
**Changed:** no ARCHITECTURE change — an implementation + slicing decision.
- **The accept/reject/tier policy lives on `SchemaRegistry` as a pure `resolve_handshake`**, separate from the data-plane wiring that will call it (5c-ii-b). The decision is a pure function of registry state, so it is isolated as a spec'd, Miri-clean method — a bug here would mis-tier a connection or let an unknown version through, so it is worth verifying before any plumbing.
- **The tier vocabulary is `Relay` / `Enforcing { version }` / `Reject`.** Relay covers both "no app" (empty `app_id`) and "app never registered" — ARCHITECTURE serves both with zero schema enforcement, so they collapse to one tier.
